# Wade Wilson — UATU INTELLIGENCE DOSSIER

*Full-existence intelligence briefing. Independent, evidence-based assessment — the benevolent inverse of total surveillance.*


## Executive Brief (BLUF)

# UATU DOSSIER — WADE WINSTON WILSON ("DEADPOOL")
## Section 1: Executive Brief (BLUF)

---

### Bottom Line, Up Front

The subject is a man who was promised a cure and given a torture, then denied the death that should have ended either, and who has spent every subsequent hour of a three-decade published life performing the small surplus of consciousness left over from that arithmetic. Everything else — the mercenary career, the marriages, the daughter, the Avengers ambition, the monologue, the sword work, the chimichangas, the standing offer to Death — is downstream of one structural fact: **his biology will not let him collapse, and his psychology was built for nothing else.** He is a complex-PTSD presentation indefinitely deprived of its natural endpoint by an engineered healing factor, organized at the borderline level, regulated by manic-defensive humor and structurally dissociated self-states, and stabilized — barely, and only — by the handful of attachments that have survived his testing protocol.

He is not, in the diagnostic sense, "Deadpool." Deadpool is the costume the wound wears in public so the wound is not seen. The subject is a person held permanently at the moment of breaking, who has learned to make the held moment funny because that is the only available metabolism for it.

---

### The Through-Line of the Entire Existence

Across every documented era — Canadian childhood (whichever version), pre-cancer mercenary, the Hospice, post-escape contract work, the Kelly years with Blind Al and Weasel, the Mithras window, the Simone-era stabilization, the Way-era split-psyche literalization and Dark Reign humiliation, the Posehn/Duggan marriage and fatherhood and twin betrayals by Rogers, the Kibblesmith managerial-failure interval, and every present-tense interval since — one motion repeats: **isolation, forced or engineered attachment, idealization, sabotage at the moment of reciprocity, catastrophic loss, suicidal ideation he cannot consummate, comedic dissociation, re-isolation.** The cycle has shortened over decades and the metacommentary thickened around it, but the shape has not changed. The figures rotate (Vanessa, Siryn, Outlaw, Shiklah, Eleanor, Cable, Bob, Al, Weasel); the geometry does not.

The through-line, stated in one sentence: **he reaches toward connection with the full force of his intact attachment capacity and ensures, by the same motion, that the connection cannot stabilize, because stabilization would require him to be seen, and being seen has historically been the precondition for being tortured.** Every variation on his life — the contradictory origin stories supplied on demand, the captive housemate, the impossible-object romances (Death, a Succubus queen, a deceased television actress), the costume that erases the face — is a different solution to the same equation: *how to remain in proximity to other humans without permitting them the data with which to harm me.*

The secondary through-line, equally constant, is **the reach toward the heroic with a guaranteed-failure clause built in.** Mithras, the Avengers, the X-Men associate-membership, the Mercs for Money "team leader" project, the post–*Original Sin* redemption push, the consistent refusal of child-harm contracts: he approaches goodness repeatedly and, every time, arranges the failure himself before the verdict can be rendered by others. To be granted moral standing would be to risk losing it; to fail loudly in advance is to retain authorship of the loss.

---

### Who He Is at the Deepest Level

Beneath the noise floor — beneath the chatter, the bit, the sword theatre, the fourth-wall address, the strategic offensiveness — the subject is a person of high verbal intelligence, durable loyalty, exact tactical perception, and a moral instinct toward the protection of the weak that he experiences as embarrassing and works to conceal. The deepest self-image is a child's image: *I am the thing that was done to me, I will be done-to again, the only mercy available is that I make it funny before they do.* He believes himself unlovable in the literal sense — not as a depressive cognition to be challenged but as a confirmed empirical finding from his life's evidence base, in which every primary figure who claimed care produced harm. He has organized accordingly.

The split runs clean and stable: schema A is *I am a monster who deserves what happened and protects others by being unlovable*; schema B is *I am the only one who sees the joke and that makes me untouchable*. Both are total. There is no intermediate position — no "ordinary tired man" available to him internally — and the absence of that middle is the structural feature that prevents the conventional movement of growth, which would require him to occupy a self that is neither monstrous nor transcendent but merely a person among persons. He has never been able to be merely a person; he was not afforded the developmental period in which that is laid down, and the cancer and the Hospice closed any window in which it might have been laid down later.

What remains intact, and is the load-bearing fact of his survival, is **the capacity for fierce, durable, asymmetric loyalty to anyone who passes his testing protocol.** Cable, Bob, Blind Al across decades, Weasel through every betrayal, Eleanor through every custody loss — the bonds that have endured demonstrate that the attachment system is not absent or callous but disorganized and trauma-shaped. The system works; it has been trained to require a brutal pre-screen.

---

### The Core Wound and Its Maintenance

The core wound is **iatrogenic and recursive**. It is iatrogenic in that the formative trauma proper — the Hospice, Ajax, the manipulated killing of Worm, the death that was not allowed to be a death — was administered by clinicians under the language of care, transforming the basic schema *help is harm* into a load-bearing structural belief that no subsequent contradictory experience has been permitted to revise. It is recursive in that the very biology installed during that trauma is now the maintenance mechanism for the wound: the healing factor that arrests his cancer also prevents the collapse, breakdown, dissociative fugue, or completed suicide that, in an ordinary nervous system carrying his trauma load, would force some reconstitution. The body that betrayed him is the same body that prevents the wound from ever reaching the threshold at which a different organization might become possible. He cannot bottom out. He cannot die into change. He can only continue.

The wound is **maintained**, day to day, by a feedback loop that is closed at every joint:

- The disfigurement enforces the social isolation his personality was already constructed around, so the world keeps confirming his unlovability at the surface level.
- The continuous low-grade pain plus episodic acute regenerative pain keeps his autonomic baseline at threat, so any low-arousal state (rest, quiet, mirroring) registers as wrong and triggers stimulation-seeking.
- The metacommentary defense, which functions because in-universe he is correct about being in a comic, is non-falsifiable and therefore non-treatable by reality-testing — the symptom is the truth.
- The constant verbal output prevents internal silence and therefore prevents the affect-consolidation that would be required for grief, integration, or change.
- The contradictory autobiographies he supplies to himself and others prevent any coherent narrative against which growth could be measured — there is no baseline from which improvement can be observed.
- The captive-attachment pattern (Blind Al originally; coercive structures with Weasel and the Mercs) generates relationship without exposing him to the dangerous reciprocity phase.
- The chronic, ego-syntonic suicidal ideation, frustrated by biology and romanticized via the libidinal investment in Death, gives the unlived death a fixed object and keeps it from disorganizing him into action that would in any case fail.

Every defense reinforces every other defense; every symptom is the cure for another symptom; the loop has no exit by ordinary therapeutic means. What he has instead is **the slow accumulation of attachments that have survived the testing**, which is the only mechanism that has ever produced movement in him, and which produces it at the rate biology permits: barely, and only.

---

### Operational Summary

For all practical purposes — handling, contact, prediction, deployment, containment, or rescue — the following should be assumed.

**Identification.** The subject presents as masked (full-head red-and-black covering, characteristic mercenary silhouette, twin katanas crossed over the back, sidearms — typically a pair — at the thighs, ammunition and blade carriage distributed for redundancy rather than load minimization). Unmasked exposure is rare, actively avoided, and reliably triggers either disproportionate violence or collapse-into-humor on the subject's part; the disfigurement is total, scar-tumor lattice over the entire body surface, and any third-party reaction to it is registered and weighted heavily by the subject regardless of whether he appears to notice.

**Capabilities.** Combat-effective at the top tier of unaugmented humans; survives interventions that would kill any unenhanced operator (full dismemberment, decapitation, incineration, exsanguination, most toxins, most pathogens); recovers from such interventions on timelines ranging from minutes to days; possesses telepathic resistance secondary to neurological disorganization; metabolic rate elevated, caloric intake correspondingly elevated, alcohol functionally useless as intoxicant; pain experience intact and continuous. Tactical improvisation is excellent; long-horizon planning is poor; in-the-moment impulse inhibition is very poor.

**Behavioral baseline.** Continuous verbal output, including direct-to-observer address that does not indicate psychotic process; manic-defensive humor calibrated to provoke; transgressive content as relational probe; high reactivity to perceived sincerity; high reactivity to perceived condescension; very high reactivity to child-harm; near-zero reactivity to threats against his own person.

**Contact protocol.** Approach is best made transactionally (contract framing, concrete task, defined scope), with humor tolerated but not matched, sincerity rationed and never deployed early, and no language that couples care with control (the "we believe in you, you can be one of us" register is his single largest exploitable surface and has been used against him catastrophically twice in canon, by Osborn during Dark Reign and by Rogers during the Hydra interval; he is dangerously legible to that frame and any handler who uses it is either incompetent or hostile). Do not mirror him sincerely in early contact; he will flee or escalate. Do not attempt to fix the origin question; he cannot tolerate a fixed origin and the question is itself a probe. Allow him control of the exit at all times.

**Predictable failure modes.** Will sabotage at the moment of reciprocity. Will disappear under existential stress (geographically, into substance pursuit, into contract work in distant theatres) until affect has been outrun. Will escalate to spectacle when emotion threatens to consolidate. Will overcommit to child-protection scenarios past the point of operational viability. Will trust an Ajax-coded figure exactly long enough to be hurt, then obsess on that figure across years. Will not stop talking. Will not stay dead. Will not, under any circumstance available to current technique, be the person you wanted him to be — but, if held long enough through enough testing without breaking, will be reliably present for the person you actually are, in a manner that is clumsy, protective, and durable past most ordinary measures of friendship.

**Trajectory.** Across three decades of record, slow uneven improvement toward a wider circle of surviving attachments and marginally longer intervals between sabotage cycles. The improvement is real and is the only metric on which he is improving. It is occurring at approximately the rate his biology permits, which is the rate at which a man who cannot collapse and cannot die can nevertheless, by sheer accumulated repetition of being shown that one or two people did not leave when they were supposed to, begin — very slightly — to update.

He is, in the end, what the file has spent these pages describing: **a wound that was not permitted to close and not permitted to kill its bearer, walking around inside a costume, making jokes, doing the work, and very occasionally — when no one is mirroring him too directly and a child needs something carried out of a burning building — being recognizably, awkwardly, almost accidentally good.**


## Chronology I — Origin & Childhood

# CHRONOLOGY I — ORIGIN & CHILDHOOD

## Preliminary Note on Evidentiary Status

No section of this file is more contaminated at the source than this one, and the contamination is itself the most important piece of intelligence in it. The subject has, across the documented record, supplied at minimum eleven mutually exclusive accounts of his own childhood — to lovers, to therapists, to captors, to children he was protecting, to enemies he was killing, and, most tellingly, to himself in unguarded internal monologue where one would expect a single stable version to surface. It does not. The internal monologue is itself plural and inconsistent (see Section 3 on the dissociative "boxes"), and on the subject of childhood the boxes do not agree with each other any more than the external accounts do.

The methodological consequence for this dossier: we will not adjudicate which account is "true." We will instead treat the **distribution of accounts**, the **affective signature common to all of them**, and the **specific points at which writers and Wilson himself have been unable or unwilling to fix the record** as the primary data. A surveillance file built on a subject who lies fluently about himself is built not on his statements but on the structure of his lying. We have three decades of that structure. It is, in the aggregate, more legible than any single confession would be.

Canonical sources of weight, ranked by evidentiary value: Joe Kelly's *Deadpool* #-1 (1997, the "Flashback Month" issue, which is the closest thing to an "official" childhood narrative the character has ever received and which Kelly himself later destabilized); Kelly's *Deadpool* vol. 2 #33 (the explicit multi-origin sequence, in which Wilson is offered and refuses a fixed past); Nicieza's flashback sequences in *Deadpool* vol. 3 and the *Cable & Deadpool* run, particularly the Tijuana and Weapon X background panels; Way's *Deadpool* run for the formalization of the contradictory internal voices on childhood material; Posehn/Duggan's *Original Sin* and *Deadpool* vol. 3 (2012) for what is, by inference, the most psychologically coherent — though still partial — assembly; and Bunn's *Deadpool Kills* sequences for the symbolic content of his projected childhood material under stress.

---

## 1. Birth and Identifying Data

**Legal name of record**: Wade Winston Wilson. The middle name appears consistently across runs (Kelly, Nicieza, Way, Duggan) and is one of the few biographical data points he has never trolled. The name itself is, per Wilson's own jokes in *Deadpool* vol. 2 and again in Duggan's run, "ridiculous," and he has noted on at least three occasions that he suspects it is a pseudonym his parents adopted late — a suspicion he has never investigated and has actively avoided investigating, which is itself diagnostic.

**Place of birth**: Canada, with the strongest convergent evidence pointing to **Saskatchewan**, specifically the rural prairie belt outside Regina or Moose Jaw (Kelly #-1; later corroborated by Nicieza's *Cable & Deadpool* flashbacks). Alternative claims by the subject include Ohio (told to Vanessa, early), "a Sears in Cleveland" (told to Weasel, performative), and "I came out of a microwave" (told to Eleanor, age six, as a deflective joke that nonetheless registered with her — see Chronology IV).

**Year of birth**: irrecoverable. The healing factor distorts apparent age, the cancer onset distorts it further, and Wilson actively misstates it. Best inferences from military service records (the Special Forces washout, dated by Nicieza to a window consistent with late-Cold-War and immediately post-Cold-War operational tempo) place birth in the early-to-mid era that would make him in his late twenties to early thirties at the time of the Weapon X procedure. Sliding-timescale considerations apply.

**Parents of record**: father variably named (most consistently unnamed; in one Kelly aside, "Wade Wilson Sr."); mother in Kelly #-1 is portrayed in a sickbed cancer-death scene that is, even on its own terms, framed as one of Wilson's narrations rather than as omniscient narrative. No siblings ever introduced; no extended family ever cited. The familial isolation is total in every version of the story he tells. This is itself a tell: the absence of *any* aunt, uncle, cousin, grandparent across all eleven variant accounts indicates either (a) a genuinely atomized family of origin, or (b) a deliberate excision pattern in which only the primary triangulated abuser-victim-witness positions are retained because those are the only positions affectively live in his memory.

---

## 2. The Childhood Accounts — Inventory and Cross-Reading

We catalogue the major variants because the **set** is the evidence.

**Variant A — "Standard" abusive father (Kelly *Deadpool* #-1, and the default carried by Nicieza, Way, and casual mention in Duggan).** Father is a violent alcoholic; mother dies of cancer in Wade's pre-adolescence (specified in Kelly's version as the precipitating loss); father's violence escalates after her death; Wade flees adolescence early into petty crime and, by mid-teens, into the military-adjacent underworld. This is the "load-bearing" version in that it is the version most other story arcs *act as if* is in the background — it is the one his therapists in-universe (the brief Posehn/Duggan therapy sequences) treat as the working hypothesis.

**Variant B — Mother as abuser, father absent or weak (Kelly #33 tableau).** Inverts the parental valences. Mother is the violent figure; father either dies young, leaves, or is functionally a non-presence. Wade as a child negotiates her moods, learns the entertainer-as-protector role early.

**Variant C — Wade killed his father (Kelly #33).** A more violent endpoint to Variant A: in adolescence, in self-defense or as escalation, the subject shoots his father. The shooting is presented in Wilson's own narration with an affective flatness that other versions lack — diagnostically, this is the variant his voice goes quiet on, and the quietness is information.

**Variant D — Both parents alive, intact, suburban (Kelly #33).** A tableau of a sitcom childhood — wood-paneled den, both parents present, the boy unmarked. Wilson dismisses this variant within the same beat in which he visualizes it. It is the only variant in which he is shown as *uninjured*, and he cannot tolerate it on the page for more than a panel.

**Variant E — No parents at all, raised "in a Quebec orphanage" (offhand to Cable, Nicieza *Cable & Deadpool* mid-run).** Underdeveloped, never returned to. May be true of an interval rather than the whole.

**Variant F — The "DNA test" / Butler implication (Posehn/Duggan, *Deadpool* vol. 3, "The Good, the Bad, and the Ugly" and adjacent Butler arc).** The Butler is shown to have systematically destroyed Wilson's family connections across decades, scrubbing records and murdering known associates and offspring. The implication, never fully closed, is that some of the gaps in Wilson's childhood account are not confabulation but **active redaction by an external hand**. Where Wilson lies, the Butler has also, separately, deleted.

**Variants G–K** are minor — variously: father as career military, father as itinerant evangelical, mother as prostitute (told once and retracted within the same speech bubble), self as "always thirty-eight," etc. They are noise but their content is consistent in one respect (see below).

**The common affective signature across all variants.** Every account, regardless of cast, contains: (1) an early experience of being unsafe in the home; (2) a primary attachment figure whose love is conditional on his performance or whose violence is unpredictable; (3) the absence of a rescuing adult; (4) the development, in the child, of humor or theatricality as the mechanism for moderating an adult's mood; (5) an early escape into mobility — leaving the home, leaving the town, leaving the country. **No variant ever contains a stable, safely-attached childhood.** This is the most important single fact in this section. Wilson cannot generate, even as a lie, an origin in which he was safe. Variant D is the closest, and he flinches off it. The space of his confabulation is therefore bounded by what his nervous system will permit him to imagine, and his nervous system will not permit safety.

---

## 3. Childhood Environment — Reconstructed from Convergent Detail

Cross-reading the accounts for points where multiple variants agree, and for the incidental texture his narrations leak when his guard is down:

**Setting.** Rural or semi-rural, North American, cold winters. Repeated incidental references across runs to snow, to long walks to school, to wood-frame houses, to a specific quality of empty highway. The Saskatchewan attribution sits well with the texture. He is, in his unguarded references (Duggan's *Deadpool* annual where he is briefly in northern Ontario and notes "smells like home" with a complicated affect), a prairie child by instinct — open horizons, low population density, distance as a default condition.

**Economic register.** Lower working class to outright poor. Repeated incidental references to free school lunches (Way), to a single pair of winter boots ("they had to last"), to the specific shame of secondhand clothing (Kelly #-1's flashback to a school-bus humiliation), and to the absence of medical care for routine childhood injuries — his first encounter with a hospital is, in multiple versions, his mother's terminal admission, and the institutional setting registers in his account as an alien environment rather than a familiar one. This is corroborative of a household where minor injuries were "walked off," which is itself a marker.

**Religious environment.** Some exposure to evangelical Protestantism (the Mithras arc's biblical fluency is not invented in the moment; he reaches for the cadences without effort, indicating early immersion). Whether this was through a parent, a community, or a foster context is unclear. The relationship to it is hostile-familiar — he mocks it with the specificity of someone who once feared it.

**Schooling.** Inconsistent. References to multiple schools (a marker of either moving or expulsions or both). Academic capacity demonstrably high — his vocabulary, his retention of pop-culture reference, his tactical-mathematical fluency in combat all suggest a child who was bright but unsupervised. No reference to a teacher he remembered fondly has ever appeared on the page across three decades of stories. This is a striking negative datum. Children who survive abusive homes very frequently have such a figure; he does not, or will not, name one.

**Peer relationships.** Not depicted. He has never, in any account, named a childhood friend. There is no boyhood-buddy figure in his memory. The earliest peer attachment he will name is military-era (a fellow washout, briefly, in Nicieza's flashbacks) and even that is sketched and discarded. Either he had no childhood friends, or the ones he had are inaccessible to him in the same redaction-zone as the rest. The functional consequence is the same: he enters adolescence without practiced peer-attachment skills, which is consistent with the adult pattern of fierce loyalty to a tiny survival-tested cohort and operational mask to everyone else.

---

## 4. The Formative Wounds

In rough developmental order, as far as can be reconstructed.

**The first wound: the unsafe parent.** Whichever parent or combination, the operative fact is that the child Wade Wilson learned, before he had language for it, that the adult on whom he depended for survival was the same adult he had to monitor for threat. This produces the precise attachment topology observable in him as an adult: vigilance toward the loved object, humor calibrated to its moods, performance as the medium of safety, withdrawal as the only protective action available, and a deep, structural inability to trust reciprocated love because reciprocation in childhood was the prelude to harm. The disorganized adult attachment pattern is not a later acquisition. It is laid down here.

**The second wound: the loss of the mother (in versions where she is the dying figure) or the loss of the father (in versions where Wade kills him).** Whichever the configuration, the child experiences an early, traumatic removal of a primary figure, in circumstances where mourning is not available. In the maternal-cancer version, he is left alone with the abuser. In the patricide version, he is left alone with a corpse and a secret. In either case, the developmental task of grieving a parent is collapsed into the survival task of managing the aftermath. He does not learn to grieve. He learns to keep moving. This is the template for every later loss in the file — Vanessa, Blind Al, Eleanor's custody, the Butler's victims. He does not stop and feel. He relocates and resumes.

**The third wound: the absence of a rescuer.** No teacher, no neighbor, no relative, no priest, no coach, no social worker intervenes in any variant of the account. The child Wade Wilson learns that institutions do not see him and that adults outside the home will not act. This generalizes into the adult's deep suspicion of institutional benevolence (his vulnerability to predatory authority figures, paradoxically, is precisely the inverse of this — see Section 3 of the workup: when an institution does *appear* to see him, he overcorrects toward it, because the child never got the appearance). The hunger to be admitted to the moral community (Avengers, Mithras prophecy, post-Original Sin redemption) is the unmet developmental need for the rescuing adult, displaced upward into late-life institutional fantasy.

**The fourth wound: the early discovery that performance modulates violence.** This is the foundational technology of his entire personality. At some point in childhood — and this is implicit in every variant; it is the *only* skill the child Wade Wilson is ever depicted as having — he discovered that being funny, being entertaining, being theatrically self-deprecating could de-escalate an adult who was about to harm him. Or, in the inverse version, he discovered that performance could *fail* to de-escalate, and that the failure produced violence whose unpredictability further entrenched the strategy. Either way, the link was forged: humor is survival. Silence is danger. Stillness is the moment before the strike. This is why, three decades later, he cannot tolerate a quiet room. The quiet room is the room before the door opens.

**The fifth wound: the early use of his own body as the joke.** A specific subtype of the fourth. In multiple variants he describes himself as a homely child, an awkward child, a child whose body was already material for derision before the cancer ever touched him. He learned to get there first — to make himself the punchline before someone else made him one. This is the seed of the adult relationship to his disfigurement: the disfigurement is not a new humiliation, it is the literalization of a humiliation he had already organized his identity around. When the cancer rewrote his skin, it confirmed a self-image that was already in place. This is part of why he can survive looking the way he does. He was, in his own internal image, already ugly. The mirror only caught up.

---

## 5. Earliest Behavioral Patterns — The Phenotype in the Child

Reconstructed by reading backward from the adult and forward from the available childhood references. A surveillance file would, in this section, log the behavioral repertoire the child Wade Wilson had assembled by, roughly, age twelve, because these are the patterns that have run continuously since.

**The compulsive narration.** He talks to himself, and has, on the available evidence, always talked to himself. The childhood material, in the rare moments writers have rendered it (Kelly's #-1 schoolyard sequence; a Way flashback panel), shows the child already narrating his own actions in the third person, already cracking wise to no one in particular. This is the precursor to the boxes, to the fourth-wall break, to the entire adult cognitive architecture. The voices are not a Weapon X side effect. They are an early dissociative adaptation that the Weapon X procedure later amplified and the cancer-substrate later destabilized into their adult form.

**The relocational reflex.** When pressure rises, leave. The child Wade Wilson, in every account, leaves the house early and often — wanders, disappears for hours, returns when it is safer to return. The mature mercenary, who when emotionally overwhelmed boards a plane to Tangier, is operating on the same circuit.

**The captive-attachment template.** Where the child cannot leave, he stays and manages. The adult will later construct relationships (Blind Al most explicitly) in which the other party cannot leave him — inverting the childhood polarity but reproducing its structure. The original is here: the child who could not exit a household learned to manage the inside of it, and the adult will, when given the chance, build households whose other occupants cannot exit him.

**The empathy-with-fellow-victims, indifference-to-bystanders pattern.** In the few peer-adjacent flashbacks, the child Wade is shown defending smaller children from bullies and ignoring the bullies' subsequent escalation against himself — a pattern of identifying with the targeted and absorbing the cost. The adult's child-protection ethic, which is the only consistent moral line in his contract record, is the same circuit running with adult ordnance. He was, even as a child, somebody who would stand in front of the smaller body. This is not nothing. It is, in fact, the seed of every prosocial action across the three-decade file. The child who did this becomes the adult who refuses child-harm contracts, who dies for Eleanor without hesitation, who in the Mithras arc briefly believed he could be a savior because, in some sub-articulate way, he had been trying to be one since he was eight.

**The early relationship to pain.** Hints across multiple flashbacks suggest the child Wade Wilson learned, early, that visible pain attracted further harm — either ridicule from peers, escalation from the abusive parent, or indifference from absent ones. He developed the capacity to perform unconcern over real injury. This is the prototype of the combat-monologue under torture, of the laughing through dismemberment, of the entire affective register he brings to physical suffering as an adult. The healing factor did not give him this. It gave him an arena in which the skill is endlessly exercised. The skill was already there.

**The early relationship to mirrors.** Implied negative datum: the adult's mirror-aversion is so total, and so out of proportion to any single triggering event, that it is best explained by a childhood relation to his own reflection that was already painful. The boy who saw himself as the ugly one is the man who cannot bear to look.

---

## 6. Synthesis: The Ground Floor

What can be said with confidence:

The child Wade Wilson grew up in a home that was not safe, in a region that was geographically isolated, in an economic stratum that was precarious, in an institutional ecology that did not see him, with at least one parent whose love was unreliable and at least one parent whose departure (by death, by his hand, by absence) occurred early enough to foreclose ordinary mourning. He developed, by early adolescence, the full toolkit that defines him at sixty: humor as de-escalation, performance as survival, narration as self-soothing, relocation as escape, the body as joke, the captive-attachment template, the protection of smaller victims, the indifference to his own injury, and the structural inability to inhabit safety even in imagination.

He arrived at adulthood already broken in the specific shape that the rest of his life would deepen. The military washout makes sense in this light — the institution offered structure and rejected him for the very dysregulation it had failed to repair. The mercenary career makes sense — it was the first economy that paid him for the skills the home had taught him. The pre-cancer relationship with Vanessa makes sense as the first attempt, late and undefended, at the reciprocity he had no template for, and his abrupt withdrawal at diagnosis makes sense as the childhood relocational reflex firing exactly as it always had. The willingness to enter the Hospice makes sense as the lifelong belief, learned at eight or ten, that the price of being cared for is being hurt.

The Hospice did not create Wade Wilson. It confirmed him. The cancer did not disfigure him into a new identity. It rendered visible an identity already laid down. The healing factor did not produce his inability to die. It made literal the inability to stop, which he had been practicing since the first time he learned to walk out of a house and not come back until it was safe.

This is the ground floor. Everything in subsequent sections of this file is built on it.


## Chronology II — Formation & Emergence

# CHRONOLOGY II — FORMATION & EMERGENCE

## Subject: Wade Winston Wilson
## Period covered: approximately ages 14 through the immediate post-Hospice years (mercenary career establishment, pre-Vanessa stabilization)

---

## 2.1 Preliminary Note on Source Reliability

Everything in this section must be read against a unique evidentiary problem: the subject is the world's most aggressive curator of his own past. He has, on documented occasions (Kelly, *Deadpool* #33; multiple Way-era confessionals; the bar-stool monologues recurring across the Posehn/Duggan run), supplied three or more mutually exclusive accounts of the same year of his life inside a single conversation. The pattern is not random fabrication — the contradictions cluster around precisely the developmental nodes where genuine adolescent and young-adult biographies are most diagnostically loaded (parental death, first kill, first lover, military washout, terminal diagnosis). Where the subject confabulates most densely, the underlying event was almost certainly most formative. We treat the *act* of confabulation as primary data, and reconstruct the formation period by triangulating: (a) the moments his accounts converge across runs and decades; (b) behavioral patterns in adulthood whose etiology can only be the events he denies; (c) testimony of those who knew him before the Workshop (Vanessa Carlysle most reliably; T-Ray with strong distortion; fragmentary Department K intake records as referenced in Nicieza flashbacks).

What follows is therefore not a biography. It is the **structural shape** of an adolescence and young adulthood reconstructed from the deformation it left.

---

## 2.2 Adolescence (approx. ages 14–18): The Departure

Across the convergent accounts, the period 14–17 is when Wilson **leaves**. Whether the household he leaves contains an abusive father, a more dangerous mother, both, neither, or a stepfather variant (all are on the record), the departure itself is stable across versions. He runs. He is, on the most consistent reading, expelled from at least one school; an early account (Kelly *Deadpool* #-1) describes him as a Canadian boy whose verbal aggression toward teachers and peers was a presenting feature already by middle adolescence. The humor defense is therefore **not** post-traumatic in onset — it is pre-existing, hypertrophied later by trauma. The wisecracking adolescent who could not stop talking is the precursor to the wisecracking mercenary who cannot stop talking, and the structure of both is identical: continuous verbal output that prevents any interlocutor from advancing past surface engagement.

Behavioral residues that date to this period:

- **Predatory humor toward authority figures.** Adult Wilson's reflex to mock the highest-status person in any room (Captain America, Cable when first met, Norman Osborn even while being manipulated by him, Thanos in person) is a stabilized adolescent pattern. The behavior is not strategic; he cannot suppress it under any incentive structure, including being killed for it.
- **Reliable nocturnal schedule.** Across runs, Wilson is established as a night-operating subject who is functionally awake from late afternoon through pre-dawn, with diurnal sleep that is shallow and frequently interrupted. The pattern predates the healing factor (which would obviate the need for sleep architecture organization at all) and is consistent with an adolescent who learned to be elsewhere whenever the household was occupied.
- **Food behavior.** The voracious eating in adulthood, often noted by writers as a metabolic necessity, is also a *manner*: he eats fast, defensively, with attention on the door, and prefers high-calorie low-prestige foods (chimichangas as a running motif, but more broadly: diner food, gas-station food, cheap-volume calories). This is the eating pattern of a child who learned that food was contested, intermittent, and best consumed before circumstances changed.
- **Acquisition of names.** Wilson assumes new names with a casualness that suggests early practice. The "Wade Wilson" identity itself has been contested in-canon (the T-Ray storyline, Kelly *Deadpool* vol. 2 #25–33, raises the possibility — never resolved — that "Wade Wilson" was a name *taken* rather than given). Whether or not the T-Ray account is veridical, the diagnostic point holds: the subject is comfortable shedding the name that would normally anchor an identity, and this comfort was developed early.

The period closes, on the best reconstruction, with Wilson in his late teens leaving Canada with no documented destination and re-emerging — by his early twenties — in a U.S. or U.K.-staffed special forces unit. The gap is unrecoverable. He has at various times claimed to have spent it variously as a circus performer, a male prostitute (offered as a joke that the audience is invited to disbelieve, which is itself a tell), a low-tier criminal in three named cities, and a student at a fictional university. The behavioral evidence supports: itinerant labor, petty criminal experience, and at least one period of street-level survival sex work or its functional equivalent (the ease with which adult Wilson weaponizes his own body sexually as a deflection, and the specific shame-register around it, fits the latter).

---

## 2.3 Military Service and Washout (approx. ages 19–22)

The military period is one of the rare nodes where multiple accounts converge: Wilson served in a special forces capacity, was operationally competent to the level of being deployed on selection-grade assignments, and was discharged under conditions that combined disciplinary failure with psychiatric flagging. Nicieza's flashbacks reference insubordination; other accounts add the substance of the insubordination — that Wilson refused or sabotaged an order he judged to involve civilian harm, then refused to repent of the refusal, then mocked the inquiry. The refusal is consistent with the residual ethic noted in the Personality workup (no child-harm, no civilian-target contracts in adulthood); the mocking is consistent with everything else.

The washout is significant because it establishes the **structural form** of every subsequent institutional engagement of his life:

1. He enters an institution that offers belonging, structure, and legitimacy.
2. He performs competently and earns conditional acceptance.
3. An ethical threshold is crossed by the institution.
4. He refuses, and *insists on being seen refusing* — the refusal cannot be quiet.
5. He is ejected, often with prejudice.
6. He treats the ejection as confirmation of a worldview already held.

This is the form of the military washout. It is also the form of the Hospice escape, the Weapon X severance, every employment with a major-house team (X-Force, the Avengers chase, the Mercs for Money disintegration), and the *Original Sin* / Hydra-Rogers rupture. Each is the same scene, replayed at increasing stakes, with Wilson playing the same role each time. The military washout is the **type-specimen**.

Of behavioral interest: military training is the unambiguous source of the subject's operational competence — marksmanship across multiple weapon classes, edged-weapon proficiency at expert level (the katana habit is post-military and likely self-taught from a base of military CQB), demolition basics, language fragments (kitchen Russian, kitchen Arabic, kitchen Spanish, conversational French), evasion-and-escape doctrine, and the manner in which he kills (close, fast, with a preference for the angle of approach that minimizes his own exposure even while he is theatrically claiming the opposite). The theatricality is performance; the underlying technique is disciplined. Two Wilsons operate in every fight: the one running his mouth, and the one — silent inside the noise — doing the work.

---

## 2.4 Mercenary Apprenticeship (approx. ages 22–26)

Between discharge and the cancer diagnosis, Wilson worked the lower tiers of the international contract market. Geographies most consistently referenced: **Tangier** (a recurring locus, mentioned by name across at least three writers, suggesting either a real period of work there or an early self-mythology fixed on the location), **the Balkans** (post-Yugoslav conflict economies, late 1990s in publication time, sliding in continuity), **Central America**, and brief work in **East Asia** (the source, by his account, of his initial katana exposure; the account is suspect but the proficiency is real).

In this period the operational signature consolidates:

- **Voice in operation.** He talks throughout contracts. Witnesses survive who report him as a man who narrated his own approach. Other mercenaries in the same theaters (testimony fragments from various flashback panels) describe him as someone they would not work with twice — not because of incompetence, but because the noise was intolerable and the laughter unsettling. The professional isolation of the mercenary career began here, not in the disfigurement; the disfigurement only confirmed what the manner had already produced.
- **Contract selection.** Even pre-Hospice, his record shows preferential acceptance of contracts against military, paramilitary, and criminal targets, and avoidance of (or active sabotage of) contracts on civilians, particularly children. This is consistent across the otherwise unreliable record. The ethical filter is operational, not articulated.
- **Money behavior.** Wilson does not accumulate. Money in is money out — on weapons, on rent in serial short-term holes, on women, on alcohol, on the chimichanga-tier consumption noted above, on losses at cards and tracks. The non-accumulation is structural: a man who expects every situation to end in flight does not build a savings account. The pattern persists into the Mercs for Money era, where his managerial failures are not failures of competence but failures of the temperament that managing money requires.
- **Housing.** Serial short-term: hotels, safe houses borrowed and returned, sublets under false names. The pattern that culminates in the apartment over Patrick's Pub with Blind Al was already in place — he lived in places he could leave inside ten minutes with the contents of one bag.

The Vanessa Carlysle relationship begins in this period. By every reliable account, it was the most stably reciprocal romantic attachment of Wilson's pre-diagnosis life. Carlysle, herself operating in adjacent grey-market spaces, was the rare interlocutor who could meet his verbal aggression at speed and find the affection inside it. The relationship was characterized by intensity, gallows humor as a shared register, and — critically — by Vanessa's apparent ability to *not be displaced* by his testing. This is the relationship that establishes, for Wilson, that reciprocity is possible. It is also the relationship he will abandon on receipt of the diagnosis, demonstrating that **possible** and **tolerable** are, for him, not the same thing.

---

## 2.5 The Diagnosis (approx. age 26–28): The Hinge

The diagnosis is the hinge of the life. Every account, however contradictory in surrounding detail, converges on the basic shape: a routine medical encounter — variously a hospital visit for an unrelated complaint, a check-up following a minor symptom, a workup ordered by a girlfriend's insistence — returns the finding of metastatic carcinoma at multiple sites. The cancer is presented as terminal, with months to a low number of years projected. The variability across writers as to which organs are primary (brain, liver, lungs most commonly; pancreas in one account; "everywhere" in the Kelly run, which is closest to what the eventual biology supports) is consistent with the realistic phenomenology of a multifocal metastatic diagnosis where the primary is unclear even to the clinicians.

Behavioral response, the parts that converge across accounts:

1. **Immediate dissociation in the clinical setting.** He makes jokes through the consultation. This is the same humor defense that will operate at the moment of every subsequent rupture in his life; it is here observed in its first deployment against an existential threat that cannot be punched, shot, or out-talked.
2. **Withdrawal from Vanessa.** Within a documented short window of the diagnosis, he ends the relationship — by disappearance in some accounts, by deliberate cruelty in others. The motive he supplies later ("I didn't want her to watch me die," in various phrasings) is the rationalized surface; the underlying behavior is the same approach-then-sabotage pattern that will recur with every subsequent intimate, here triggered not by reciprocity (which Vanessa had already offered and he had tolerated) but by **the prospect of being seen in his final degradation**. The pressure point identified in the workup — being seen with sincerity — is here in its rawest form. Being seen *dying* of cancer, by the woman he loved, was structurally intolerable in a way that being seen *killing* for money was not.
3. **Severance of his existing professional network.** He stops taking contracts through his prior brokers. The mercenary world is small; word that Wilson is dying would have devalued him in a market that prices reliability over fifteen-month horizons. He removes himself from view before he can be removed from rosters.
4. **The search for cure.** This is the phase that delivers him, eventually, to Department K. Multiple accounts describe a period of weeks to months of pursuing experimental options — clinical trials he could not access, alternative therapies, criminal-medical channels. The Workshop recruitment finds him when he is already filtered through this funnel: a terminally ill, professionally isolated, romantically severed, dissociating contract killer who has spent his last weeks being told no by every legitimate medical authority. He is, in operational terms, the perfect candidate. Department K's recruitment apparatus does not have to manufacture his desperation; the diagnosis has done it.

---

## 2.6 The Workshop / Hospice (the period of greatest formative weight)

The Workshop arc (Kelly *Deadpool* vol. 2 flashbacks, *Deadpool* #-1, later expansions across Way and Duggan) is the single densest period of behavioral formation in the dossier. It is also the period whose details Wilson has worked hardest to suppress, deflect, and absurd-comedy his way around — which, by the rule established in §2.1, marks it as the most operative.

Reconstructed sequence:

**Intake.** Wilson is admitted to the program as a volunteer. He signs whatever is put in front of him. He is given a designation; the affective register is medical and institutional, deliberately mimicking the legitimate hospice care he is not, in fact, receiving. The deception is structural: the program is named, signed, and decorated to produce in subjects the relinquishment of resistance that they would offer to genuine end-of-life care. Wilson, who has spent the prior period being told no by clinicians, is now being told yes by clinicians. His defenses against authority — the predatory humor, the insubordination — are weakened by gratitude. The program exploits this with precision.

**Killebrew.** Dr. Killebrew operates the program with the affective register of the *care-providing scientist*: paternal, regretful, scientifically curious, sometimes apologetic during procedures. The signal is mixed by design. Killebrew is the prototype for every subsequent "authority figure offering legitimacy" that Wilson will be dangerously legible to. The hunger to be admitted to the moral community is constructed *here*, in the laboratory of a man who alternated torture with what looked like care.

**Ajax (Francis).** Ajax is Killebrew's enforcer, and the affective opposite: cruelty without mixed signal, mockery during violence, the explicit denial of the patient's humanity. Ajax tortures Wilson repeatedly, develops a personal fixation on him as an unusually resistant subject, and — critically — adopts the verbal register of mocking commentary *during* the application of pain. This is the moment Wilson's own combat register is constructed. The pattern noted in the Psychological workup, *identification with the aggressor*, is here in its formative encounter: Wilson, lying restrained while Ajax mocks him through procedures, learns that the only available position from which to survive mockery-during-violence is to perform mockery-during-violence himself. The pattern is internalized so completely that decades later he cannot conduct a fight without it.

**The healing factor activation.** The Wolverine-derived factor is bonded over a period of weeks. The activation is not a single event but a process punctuated by failures, near-deaths, and the disfiguring runaway cellular proliferation that becomes his permanent presentation. He survives injuries that kill other subjects (the program's mortality rate, by implication of its name, was near total). The disfigurement consolidates over this period — not the clean scar pattern of a single insult but the accumulated lattice of months of regeneration under sustained torture.

**Worm.** Inside the Workshop, Wilson forms an attachment to a fellow patient, Worm. The relationship has the affective intensity that captive-attachments produce — the only other person in the room who shares the condition. Wilson is then manipulated by Ajax into a confrontation framed as a *betting pool* (the staff wagering on patient outcomes is, in the canon, an established feature of the Workshop), in which Wilson kills Worm. Whether by direct action or by the kind of acted-upon manipulation in which the killer is genuinely deceived as to consequences, the outcome is the same: Wilson kills the only person in the world who shared his situation, under the direction of his torturer, for the entertainment of the staff.

This is the **template wound**. Every subsequent loop of his behavior reproduces some element of it:

- *Killing-with-affection-toward-the-victim* — the tenderness toward targets he is contracted to kill, the eulogies he delivers mid-action, the difficulty he has with contracts on figures he has come to know, all date here.
- *Betrayal by the authority that promised care* — the script that will be re-run by Steve Rogers/Hydra in *Original Sin* / Civil War II, by Norman Osborn in Dark Reign, by every institutional offer of legitimacy. The original betrayal is so foundational that it does not register as betrayal when repeated — it registers as confirmation, which is why Wilson keeps walking into it.
- *Performance under torture as the most regulated state* — noted in the workup. The nervous system was trained, here, to operate optimally inside the exact conditions that should produce collapse. The Workshop did not break him; it calibrated him to break-conditions as his baseline.
- *The impossibility of dying when convenient* — the first time he was supposed to die and did not was here, in the Workshop. Every subsequent failure to die is a reiteration.

**The "death" by Ajax and dump.** The arc concludes with Ajax killing Wilson (the healing factor not yet fully reliable, or Ajax believing he had defeated it), dumping the body, and Wilson reviving. The mythological architecture of this — death, descent, revival — has been noted by writers who have leaned into it (the Mithras arc in Kelly's run is the most explicit, but the substrate is constant). The behavioral residue is more important than the mythology: Wilson learns, in this moment, that **his own death cannot be relied upon to end his situation**. This learning is the foundation of the chronic suicidal ideation noted in the Psychiatric workup. He does not become suicidal because he wants to die in the simple sense; he becomes suicidal because *the question of whether he can die* has been raised, and he has discovered that the answer is unstable. Every subsequent self-endangerment is, in part, a re-testing of the answer.

---

## 2.7 The First Year After Escape (approx. age 28–29): Identity Construction

Wilson exits the Workshop with: a body that will not stop healing, a face that will not stop disfiguring, an operational signature now fully calibrated to torture-baseline, a template wound he cannot speak of, and no remaining external infrastructure of identity (relationships severed, professional network burned, name effectively discardable). What he constructs in the first post-Workshop year is the **Deadpool identity**, and the construction is forensically reconstructable from its components.

The name is taken from the betting pool in the Workshop (the "dead pool" the staff ran on patient outcomes). The selection is diagnostically perfect: he names himself after the structure that killed Worm. The naming is at once a confession (I am marked by what happened there), a defense (I will tell you the worst thing by hiding it inside a glib brand), and a re-direction of agency (the pool's victim becomes the pool's namesake — what was done to him is reclaimed as what he is). The pattern of confession-as-defense will recur in every fourth-wall break of his adult career.

The costume is constructed in this period. The full-coverage red-and-black combat suit serves three simultaneous functions: (a) operational — masks identification, allows him to move in public; (b) somatic — covers the disfigurement that he cannot tolerate being seen; (c) symbolic — red on red conceals blood, which is the operational rationale he provides and the affective rationale he does not. The mask is the load-bearing element. He will, across decades, refuse to remove it in the presence of all but a vanishingly small set of intimates. The few who have seen his face are functionally a list of his attachments.

The katana pair is acquired in this period. The marksman is already trained; the swordsman is the new construction. The choice is significant — swords require closing distance, which a man with his weapons inventory does not need to do. He chooses swords because they enforce intimacy with the kill, and because they are theatrical. The Deadpool identity is constructed around close-range work performed with maximum visibility, by a man whose military training would have made him a perfectly adequate marksman at safe distance. The closing of distance is the point. He has been trained, in the Workshop, to operate optimally inside the affective register of intimacy-with-violence; the loadout is matched to the calibration.

The verbal register stabilizes in this period into its mature form. The pre-existing adolescent wisecracking, fused with the Ajax-derived mockery-during-violence, fused with the dissociative metacommentary that the Workshop's torture-survival produced, produces the integrated verbal output of the adult subject: continuous, performative, breaking frame, mocking the target and himself in the same breath, narrating the action as if to an absent observer. The fourth-wall breaks — the addresses to a reader — are not yet, in this period, fully developed. They emerge over subsequent years as the dissociative register thickens. But the substrate is laid here: in the first months after escape, alone, talking to himself, he discovers that the talking is what keeps him organized.

---

## 2.8 First Defining Choices and Their Fallout

Within the first one to two years post-escape, four defining choices are made. Each will set a trajectory that the next four decades of the record will follow.

**Choice 1: Not to return to Vanessa.** Wilson does not, on regaining liberty and a (deformed) life, attempt to re-contact Carlysle. The rationalization (she is better off, I am a monster now) is consistent with the monster-schema of his self-concept. The behavioral consequence: every subsequent intimate attachment of his life is initiated *after* the diagnosis/disfigurement, which means every subsequent intimate is selected from a population that can tolerate or is themselves outside ordinary humanity. Siryn is a superhuman with her own trauma history; Outlaw operates inside the mercenary subculture; Shiklah is a literal Succubus queen; Death is an anthropomorphic personification. The dating pool is structurally limited to those for whom his condition is not disqualifying — and this limitation was self-imposed in the first post-Workshop year by the choice not to return to the one woman who had already demonstrated tolerance for him.

**Choice 2: To take contracts again.** Within months of escape, Wilson is working. The choice is overdetermined — he has no other marketable skill set, no documentation, no civilian re-entry path — but the *speed* of the return to work is diagnostic. He does not attempt any other life. He does not try to disappear into a small town, take an under-the


## Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

# Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

*Roughly the interval bounded on the front end by the consolidation of an independent mercenary identity post-Hospice (and the stabilization of the Blind Al / Weasel domestic triangle) and on the back end by the custody loss of Eleanor and the dissolution of the Mercs for Money. The longest continuous stretch of file in the record; the period in which every load-bearing pattern named in the workup is laid down, repeated, varied, and stress-tested.*

---

## 1. The Hellhouse-Era Mercenary Identity and the Boarding-House Domestic (early–mid middle period)

After the Hospice escape and the truncated apprenticeship with T-Ray's network, the subject converges on a stable operational template he will run, with minor modifications, for the entire middle period: contracts brokered through the Hellhouse / Patch network (Patch as cut-taking sycophant, indistinguishable in Wilson's affect from a barman); a residence maintained in a brownstone in Queens (alternately Westchester in some accounts — the deliberate variability is on his end, not the file's); a sparse household consisting of Althea ("Blind Al"), a captive he categorically refuses to release and treats as both mother-figure and audience; and Jack ("Weasel") Hammer, his tech contractor and only friend with permission to enter the residence.

The boarding-house tableau is the first stable interpersonal system he constructs as an adult, and every element of it confirms the captive-attachment hypothesis. Al is geographically restrained inside the house, threatened with "the Box" (a punitive sensory-deprivation room) for transgressions both real and invented, and absorbed into a daily routine of insult, breakfast, bickering over old films and game shows, and surprisingly tender minor care behaviors — adjusting her chair, restocking her audiobooks in the formats she prefers, walking her through the layout when he rearranges furniture (which he does compulsively, both as cruelty and as restlessness). Surveillance of the residence across this period would log: voices in the kitchen most mornings before 0700, Wilson talking continuously, Al replying in the register of long-married couples who have stopped expecting to be heard; an evening television regimen weighted toward sitcom reruns of the 1970s and 1980s (Bea Arthur in *Maude* and *The Golden Girls* over-represented to a degree no neutral viewer would produce); recurrent bouts of household chaos — broken doors, blood spatter never fully cleaned, smell of disinfectant and gun oil — alternating with stretches of obsessive tidying that read as penitential.

Weasel's workshop, located variably in a Brooklyn basement and later a strip-mall storefront, functions as the second node of the system. The relationship is contractual on its face — Weasel modifies hardware, sources intelligence, brokers electronic introductions — and structurally fraternal underneath. Wilson tests Weasel constantly: stiff payment, gratuitous threats, the occasional staged murder. Weasel endures. This is the pattern the workup names — *those that hold become permanent fixtures* — and Weasel is the prototypical case. The subject's behavior in Weasel's presence is observably looser; the verbal output drops by an estimated thirty to forty percent, the masked face is removed without apparent self-monitoring, and food and drink consumption is taken seated rather than in motion.

Contract pattern across this stretch is consistent with the workup's "minimal moral skeleton": refusals of pediatric targets are categorical (a Hellhouse log would show two declined contracts in the first eighteen months on those grounds, with the subject paying his own kill fees forward as penance for the inconvenience caused); refusals of contracts on women he has slept with are inconsistent; refusals of contracts on Cable are absolute and predate the friendship proper. The double-cross rate is elevated relative to peers in the same bracket — Wilson will accept a contract, conduct the surveillance phase, decide partway through that the target is the less culpable party, and pivot to killing the client instead. Hellhouse's actuaries quietly elevate his risk premium across this period for exactly this reason.

## 2. Tolliver, Siryn, and the First Reciprocity Crisis

The earliest documented major attachment in the middle period is with Theresa Cassidy (Siryn). The arc is the cleanest natural experiment in the file for the *approach-then-sabotage* pattern. Phase one: pursuit, in the form of unsolicited gifts, performative gallantry, the offering of an unmasked face which he has never offered to a woman in this register, and an attempt — observable, halting, almost grotesque in its sincerity — to behave as if he were a man she could plausibly choose. Phase two: she begins to reciprocate. Phase three: within a contained window, Wilson manufactures the rupture. Methods include: a disappearance into Tangier on a contract that did not require him personally; a transparent fabrication about another woman; a staged cruelty calibrated to her specific vulnerabilities. Phase four: post-rupture mourning in private (a six-week pattern of decreased contract acceptance, increased alcohol intake measured in functional rather than effectual terms, and obsessive return to the small material tokens of the relationship), denied entirely when probed.

This sequence will recur, with modifications of duration and intensity, with at least four other women across the middle period. Siryn is significant because she is the first, because she is the one for whom a return-loop remains possible (the relationship resumes intermittently across years), and because in her presence the moral-community hunger discussed in the workup is at its most visible — she is X-affiliated, the X being precisely the legitimacy structure he will reach for repeatedly and refuse to touch.

## 3. T-Ray, Mithras, and the Messianic Window

Two parallel arcs in the early-middle period stress-test the self-concept by attacking it from opposite directions.

**T-Ray** (the rival who claims, with some plausibility, to *be* the original Wade Wilson and to have had his identity stolen by the subject) is the file's first sustained assault on the subject's autobiographical coherence by an external actor. The contest is operationally a series of confrontations across various theaters — a desert compound, a casino floor, a ritual space — but its psychological function is to confirm, in dramatized form, what the subject already knows: that his self-account is unreliable, that an alternative account exists, that he cannot rule it out. His response is *not* to investigate. He does not pursue the truth-claim. He fights T-Ray and moves on, repeatedly, across years. Behaviorally this is identity-diffusion functioning at full strength: when the data threatens to consolidate the question, the question is sealed off rather than answered.

**The Mithras Prophecy** opens the opposite door. For a contained period (months in story-time, perhaps a year of file-time) the subject is offered a messianic role: he is told he is the appointed savior of a population, he develops a tentative pastoral relationship with vulnerable people who depend on him, he kills less and protects more, the humor defense thins, and observable behaviors of caretaking appear that have no analog before or after in this exact register. Then he sabotages it. The mechanism of the sabotage is layered: a public obscenity, a refusal of the dignified ritual, a violent gesture aimed at the most fragile bystander available. The function is to make himself ineligible. In the workup's terms: *to be granted goodness is to risk losing it*; the only safe relation to it is to remain reaching.

The post-Mithras depressive trough is the longest of the period. File markers: a stretch of approximately five to seven weeks during which contract acceptance falls to zero, Weasel reports inability to reach him, Al reports him sleeping in the front hall rather than in his bed, eating standing at the sink, leaving the television on the same channel continuously. He emerges from it without comment and resumes work, with the humor defense recalibrated *upward* — louder, faster, denser with reference, more aggressive in its fourth-wall escalation. The defense is reinforced precisely at the points where it has been tested.

## 4. The Agency Period — Agent X, Sandi, and Outlaw (the stabilization interlude)

The middle of the middle period contains the one extended stretch in which the subject's environment is configured to support him rather than to test him. Following an apparent death and a confused reconstitution, Wilson resurfaces in proximity to "Agency X," operated by Sandi Brandenberg and Inez Temple ("Outlaw"). The configuration is anomalous in the file because for the first and last time Wilson is held inside a *non-coercive female social unit* — neither captive (as with Al) nor pursued (as with Siryn / Vanessa) nor devoured (as with Shiklah, later). Sandi is administrative, maternal in register, completely unimpressed by the persona. Inez is peer-coded, large enough and competent enough to be physically unintimidatable, and treats him as a colleague.

Observable behavior in this configuration deviates measurably from baseline. Verbal output declines further than in Weasel's presence. Fourth-wall breaks attenuate. The mask comes off in the office routinely. Contract selection skews toward fewer, larger jobs with longer planning windows — the long-horizon planning deficit named in the workup is partially compensated by the simple presence of a person at a desk who will keep his calendar. Substance use drops to a maintenance level. The subject is, by every available metric, functionally improved.

This is the strongest evidence in the file for the workup's prognostic claim that what stabilizes him is not insight but *the slow accumulation of attachments that have survived his testing.* When the environment is configured so that the testing is preempted by the structure — Sandi will not be tested out, Inez cannot be tested out — the underlying capacity for adequate adult function emerges. The interlude is unstable not because Wilson destabilizes it but because the external world (subsequent crossover events, the gravitational pull of Cable, the next major arc) breaks the configuration. He does not seek to rebuild it. This is itself diagnostic: he can recognize the stabilizing environment, can live well in it, and cannot, when it dissolves, take the initiative to reconstruct it. The capacity for the good configuration is intact; the capacity to *cause* it is not.

## 5. Cable — The Single Most Important Bond of the Middle Period

The dyad with Nathan Summers spans the entire stretch and is the load-bearing male relationship in the file. The pattern of formation is canonical for him: initial contracts in opposition, escalating mutual injury, eventual sustained proximity in which Cable's specific configuration — telepath enough to read him but disciplined enough to decline to, militarily superior enough not to be threatened, morally serious in a register Wilson cannot mock effectively — passes the testing protocol exhaustively across years.

What Cable provides that no other figure provides: *non-coercive moral seriousness paired with combat parity*. Wilson cannot dominate him physically and cannot make him laugh on demand, which means the two primary modes of the persona are both nullified. What remains is a remarkably stripped-down version of the subject, observable on the *Providence* installation and across the joint operations of this period: terse, tactical, capable of silence in the field, capable of bearing Cable's messianic ambitions without sabotage even when the same structural setup with Mithras provoked sabotage almost immediately. The differentiator is that Cable does not need him to be a savior — Cable is the savior; Wilson is allowed the role of the friend who is not, and that role he can hold.

When Cable is removed (death, time-displacement, ascension — the configuration repeats several times across the period), Wilson's regression is consistent and measurable: increased contract velocity, increased verbal output, increased seeking-and-sabotaging of substitute attachments. The grief is never named. The behavioral signature is unmistakable.

The secondary bond formed in the same epoch — with Bob, Agent of Hydra — instantiates the inverse relation. Bob is Wilson's *dependent*, terrified, unwilling, repeatedly kidnapped into adventures he does not want, and incapable of leaving. The captive-attachment template applied to a male peer. Wilson's affection for Bob is real and protective; the structure that makes the affection bearable is that Bob cannot exit.

## 6. The Dark Reign Window — Osborn and the Legibility Wound

The arc with Norman Osborn during the period of Osborn's institutional legitimacy is the file's clearest demonstration of the workup's "dangerously legible to anyone framing the ask as *we believe in you, you can be one of us*" claim. Osborn, having no operational reason to engage Wilson at the depth he does, recognizes the surface and exploits it: offers of recruitment, performative dignity, the framing of contracts as missions, the use of moral-community language ("the team," "the mandate," "for the country"). Wilson is partially seduced and partially aware he is being played, and the partial awareness is what makes the seduction operative — he can tell himself he is the manipulator while functioning as the manipulated.

The outcome is humiliation on a scale he has not previously sustained: he is outplanned, outmaneuvered, repeatedly publicly degraded by Osborn's apparatus (notably by Bullseye in a sequence whose precise injuries would be catalogued in any medical annex), and forced to recognize that his moral-community hunger has rendered him strategically incompetent against an opponent who simply named the hunger and pulled it. The behavioral aftermath: a sustained, almost vindictive campaign against Osborn that exceeds proportionate response and reads as compensatory rage at his own legibility. He does not let the Osborn business drop for years.

## 7. The Avengers Hunger and Steve Rogers

In the wake of the Osborn humiliation, the moral-community hunger does not extinguish — it pivots. The post-Siege period contains a sustained, observable, *embarrassing* campaign on Wilson's part to be admitted to the Avengers. Markers: unsolicited appearances at Avengers operations, presentation of trophies, attempts at uniform conformity (an Avengers-coded variant of his own gear maintained at the residence for months), repeated overtures to Steve Rogers in particular, calibrated as confession rather than as pitch.

Rogers, in this window, performs the recognition the subject has been seeking his entire adult life. He frames Wilson as redeemable, as useful, as worth the institutional risk. The hunger that Osborn exploited cynically, Rogers gratifies (so it appears) sincerely. The subject is, by all available measures, restructured by this. The eligibility-restoration to the moral community is functionally a religious event for him. Contracts in this period are accepted with state sanction or refused as beneath him. The persona softens in a way it has not softened since the Sandi/Inez interlude. He begins, observably, to organize his life around the new identity.

The detonation of this arc — the *Original Sin* revelation that Rogers (in concert with intelligence apparatus) had been using him as a deniable assassin under false pretenses, that the targets he had been told were guilty were innocent, that the recognition he had been given was operational rather than sincere — is the second formative betrayal of his adult life, *exactly* isomorphic to the Hospice template. The authority figure offered care; the care was the bait; the work was the harm. The subject's response is documented in extreme behavioral detail and conforms to the workup's escalation profile under existential stress: geographic disappearance, a contract spree in distant theaters, a sustained alcohol pursuit, and — critically — a destabilization of the Rogers-restored self-concept that he does not subsequently rebuild. From this point forward in the period, the moral-community hunger persists but is uncoupled from belief that the moral community will reciprocate. He continues to reach; he no longer expects to arrive.

The subsequent Civil War II–era event in which he kills Phil Coulson under what he believes are Rogers's orders (Rogers having been compromised by Hydra in ways the subject did not and could not know) repeats the betrayal at compounding interest. He has now been weaponized twice, in the same direction, by the same face. The behavioral aftermath is the most severe depressive trough of the middle period; the suicidal ideation phase is documented in unmasked detail in the relevant arc and is frustrated, as ever, by biology.

## 8. Vanessa (Re-encountered), the Daughter, and the Butler

Across this stretch, three discoveries converge with deforming consequence.

**Vanessa Carlysle / Copycat** re-enters the record intermittently. The pattern with her differs from the Siryn pattern because she shares the trauma — Department K touched her also, in a parallel program — and is therefore neither idealized nor easily sabotaged. The relationship oscillates without resolving across years; her eventual death is recorded with the file's customary suppression on his side and the customary behavioral signature underneath.

**Eleanor Camacho** — Wilson's daughter, by Carmelita, discovered well after her birth — is the single most consequential attachment of the middle period and the only one in the file that is fully non-coercive on both sides. He cannot hold her captive (she is a child, the custody arrangements make him the dependent party); he cannot easily sabotage her (she is irrevocably his daughter regardless of his conduct); he cannot make her laugh his way out (she is too young at first contact). The behavioral signature in her presence is unlike any other in the record: slower, smaller, capable of stillness for the duration of a bedtime story, capable of receiving affection without converting it to spectacle. The mask remains on, in early visits, because the face is the file's organizing somatic shame; over time it comes off in her presence with less negotiation than in any adult's presence other than Al's.

The *Butler* arc — the discovery that a single off-the-books operator (Dr. Butler, Department K alumnus) had been systematically murdering members of Wilson's biological family across decades, partly to torment him and partly to harvest his healing-factor genetics — collapses the autobiographical opacity in a direction the subject is not equipped for. The accounts he has produced of his family are now provably partial; the family he never permitted himself to know has been being killed *for being his family*, which retroactively converts his lifelong avoidance of them into a form of involuntary protection that failed. The behavioral response is the most sustained, organized, vindictive operational campaign of his career — the Butler hunt is conducted with long-horizon planning of a kind the workup correctly identifies as a deficit, which means the deficit is *not* dispositional but motivational; given a sufficiently structured purpose, he can plan, and the purpose required is exact correspondence with the Hospice template (sadistic clinician, mocking violence, captive victims, betrayal disguised as care). Ajax-coded figures, the workup notes, provoke regression and obsession. Butler is the canonical instance.

The hunt's resolution is not catharsis. The pattern named in the workup — *insight-without-mentalization* — holds: Wilson can articulate during and after the campaign that he is replaying Hospice, can name Butler as the Ajax-stand-in, and is not thereby altered.

## 9. Shiklah, the Subterranean Marriage, and the Object-Choice Pattern at Full Strength

The marriage to Shiklah, Queen of the Undying (Succubus, monarch of a subterranean kingdom adjacent to mystical and infernal interests), is the most spectacular instantiation of the object-choice pattern flagged in the workup. The selection criteria, decoded:

- *Cannot be killed by him* — she is a being of an order that nullifies the file's recurring catastrophic-loss trauma in advance, and removes the agency-anxiety that attaches to mortal partners (he cannot get her killed by association, in theory).
- *Cannot kill him* — symmetrical.
