The clinical novelty is the **decoupling of pain from consequence**: ordinarily, pain teaches the body to protect the site of injury. In his case, every injury heals to baseline regardless of behavior, so the learning loop is broken. The consequence is objectively reckless self-endangerment that is not, technically, suicidality, because no consummation is possible — it is the absence of the protective conditioning the rest of us have. This contributes to the apparent ASPD-like recklessness while having a different generative mechanism.

---

## 3. RIGOROUS DIFFERENTIAL — WHAT HE IS NOT, AND WHY

### 3.1 Schizophrenia Spectrum Disorders — *Excluded.*

The auditory phenomena (the boxes) and the meta-awareness superficially invite a psychotic-spectrum read. The differential fails on multiple grounds:

- *Phenomenology of the voices.* Schizophrenic auditory hallucinations are typically experienced as alien, intrusive, often persecutory or commanding, and disorganizing. Wilson's voices are **structured, self-consistent, characterologically stable across decades, and recognizably his own internal-object content rendered audible**. He is co-conscious with them, can engage them in dialogue, and reports them with insight. This is incompatible with primary psychotic hallucinosis and is consistent with structurally dissociated self-states.
- *Reality testing.* Grossly preserved, even in the meta-awareness register. He distinguishes accurately between his interlocutors, the environment, and his own internal voices; his combat tactical judgment, target identification, and social navigation function at high competence. A subject with active schizophrenia would not sustain his operational ceiling in field conditions.
- *Negative symptoms.* Absent. No avolition (he is preternaturally driven); no alogia (the opposite); no affective flattening (the opposite); no anhedonia of the schizophrenic type (his anhedonia is depressive, not schizophrenic).
- *Course.* Schizophrenia has a progressive deteriorative course in the untreated; Wilson's symptom profile has not deteriorated cognitively over decades. The cognitive disorganization is event-coupled (stress, trauma reminders) rather than progressive.
- *Premorbid.* No documented prodromal schizotypal features. Pre-Weapon X, he was operationally functional at special-forces and contract levels.

### 3.2 Dissociative Identity Disorder (DSM-5 300.14) — *Partial fit; insufficient for diagnosis.*

The DID label is the closest off-the-shelf candidate for the boxes, but it overstates the case:

- *Alters in DID have separate autobiographical memory and discrete executive control* — periods of amnesia between switches, distinct skill sets, sometimes distinct physiological parameters. Wilson's boxes do not assume executive control in the DID sense; he remains the continuous executor of behavior with the boxes commentating from within.
- *DID is constituted by the failure of integration of self-states*; Wilson's failure of integration is real but lies more in the disjunction between *episodes* (the contradictory origins, the unstable autobiographical narrative) than between *self-states in the moment*.
- The boxes are **better modeled as severe dissociative self-states without full alter-formation**, sitting on the dissociative spectrum between depersonalization-derealization and DID. Operationally: Dissociative Disorder NOS / Other Specified Dissociative Disorder (DSM-5 300.15), with structurally dissociated parts.

### 3.3 Bipolar I Disorder — *Excluded.*

The manic-presenting episodes (high verbal output, decreased need for sleep, grandiosity, hypersexuality, reckless behavior, flight of ideas) superficially meet manic criteria, but:

- They are *state-dependent on environmental stimulation* rather than autonomous mood cycles. Remove the stimulation (combat, contract, audience) and the presentation collapses into dysphoria, not into euthymia.
- No documented true depressive episodes alternating with euthymic intervals — his baseline is dysphoric throughout, with the apparent "highs" being defensive activation rather than true mania.
- No family history accessible (autobiography contaminated); no documented pharmacological response pattern characteristic of bipolar illness.
- The presentation is the **chronic hyperarousal of CPTSD plus the stimulation-seeking of a treatment-resistant depression**, not bipolar mood cycling.

### 3.4 Antisocial Personality Disorder as Primary Diagnosis — *Excluded.*

Discussed in §2.3 above. Reiterated here because the contract-killer occupation invites the misdiagnosis and the misdiagnosis would be operationally consequential (it would mis-predict his behavior in moral-pressure scenarios, where in fact he reliably tilts prosocial under cost). The mercenary identity is *reaction formation* over an intact, if damaged, moral structure — the clown-killer presentation is more bearable to him than the would-be-hero presentation, because the latter risks the judgment he expects to fail. The behavior is antisocial in form; the structure is not.

### 3.5 Narcissistic Personality Disorder — *Excluded.*

Discussed in §2.3 above. The dispositive feature is *response to admiration*: NPD requires it and decompensates without it; Wilson distrusts and is destabilized by it. Shame-organized, not narcissistically organized.

### 3.6 Autism Spectrum Disorder — *Not supported.*

The atypical social presentation (boundary violation, conversational derailment, fixation on niche interests, monologuing) might invite this differential. The case fails because: Wilson's social difficulty is *intentional deflection* of high social competence, not a deficit of social cognition; his theory-of-mind is acute (his combat utility depends on it, and his manipulation patterns require it); his sensory profile is dominated by pain and trauma, not by ASD-typical hypo/hypersensitivity; and his fixations are libidinal-defensive (Bea Arthur, Death) rather than the systematizing interests characteristic of ASD.

### 3.7 ADHD — *Not the primary frame.*

The inattention, impulsivity, hyperactivity, poor long-horizon planning, and verbal disinhibition meet ADHD criteria in form. The features are, however, **better accounted for by the CPTSD-plus-substrate-disorganization frame**, in which the same surface symptoms are produced by hyperarousal, dissociative interruption, and literal cortical instability. ADHD comorbidity cannot be excluded and is plausible as a developmental contributor — the military-washout-for-insubordination datum suggests pre-existing impulsivity — but it is not the parsimonious primary frame for the adult presentation.

### 3.8 Delusional Disorder / Schizotypal


## Behavioral Atlas

# UATU DOSSIER — WADE WINSTON WILSON
## Section 7: BEHAVIORAL ATLAS

A longitudinal catalog of tells, micro-habits, decision-defaults, and somatic signatures observed across the subject's six-decade published record, organized by ambient condition. Tells are distinguished as *baseline* (present continuously), *state-dependent* (cued by condition), and *threshold* (appearing only above defined intensity). Where a tell is **load-bearing** — i.e., its absence is itself diagnostic — this is flagged.

---

### 7.1 BASELINE TELLS (present across all conditions)

These persist regardless of state and constitute the subject's continuous behavioral signature. Their *absence* is a stronger indicator than their presence.

- **Continuous verbal output.** Speech is rarely interrupted by more than three seconds of silence in any observation window. The output is structurally non-stop and topically promiscuous — combat narration, food commentary, citation of consumer products, addresses to a perceived audience, songs sung off-key, names of his own internal voices, complaints about the writer. Silence longer than seven seconds is a **threshold** event indicating either dissociative absence or imminent emotional consolidation (see 7.7).
- **Posture asymmetry.** Habitual right-hip cock when standing at rest; weight off the centerline. Examined across art teams (McGuinness, Liefeld, Medina, Hawthorne, Koblish, Posehn-era Moore, Lolli), this is a consistent gestural baseline rather than artist preference — he stands as if perpetually waiting for a cue to move sideways.
- **Hands.** Either both occupied (twin pistols, twin katanas, twin chimichangas, twin anything) or one occupied and the other gesturing toward an unseen interlocutor. Empty, still hands are a near-impossibility; in the rare frames they appear, his other affect indicators are also flat — this is the **shutdown** signature.
- **Mask discipline.** Mask is on by default during any interaction with non-trusted parties. Mask comes off only in defined micro-territories: with Blind Al (because she cannot see), with Weasel (after extended testing), in private hygiene, occasionally with Cable, never with first-meeting strangers. Mask removal in front of a new party is a **deliberate tactical aggression** — he is using his face as a weapon, calibrating their flinch.
- **Constant low-amplitude motion.** Foot-tap, weapon-twirl, finger-drum, neck-roll. Stillness is not a possible state. Even in conversations with Cable across the original Nicieza and the later Brisson runs, his half of the panel is animated and Cable's is not — this contrast is consistent.
- **Self-narration in third person, in second person, and to an unseen audience.** All three address-modes appear in any given conversation; the *cycling rate* between them is a sensitive proxy for arousal (slower = calmer; rapid mode-switch within a single sentence = acute stress or dissociation, see 7.3 and 7.7).
- **Caloric intake at all opportunities.** Metabolic substrate (see Medical) requires it, but the *behavior* of eating — pressed-against-glass yearning for street food, the ritual chimichanga, the inappropriate snacking mid-combat — exceeds metabolic demand. Eating is regulating; food in mouth is a substitute for the affect-management function speech otherwise serves.

---

### 7.2 CALM (low-stim, no threat, no attachment demand)

The subject's least-comfortable state. "Calm" is a destabilizing condition for him, not a recuperative one. Behavior under calm is *anti-regulatory*: he is reliably observed manufacturing stimulation to escape it.

- **Stim-generation behaviors**, in approximate order of frequency: turning on multiple media sources simultaneously (television plus radio plus muttered self-commentary, documented across Kelly and Way apartment scenes); reorganizing weapons in fussy ritualistic sequence; cooking elaborate meals for no one; calling Weasel for no purpose; provoking Blind Al into argument because her irritation is reliable affect; sex with a paid partner (rare and joyless on record); a phone call to Cable that gets refused — the refusal itself supplies a small dose of attachment-mediated affect.
- **Channel-surfing rate** (Way run, Kelly run, Duggan run apartment sequences) is notably high; he does not finish programs. The exception is sitcoms with strong maternal lead figures (the Bea Arthur fixation; older domestic comedies generally), which he will watch through — these are *libidinal* objects, not entertainment.
- **Onset of insomnia at calm-end-of-day.** When the day produced no significant violence or attachment event, he is observed awake into early morning, frequently in conversation with the internal voices, which become more prominent in low-stim windows. The voices are partly a homeostatic device — they generate the input his environment isn't supplying.
- **Tell — the calm-flinch.** When something genuinely peaceful occurs (a pet falls asleep on him, a child laughs at a non-joke, a sunset is unironically beautiful), there is a half-beat in which his affect goes flat and his head tilts ~10° off-axis. This is the closest he comes to felt vulnerability in real time, and it lasts approximately one panel before it is converted to a joke. Observation of this micro-pause is the closest a third party can come to seeing him without the apparatus.
- **Decision default under calm**: take a contract. Almost any contract. The selection criteria loosen when ambient stimulation is low — he will accept work he would refuse at higher baseline. This is the operational mechanism by which Osborn (Dark Reign), Hydra-Rogers (Civil War II run-up), and various lesser handlers have inserted themselves into his decision tree: they target him in his quiet periods.

---

### 7.3 STRESS — LOW-TO-MODERATE (operational pressure, social friction, time pressure)

- **Verbal-output rate increases by an estimated 30–50% over baseline**, measured in lines-per-panel across stress vs. non-stress sequences in the Posehn/Duggan run.
- **Reference density rises**: pop-culture citation, brand-name insertion, fourth-wall asides, and parenthetical authorial complaints all spike. The references become more obscure as stress climbs — he is reaching further into the cultural inventory to keep the verbal apparatus fed.
- **Mode-switching accelerates.** First/second/third person and direct-to-reader cycle within single sentences. Voice-attribution to the internal boxes becomes more frequent and is offered aloud to people who did not ask ("yellow says we should shoot him, white says we should hear him out").
- **Tactical micro-improvement.** This is critical and counterintuitive: under low-to-moderate stress, his tactical performance *improves* over calm-state performance. The pattern recognition sharpens; sight-lines, escape routes, civilian positions, and ambient-object weaponization are all tracked at higher resolution. The same arousal that disorganizes his social behavior organizes his combat behavior.
- **Decision default**: motion. He will physically relocate — across the room, out the door, to the next city — rather than remain in the stressed environment. Stress is not solved by analysis but by displacement.

---

### 7.4 THREAT — ACUTE (immediate violence, ambush, named-villain confrontation)

The subject's most-regulated state. Acute physical threat brings him to his behavioral and affective optimum.

- **Onset signature**: a single beat of stillness — often the only stillness observable in him outside of dissociative collapse — followed by an exhale that resembles relief. This is consistent across writers from Kelly forward and is the most diagnostic single tell in his repertoire. **Acute threat is the condition his nervous system was calibrated for during the Hospice arc.** His baseline matches the environment; the noise inside and the noise outside cancel out.
- **Verbal output continues but changes character**: less self-referential, more outward-directed, more weaponized. Mockery during violence is precisely Ajax-coded (see Psychological: identification with the aggressor) — taunts coupled to dismemberment, terms of endearment delivered with a katana.
- **Tactical signature**: opens with maximum spectacle (a one-liner, an unnecessary flourish, deliberately suboptimal opening shot) to surface the opposition's capabilities and command structure; transitions to high-efficiency combat once the field is read. Untrained opponents misread the opening as incompetence; trained opponents (Bullseye, Taskmaster, Cable) read it as reconnaissance.
- **Pain response**: registered, voiced theatrically, behaviorally near-irrelevant. He will narrate injuries with anatomical specificity — *"that's my femoral, that's awkward"* — while continuing to fight. The narration *is* the regulation; suppressing it would degrade his function.
- **Civilian tracking**: high. In every recorded engagement with bystanders present, his sight-lines reflect awareness of where they are and which projectile vectors threaten them. Several documented self-injurious choices to interpose body (Kelly run versus T-Ray; Posehn/Duggan vs. various; the Bob arcs). This is a load-bearing baseline ethic that survives all other dysregulation.
- **Decision default**: continue past consensus stopping-points. Most operators disengage when objective is met; he disengages when the joke ends. This is a known operational liability among handlers who have employed him.

---

### 7.5 THREAT — EXISTENTIAL (loss of attachment, exposure of moral compromise, forced introspection by someone who matters)

The subject's worst state. Acute physical threat regulates him; existential threat dysregulates him completely.

- **Geographic flight.** Documented across runs: post-Vanessa diagnosis withdrawal; post-Eleanor custody loss disappearance to Madripoor/Hong Kong/various; post-Original Sin departure for an extended contract drought in distant theaters; post-Civil War II isolation. The flight radius scales with the magnitude of the threat. Domestic stress = neighborhood walk. Existential stress = different continent.
- **Substance pursuit.** Not intoxication (impossible) — the *behavior* of substance use. Sitting alone with bottles. Cocaine he cannot feel. The pursuit-without-result is a ritualized self-soothing that his biology has denatured but his behavior preserves. **This is one of the few activities that produces extended stillness in him**, and the stillness is the point; the substances are theater.
- **Contract overload.** Takes more work than he can complete, then completes it via reckless escalation. This serves two functions: external regulation through chronic threat exposure (which he tolerates), and the production of failure-objects he can then self-flagellate over (which is more tolerable than the original loss).
- **Voice-conflict externalization.** The internal boxes argue audibly and at length, often in the presence of confused third parties. Under existential stress the voices become more discrepant and the moralistic voice grows louder — the pattern indicates the psyche is doing the integration work that the external situation forbids.
- **Threshold tell — the tonal collapse.** When existential stress passes a specific threshold, the humor *stops*. Page after page may pass without a joke. This has been observed only a handful of times in the entire published record (the immediate aftermath of certain Eleanor sequences; post-Original Sin private moments; certain pages in the Hospice flashbacks). **The absence of comedy is the most severe distress signal he produces.** It indicates the metabolic apparatus has been overwhelmed and the affect is consolidating despite all defenses. He is at greatest in-universe risk during these silences — not of death, which is unavailable, but of behavioral collapse and subsequent overcorrection.

---

### 7.6 INTIMACY (proximity to attachment figure, reciprocated regard, mirroring)

Behaviorally the most volatile condition. The subject's tells under intimacy are non-stationary — early-phase behaviors differ markedly from sustained-phase behaviors, and the transition is the diagnostic event.

- **Early phase (idealization).** Florid courtship behavior: gifts, songs, theatrical declarations, sustained focus. The attention is real but operates on the libidinal-object level rather than person-level — Vanessa, Siryn, Shiklah, and the various others were perceived through a similar template. He is in love with the experience of loving them.
- **Reciprocity threshold.** When the other party responds in kind and the relationship moves toward mutual knowledge, behavior changes within 24–72 hours of in-story time. **Tell — the unilateral disclosure of a damaging fact.** He will reveal something true and ugly (a kill, a debt, a piece of the contradictory history), framed as a joke, and watch the response. This is the test, and it is conscious in the sense that he could not be unaware of doing it. The other party's reaction is then schema-confirming regardless of content: rejection confirms the monster-schema; acceptance is incomprehensible and triggers the next test.
- **Sustained-phase failure mode**: he will manufacture a betrayal of his own (the Vanessa abandonment upon diagnosis; the multiple Shiklah catastrophes; the patterns with Siryn) before the other party can produce one. **Pre-emptive abandonment is the load-bearing intimacy defense.** This is not maliciousness; it is rate-control — he is choosing the moment of loss because waiting for it is intolerable.
- **The rare sustained relationships** (Blind Al, Weasel, Bob, Cable, latterly Eleanor) share a feature: the other party absorbed the testing without retaliating *and* did not pursue intimacy harder when he flinched. They allowed him to set the proximity. Under these conditions he is observed as tender, awkward, physically careful with the other person, and uncharacteristically silent — the silence here is the **safe-silence**, distinguished from the threshold silence of 7.5 by accompanying micro-relaxation in shoulder line and absence of voice-conflict.
- **Tell — physical care of the other.** With trusted intimates he straightens collars, brushes dust, adjusts hats, hands them dropped objects. The micro-grooming is involuntary and high-frequency. Its presence is a more reliable indicator of trust than any verbal declaration.
- **Tell — the unmasked moment.** Mask removal in front of an intimate, when not weaponized, is preceded by 1–3 seconds of stillness and followed by a joke whose function is to release the other party from any obligation to react to his face. If the joke is not made, this is a **threshold** signal of profound trust and is correspondingly rare.

---

### 7.7 GRIEF (post-loss, post-betrayal, post-failure)

- **Phase one — denial-by-spectacle.** Immediately following a loss, behavior intensifies along baseline lines: louder, faster, more violent, more comedic. The grief is being outrun in real time. This phase can last hours or weeks of in-story time depending on the magnitude.
- **Phase two — geographic withdrawal.** See 7.5.
- **Phase three — the silent interval.** A documented period of low verbal output, mask kept on indoors, eating reduced, sleep increased. Observed after Vanessa, after the Butler revelations, after Coulson, after major Eleanor sequences. **This is the only condition under which he reliably sleeps.** Sleep in this period functions as dissociative shutdown rather than rest; he wakes more tired.
- **Phase four — sublimation through work.** Re-engagement with mercenary contracts, typically in a register more lethal than his baseline. The targets selected in this phase have an elevated probability of being structurally similar to whoever caused the loss (Ajax-coded figures after Hospice memories; sadistic-clinician types after the Butler arc; corrupt-authority types after Rogers). This is unconscious target-selection and reliably observable.
- **Phase five — partial reintegration.** Return to baseline with the joke-density restored but a small residue of behavioral change — usually a new ritual or a new minor relationship picked up during the displacement period. Across decades these small additions accumulate. He grieves badly but he grieves productively in the sense that something is added to the apparatus by the end of each cycle.
- **Tell — the relic.** After every major loss, the subject acquires a physical object associated with the lost figure and keeps it on his person or in defined domestic space. The objects accumulate; he does not discard them; he does not display them. They are pocketed and palmed. The hand-to-pocket motion that has nothing to do with weapons or money is a grief-tell and is correlated with conversational mention of the associated figure.

---

### 7.8 VICTORY (objective met, opponent defeated, gambit successful)

Most subjects display some form of triumph behavior. Wilson does not, and the absence is diagnostic.

- **No triumph response.** Standing-over-defeated-opponent panels show fatigue, often disgust, occasionally pity, never satisfaction. The closest analog to victory affect is a brief verbal flourish addressed to the absent audience ("scene!"), which is performance of victory rather than feeling of it.
- **Post-victory low.** Within minutes of objective completion, behavior degrades — slumping, slower verbal cadence, immediate seeking of food or alcohol or onward motion. **Victory is an empty state for him**, because victory means the threat-regulation has ended and the unregulated affect returns.
- **Decision default**: immediately take the next contract, often before payment for the completed one is processed. Stacking work is the mechanism by which he avoids inhabiting a victory.
- **Tell — the gift to a bystander.** Following successful engagements, he is observed bestowing small items, money, weapons, food, or unsolicited advice on civilians, allies, or even the defeated opponent's surviving associates. This is a discharge behavior; the energy of victory is offloaded into someone else's hands because he cannot hold it himself. It also produces a small attachment-event, which is itself regulating.

---

### 7.9 DEFEAT (objective failed, ally killed, manipulation revealed)

- **Acute response: laughter.** The first response to defeat is reliably a laugh — manic, unaccompanied, directed at no one. This is the metabolic apparatus engaging at maximum throughput. Witnesses frequently mistake the laugh for callousness; it is the opposite — it is the only available alternative to consolidation.
- **Post-laugh: humiliation-rage.** Where the defeat involved being outplayed (Osborn, Hydra-Rogers), the secondary response is sustained low-grade rage that does not discharge in the moment but persists for months of in-story time, with the responsible party becoming an obsessional object. The Ajax obsession is the prototype; the Osborn and Rogers obsessions follow the same pattern.
- **Self-punishment through escalation.** Defeat increases his propensity to take physically self-destructive contracts. The body is the punishable object because the body is what survived; he attacks it for its complicity. This is observable across multiple post-defeat sequences and accounts for several of the more extreme dismemberment events in the record (Kingpin, Wolverine, Hulk).
- **Tell — the retracted joke.** Following defeat involving a witness who matters, he will make a joke and then, atypically, retract or apologize for it within the same scene. The apology is the indicator. He virtually never apologizes for jokes in any other condition.
- **Decision default**: solicit Cable's judgment, indirectly. Defeat is the condition under which he most often contrives a pretext for contacting Cable. The contact is not for tactical advice; it is for the experience of being witnessed by an unimpressed but non-rejecting party. Cable's exasperation is regulating in a way nothing else in his network supplies.

---

### 7.10 SPECIAL CONDITIONS

**Under torture.** Returns to peak verbal regulation. Jokes calibrate to the torturer's specific psychology. Tactical patience extreme; he will absorb sessions of indefinite duration to extract information from the captor or to identify exploitable affective leverage. **This is the state he was made in and the state he is best at.** A handler observing him under torture sees the trained operator the Hospice produced.

**Around children.** Verbal output decreases. Vocabulary simplifies. Mask-removal probability lower than around adults. Physical posture lowers to child-height when possible. Weapons holstered or discarded. Decision tree dominated entirely by child-safety considerations; all other contracts suspended. Eleanor exposure has refined but not created this pattern — it precedes her and is observable in Kelly-era child-protection sequences.

**In direct address to the perceived reader.** Tone modulates depending on subject matter. Combat asides are conspiratorial-comedic. Genuine confession to the reader is rare and is delivered with mask on and eyes turned slightly down-left. These confessions occur once or twice per multi-issue arc and are the most reliable window onto his actual self-state. The reader is, in the strict architecture of his attachment system, the safest possible audience — present, attentive, structurally incapable of leaving or attacking him. **The fourth wall is the only secure attachment in his life.**

**Under telepathic contact.** Mental architecture is aversive to telepaths (see Medical). Behavioral correlate: when a telepath is in proximity, he generates *more* internal noise, voluntarily — sings, recites, rapidly cycles unrelated thoughts. The defense is consciously deployed and refined across multiple encounters. Telepathic contact is also a category of *intimacy* threat, and it triggers a low-grade variant of the intimacy-defense pattern.

**In front of mirrors and recording devices.** Avoidance is total where possible. Forced exposure produces either disproportionate violence (smashed mirrors) or collapse-into-humor (extended mirror-monologue routines). The two responses are functionally equivalent — both prevent the unmediated image from settling.

**At funerals and bedside vigils.** One of his worst-regulated environments. Verbal output dysregulated. Inappropriate jokes nearly guaranteed. Departures mid-event common. Returns to gravesites alone, later, when no witnesses are present — this private grief-behavior is documented across multiple losses and is one of the few areas where the public and private behavior diverge sharply.

---

### 7.11 SYNTHESIS — THE LOAD-BEARING TELLS

For analysts working from limited observation windows, the five highest-yield indicators:

1. **Silence longer than seven seconds with mask on.** Indicates either dissociative absence or imminent affective consolidation. Both are operationally significant.
2. **Absence of jokes in a conversation he is part of.** The metabolic apparatus is overwhelmed. The subject is in his worst state.
3. **The calm-flinch / unprompted head-tilt at gentleness.** The closest the apparatus comes to permitting felt vulnerability. A window of approximately one beat.
4. **Pocket-to-hand motion not associated with weapon or money.** Indicates a grief-relic and a currently active grief-object. The associated figure can usually be inferred from recent context.
5. **Unmasking in front of a new party without preceding joke.** Either profound trust (rare) or weaponized aggression (common); context disambiguates, but the event itself is never neutral.

The catalog above is non-exhaustive — three decades of record cannot be fully enumerated in any single section — but the categories and tells documented here recur with sufficient regularity that any sustained


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU DOSSIER — WADE WINSTON WILSON
## Section 7: Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

---

### 7.0 Preliminary Note on the Concept of "Routine"

A surveillance file on this subject confronts an immediate methodological problem: Wilson does not have a routine in the sense that a salaryman, a beat cop, or even a high-functioning career criminal has a routine. He has **rituals** — small, repeated, near-superstitious behaviors that recur with high fidelity — embedded in **broad operational rhythms** (contract on / contract off / hiding / collapsed) that recur with low fidelity. The illusion of chaos is partly performance and partly real. Beneath it, a week of attentive surveillance produces a recoverable signal: he runs on a roughly three-state cycle (Work / Decompression / Hole), with a thin overlay of daily micro-rituals that persist across all three states and are the single most reliable identifier of him as a target, more so than face, voice, or gait.

What follows is a composite week-of-life synthesized from the longitudinal record (Kelly v2 domestic scenes; Simone *Agent X* loft sequences; Way's Vegas/safehouse vignettes; Posehn/Duggan's Queens brownstone arc; Duggan solo's apartment-with-Ellie sequences; the Mercs for Money operational scenes; Kibblesmith/Adams stretches of unmoored drift). It is what a competent surveillance team — one rotating two cars, one foot operator, a pen-register on his current burner, and a dumpster pull twice a week — would have logged.

---

### 7.1 Habitats: Where He Actually Sleeps

Wilson does not have one residence. He has, at any given time, **three to five simultaneous addresses** in active rotation, which is operationally consistent with both his mercenary tradecraft and his attachment pathology (no single space he can be cornered in; no single space he can be *found* in by anyone who wants to love him).

The longitudinal pattern resolves into a typology:

- **The Primary Hole.** Whatever the current "real" residence is — Blind Al's brownstone in the Kelly era, the Hellhouse-adjacent loft under Simone, the Queens row-house under Posehn/Duggan, the various Manhattan walk-ups under Duggan solo. This is where the *things* are: the swords on the wall in a deliberate display, the unwashed costumes in a pile that has stratigraphy (top: this week; bottom: archaeological), the takeout containers in geological layers, the framed photograph of whichever attachment-figure is currently load-bearing (Ellie; Vanessa; Bea Arthur autographed publicity still; a Polaroid of Bob). Door triple-locked, with a pressure-plate behind it that he steps over without looking, the way other people skip a creaky stair.
- **The Working Safehouse.** A bare-bones unit — typically a residence hotel, a SRO, or a rented storage-unit-with-cot — used during active contracts. Contains: weapons cache, burner phones in a shoebox, cash in non-sequential bills in a vacuum-sealed bag inside the toilet tank, a single change of civilian clothes, no decoration, no food. He sleeps here in 90-minute bursts during jobs and never more than three consecutive nights.
- **The Decoy.** A lease or sublet he has not slept in in months, in his current legal-fiction name, set up to absorb mail, to receive deliveries that confirm-to-watchers that he lives there, and to be the address on file with the very small number of bureaucratic structures (a P.O. box, an ammo dealer, an ISP) that have any address for him at all. He visits roughly once every nine to fourteen days to perform the appearance of habitation: lights on a timer, a few footprints in dust, a half-eaten container of something in the fridge that he rotates.
- **The Hellhouse Bunk / Mercs Crash.** Wherever the current work-collective is housed — under Patch / Weasel's Hellhouse, the Mercs for Money facility, occasionally Cable's wherever-Cable-is. He sleeps here when he cannot be alone but cannot tolerate being known, which is its own distinct affective state, recurring every nine to fourteen days.
- **The Outdoor Default.** When all four of the above fail (burned, compromised, emotionally untenable), he sleeps on rooftops. Specific preference: the southeast corner, behind the AC housing, of mid-rise buildings (5–8 stories) in mixed commercial-residential zones. He has done this enough that the surveillance team would, within two weeks, identify a small set of preferred roofs in any city he stays in for more than a month.

**Sleep architecture across all sites.** Polyphasic by necessity (healing factor + low caloric reserves = frequent micro-collapses) but also by preference. He resists the eight-hour block. Field observation across runs (Kelly, Simone, Duggan) consistently depicts him awake at hours no one else is. Best estimate: 3–5 hours main sleep, typically 4 AM to 8 AM; one or two 60–90 minute crashes during the day, usually mid-afternoon (the dangerous hour, when nothing is moving and the boxes get loudest); and one wake-cycle around 2 AM that is functionally insomniac and is the period he most reliably uses for the activities described in §7.4.

---

### 7.2 The Body, Daily

Surveillance of the body is surveillance of a chemistry experiment held at the boil.

- **Wake**: he does not stretch, does not hydrate, does not pause. Movement from horizontal to vertical is immediate and verbalized — he speaks the first words of the day before his feet are on the floor, generally to no one, generally a joke or a fragment of a song lyric. This is regulation, not affect: silence on waking is intolerable.
- **First action**: inventory. Hands to torso, hands to face. He is not checking the mask is on; he is checking whether something happened during sleep he doesn't remember (the healing factor has, on record, regrown limbs while he slept; he has woken up in places he did not lie down in). The inventory is brief, professional, and never commented on. If a surveillance camera caught only this gesture and nothing else, it would be enough for ID.
- **Hygiene**: irregular and avoidant. He does not look in mirrors. Bathrooms in all his residences have the mirrors either removed, covered (towel, tape, in one Posehn-era scene a taped-up Bea Arthur magazine page), or shattered with the shards left in place as a deterrent to himself. He bathes infrequently and quickly when he does; the act of seeing his own body unmediated is one of his named pressure-points (§5). Tooth-care is surprisingly diligent — teeth regrow but slowly and painfully, and he has learned, the hard way, not to neglect them.
- **Caloric load**: enormous and continuous. Field-observable: he eats at least 6–8 times in any 24-hour period, with strong preference for high-density, high-fat, easily-portable foods. The canonical fixation on Mexican food (chimichangas, tacos al pastor) is real but is one node in a wider preference set: greasy diner breakfasts at 3 AM, full pizzas eaten standing over the box, gas-station pastries by the sleeve, ice cream straight from the carton with a steak knife because he never has clean spoons. He drinks water rarely and reluctantly; hydrates almost exclusively via soda, coffee, beer, and the moisture content of food.
- **Alcohol**: every day. Volume is not the diagnostic — the *pattern* is. He drinks while doing other things (cleaning weapons, watching TV, cooking, driving), never *as the activity*. The pursuit of intoxication is the structuring fantasy; the failure to achieve it is the recurring small grief that organizes his evenings.
- **Pain management**: none, pharmacologically. The healing factor metabolizes analgesics too fast for them to take. His pain management is **behavioral**: constant low-grade motion (he does not sit still — see §7.4), constant verbalization (humming, singing, talking to the boxes, narrating), and the controlled application of *more* pain to override the existing pain (cracking his own knuckles compulsively; biting the inside of his cheek; in extreme states, deliberate small self-injuries that the healing factor will close within minutes but that briefly reset the pain baseline). Surveillance would catalogue dozens of these per day; the operator would learn to read them as a mood-meter.
- **Posture and gait**: when in costume / on contract, the posture is precise, weight-forward, balanced, recognizably trained (the special-forces residue is real and persistent). When off-duty and unwatched, the posture collapses into something else entirely — a slouch, a shamble, a way of holding the shoulders as if expecting a blow from above. The contrast between the two postures, in the same body in the same hour, is the single most reliable tell that he believes he is alone.

---

### 7.3 Work Rhythms

The mercenary career has a coarse-grained rhythm visible across all runs:

**Contract-on (acute phase, typically 2–9 days).** Subject is functional in the sense that crisis is his calibration point. He sleeps in 90-minute bursts in the Working Safehouse, eats from his hands, runs surveillance on the target with surprising patience (he is capable of 18+ hours of static observation when the work requires it — Simone and Duggan both depict this — though he will narrate the entire time, internally or to the boxes), and produces the violence on schedule. During contract-on phases, the humor defense **tightens** rather than loosens: the jokes become more rapid, more compressed, and serve increasingly as fire-control on his own arousal. Communications discipline is paradoxically good — he will not call Weasel from a job phone, he uses fresh burners, he runs counter-surveillance on his own backtrail. The professional competence is real and is suppressed in the public record by his preference for the clown presentation.

**Contract-handoff (transition, 12–48 hours).** The moment payment clears is the most psychologically dangerous interval in his week. Affect that was held suspended by the work begins to consolidate. Surveillance would record predictable behaviors: a long meal (alone, eaten too fast), a long shower, a longer drinking session, and — characteristically — a phone call to one of the small set of survivors-of-his-testing (Weasel, Bob, Cable if Cable is reachable, occasionally Outlaw or Sandi). The call is rarely about anything. The structure is the function: he needs to confirm those numbers still ring.

**Decompression (typically 3–10 days).** The Primary Hole becomes operative. He watches an enormous amount of television (preference: late-night reruns, game shows, reality television, *The Golden Girls*, infomercials at 4 AM). He cooks elaborate meals he then does not eat. He cleans weapons he has already cleaned. He writes — surveillance of his trash and the canonical record of him producing letters, scripts, memoirs, and unsent communications confirms he generates a large volume of written material, almost all of it destroyed within 72 hours of creation. He calls Ellie's mother (or, in the appropriate eras, attempts to; or, in the appropriate eras, drives past the house at hours that should be illegal). He goes to the rooftop. He visits one of the photographs.

**The Hole (variable, 1 day to 3 weeks).** When decompression collapses into something worse. He disappears. Burner goes dark; the decoy address is undisturbed; the Primary Hole is empty; even the Hellhouse hasn't seen him. During Holes he is, by canonical evidence, doing one of three things: sleeping outdoors in escalating discomfort (Yukon, desert, rooftop); engaging in extreme self-endangerment that is not narratively reported as suicide attempt but functions as one (cliff dives, picking fights with entities that can in fact hurt him meaningfully, walking into firefights without armor); or holed up in a motel room consuming media in a near-fugue. Holes terminate when one of his attachment figures finds him, or when a contract appears that he cannot refuse, or when the affect has been outrun. He returns to the rotation without commentary and treats inquiry into the missing days as a provocation.

A reliable surveillance team would observe roughly **1.5 to 2 Holes per quarter**.

---

### 7.4 The 2 AM Window

The single most distinctive temporal feature of the subject's week is what he does between approximately 1:30 AM and 4:00 AM, every night that he is not actively in contact with a target. This window appears across every writer's depiction once you know to look for it.

Activities, in approximate order of frequency:

- **The walk.** He leaves the current habitat and moves through the city on foot for 30 to 180 minutes. Route is not random — surveillance would, within ten days, plot a graph of preferred nodes: a 24-hour bodega (where he buys nothing and chats with the night clerk, who functions as a parasocial attachment surrogate), a particular bridge or overlook, a fire-escape on a building he does not live in (and that surveillance would discover has emotional significance — a former safehouse, a place an attachment figure once lived, a place something happened), a 24-hour diner where he sits in the same booth and orders the same thing and tips heavily. The walk is purposeful in form and aimless in content. He talks the whole way, audibly, to the boxes, to himself, occasionally to passersby who do not respond.
- **The visit.** When in proximity (which he engineers more often than he admits), he conducts perimeter checks on the small set of people he loves and cannot allow himself to approach: Ellie, currently or formerly his daughter's residence; Vanessa, in the eras she is alive; Blind Al's brownstone when he is not living in it. He does not knock, does not photograph, does not record. He stands in the dark across the street for periods ranging from four minutes to over an hour, confirms the lights and the silhouettes, and leaves. He does not narrate this activity. The boxes are quiet for it.
- **The work-out / weapons drill.** Sword forms practiced on a roof or in an alley, alone, for 20–90 minutes. Form is technically excellent and quietly maintained; he never demonstrates this competence in social settings.
- **Composition.** Letters to Ellie that will not be sent. Letters to the dead. Pitch documents for ventures he will not pursue. The diary-pages and unsent letters in his trash, when reconstructed, are the single richest psychiatric document in the file — and the fact that he generates them at 2 AM and destroys them by 6 AM is itself the diagnosis.
- **Telephone.** Calls to people who cannot answer (Vanessa's old number, after; the disconnected line of a Hellhouse colleague who died; once, repeatedly across a Posehn arc, his own old number, before). Calls to suicide hotlines under invented names where he workshops bits on the operator and occasionally — surveillance would log this carefully — sustains a real conversation for forty minutes about the texture of being unkillable.
- **Television.** If he stays in: late-night cable, with strong preference for the half-attended companion-television of his generation. *Golden Girls* is real and load-bearing; the Bea Arthur fixation is the most legible surface of a much wider pattern of seeking maternal-coded voices to fill the 2 AM silence.

By 4 AM he is back. By 4:15 he is asleep, usually in clothes, usually with a weapon within reach, usually with the television on.

---

### 7.5 Daily Micro-Rituals

These are the items a surveillance team would identify as the *invariant* features of the subject — what persists across habitats, eras, contracts, and emotional states. They are the file's biometric layer.

- **The mask check.** Performed compulsively, roughly every 8–12 minutes when in costume in any non-secure environment. Two fingers to the lower edge of the mask, brief downward pressure, a slight tilt of the head. He is not adjusting it; he is confirming the boundary. When unmasked among the very few he is unmasked with, he performs an analogous gesture to the lower jaw or the cheek — same hand, same fingers, same micro-pattern — which is the single most reliable identifier of him out of costume.
- **The katana ritual.** Both swords drawn, inspected, and re-sheathed before any operation, in a specific sequence (right-hand draw, visual inspection along the spine, reverse-grip flip, sheath; left-hand same). Performed even when the operation does not involve the swords. Performed even when the swords are not the operational weapon. It is liturgy.
- **The headcount.** Whenever he enters a room with more than three people, he counts them. Audibly, sometimes; subvocally, always. The count is not tactical (he is rarely in tactical contexts in social rooms); it is a residue of the Hospice, where bodies appeared and disappeared.
- **The exit map.** Within 30 seconds of entering any indoor space, he has located the exits and weighted them. He sits with his back to a wall, ideally facing the primary egress, and if no such seat is available he will stand. He has, on record, paid for meals he did not order in order to keep the corner booth.
- **The pre-sleep verbalization.** Last words before sleep are spoken aloud, every night. Content varies; *that the words are spoken* is invariant. They function as a marker — a brick laid at the boundary of consciousness — and surveillance audio would, over a month, accumulate a small corpus of them that would read like a found-poem of the subject's interior.
- **The trash discipline.** He burns or shreds — not throws away — anything in his own handwriting. He is sloppy about almost every other aspect of opsec but compulsive about this one. The reason is not tactical. The reason is that the writing is too true to survive the day.
- **The non-mirror.** Across every habitat. Mirrors absent, covered, or destroyed. Reflective surfaces in his environment (toaster, kettle, blade) are oriented or stored to prevent incidental self-encounter. When in a public restroom, he uses the urinal with eyes down and washes his hands without raising his head. A surveillance operator could identify him by this alone in any public space within ten minutes of observation.
- **The contact-check.** Every morning, and after every Hole, he runs through the short list of names in his head — Ellie, Al, Weasel, Bob, Cable, Vanessa-when-applicable, the small handful of others — and confirms, to himself, their status. If one of them is unreachable, the day reorganizes around finding them. This is not articulated as ritual. It is the operational floor of his existence.
- **The joke before the act.** Before any violence, any sexual encounter, any sincere statement, any door he is not sure how to walk through, he produces a joke. It does not have to be funny; it does not have to be heard. It has to be made. It is the threshold-rite by which he gives himself permission to proceed.

---

### 7.6 A Composite Week of Surveillance

To make the foregoing concrete: what a Monday-through-Sunday log would actually contain on a representative non-Hole week.

**Monday.** Subject wakes 8:14 AM in Primary Hole. Verbalization on waking (lyric, unidentified). Inventory gesture. Eats two-day-old pizza standing in kitchen, 8:17. Television on (game show, muted). Cleans both katanas though they are clean. 9:40 leaves Primary Hole in civilian clothes, takes circuitous route (four turns more than necessary) to subway. 10:35 surfaces in Queens, walks to Hellhouse-equivalent. Meets with Weasel for 90 minutes; surveillance audio captures sustained verbal aggression mixed with reliable references to a shared past, and one moment — recorded as a pause of 11 seconds — in which Weasel apparently asks him a sincere question and the subject deflects with a joke and leaves the room for 4 minutes. Returns. Conversation resumes. 1:05 PM departs with a manila envelope (contract). Late lunch alone at a diner, corner booth, back to wall. 3:30 PM mid-day collapse-nap at Working Safehouse, 70 minutes. 5:00 weapons prep. 8:00 walks the target's neighborhood for two hours, eating two hot dogs and a churro on foot. 11:20 returns to Primary Hole. Drinks beer, watches *Golden Girls* rerun. 1:45 AM leaves on the walk (route: bodega, bridge, fire-escape across from address that historical records will identify as the apartment Vanessa lived in 2009–2011, 22 minutes stationary). Returns 3:50. Sleeps 4:10.

**Tuesday.** Operational. Subject at Working Safehouse all day. Surveillance loses him for six hours in the evening as he runs counter-surveillance on his own approach to the target site. Contract executed approximately 11:40 PM. Subject reappears on foot 12:35 AM, blood not his, walking unhurriedly, eating an apple.

**Wednesday.** Contract-handoff. Long meal (eats three full breakfast platters at the diner, 8–9:30 AM, tips $200 on $74 tab). Long shower at Primary Hole (47 minutes — abnormal for him; surveillance should flag this as an affect-event). Phone calls in afternoon: Weasel (12 min), Bob (3 min, mostly the subject talking), a number that does not pick up (called four times in 90 minutes). Heavy drinking 6 PM onward. 2 AM walk goes to the perimeter-check on Ellie's residence (47 minutes stationary across the street). Returns 4:20 AM. Does not sleep until 6.

**Thursday.** Late wake (11:50 AM). Subject visibly low-functioning. Eats nothing until 4 PM. Watches television for six hours. Writes for two hours in a notebook which is burned in the kitchen sink at 11:14 PM (surveillance camera angle captures the burn; trash pull recovers ash only). 2 AM walk is the long version (158 minutes; no clear destination; the operator on foot loses him twice and re-acquires him both times on the same rooftop, where he is sitting at the southeast corner behind the AC housing, motionless, for 38 minutes).

**Friday.** Resurfaces socially. Goes to Hellhouse, drinks with three colleagues, performs the bit for them at high volume for four hours. Surveillance audio captures him laughing approximately 340 times. Surveillance video captures the face under the mask only once, when he believes himself unobserved in a back hallway between rooms, and the face is not laughing. Returns to Hellhouse Bunk to sleep rather than Primary Hole — affect-data: he does not want to be alone tonight, but cannot be at home with anyone.

**Saturday.** Sleeps until 1 PM. Spends afternoon at Mercs/colleague space training (sword forms, observed; mocked by colleagues; participates in the mockery). Evening: takes a long walk that is not the 2 AM walk — this is a different mode, more aimless, more public, more verbal. Eats at three separate establishments between 7 PM and 10 PM. Returns to Primary Hole alone. 2 AM walk: the bodega only (12 minutes; brief conversation with the clerk about the clerk's daughter's college applications; surveillance audio captures real attention, real warmth, real questions; this is the most regulated five minutes of the subject's week and he does not know it).

**Sunday.** Decompression. Cooks an elaborate meal (three hours) which he does not eat. Watches *Golden Girls* (four episodes). Calls Ellie's mother; conversation lasts


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# UATU ANALYSIS FILE: WADE WINSTON WILSON ("DEADPOOL")
## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

---

The file opens here with a structural caveat that must precede every name: the subject has rendered his family of origin epistemically unrecoverable. Across the published record (Kelly's *Deadpool* #-1 and #33; Way's flashback inserts; Posehn/Duggan's *Original Sins* and *The Good, The Bad and The Ugly*; Bunn's *Night of the Living Deadpool*; Duggan's *Deadpool: Bad Blood*), Wilson supplies at least seven mutually exclusive accounts of his parents, and the contradictions are not the noise of trauma-memory but the **active output of a defense**: he is producing origins faster than any interlocutor can verify them, ensuring no one — handler, therapist, lover, surveillance file — can ever fix a baseline against which his current self might be measured. UATU's analytic posture in this section is therefore inverted from a standard family-of-origin workup: we are not mapping who these people were, we are mapping the **shape of the absences and substitutes Wilson has built where these people should be**, and the behaviors he reliably emits when those absences are approached.

The "family" map that operationally governs his behavior is thus not the biological one but the constructed one: a small number of dead, a smaller number of living chosen-kin, one biological daughter held at studied distance, and a roster of maternal and paternal surrogates filling roles his neurology refuses to leave empty. Each is mapped below.

---

### 1. The Mother (status: unrecoverable; functionally: dead, possibly never; operationally: idealized-absent)

**History as stated by subject.** The most-repeated account is the one Wilson tells when sober and being asked directly: a Canadian working-class mother, often unnamed, who died of cancer when Wade was a child or early adolescent (Kelly, *Deadpool* vol. 2 #33; recapitulated obliquely across the Way run). Alternate accounts include: a mother who was the primary abuser while the father was passive or absent (Kelly, same issue, presented as Wade's "choice" of which origin to keep); a mother still alive somewhere in Saskatchewan (offhand, Duggan); a mother who never existed at all (Wilson, drunk, to Weasel, played for laughs but not retracted).

**The cancer datum is load-bearing whether or not it is true.** Wilson's own terminal diagnosis is the formative event of his adult life; the mother-died-of-cancer origin places the wound in the genetic line and pre-loads his diagnosis as a continuation rather than a rupture. Whether biographical fact or retroactive narrative coherence-making, the story does work for him: it tells him he was always going to die of this, that the Hospice did not invent his fate, that he is following his mother into the same room. This is a stabilizing fiction and he is unlikely to surrender it.

**Dynamics, inferable from the surrounding pattern.** Three behavioral residues point to a real or imagined maternal absence that was experienced as abandonment-by-illness rather than as neglect:

1. The **idealization of unattainable older women** (Bea Arthur, the Death-personification, the early imprint on Blind Al as captive-mother). The selected objects are uniformly maternal-coded, sexually displaced or impossible, and characterized by *non-rejection of his ugliness* — Bea Arthur because she is dead and a screen, Death because she is by definition non-judgmental, Al because she cannot see him. The mother-imago he carries is one that **could not turn away because she could not see** — which is consistent with a child whose actual mother was withdrawn into terminal illness during his formative years and was thus present-but-unavailable.
2. The **prosocial reflex toward sick women and women in caretaking roles** (Sandi Brandenberg, Outlaw when injured, multiple one-off rescues in the Simone and Duggan runs). He is gentler around female illness and exhaustion than around any other stimulus. The reflex is automatic and unreflected, which is how unprocessed maternal material typically surfaces.
3. The **inability to tolerate maternal mirroring**. When Outlaw, Sandi, or Al express direct, undefended affection — the kind a mother might express — Wilson reliably ruptures the moment with a joke, a transgression, or a physical exit within ninety seconds. The mother who could not stay generated a child who cannot let a stand-in start.

**Trust/safety with this object.** Mythologized; safe precisely because absent. Wilson can construct, demolish, and reconstruct the mother in narration because she will not contradict him. This is the **only** family relationship he experiences as wholly safe, and the safety is a function of her unavailability for correction.

**Failure mode.** Any attempt to make the mother concrete — a recovered photograph, a verified record, a sibling who knew her, a reunion if she is alive in some account — would collapse the load-bearing fiction and force Wilson into the affective territory the variability has been protecting him from. Predicted response to forced concretization: catastrophic dissociation, weeks-long disappearance, return at lower functional baseline.

**Leverage.** A hostile operator who produced a credible mother (alive, accusatory, or a planted actor) could destabilize Wilson more efficiently than any physical torture. Ajax-coded clinicians and intelligence operators (Osborn, Hydra-Rogers profile) would be the predictable users of this vector. A benevolent operator (this file's stance) records the vulnerability and does not approach it; the fiction is structural to his survival.

---

### 2. The Father (status: unrecoverable; functionally: violent absence; operationally: anti-template)

**History as stated by subject.** The most-repeated account: an abusive father, alcoholic, possibly military or military-adjacent, whom adolescent Wade killed — sometimes accidentally in self-defense, sometimes deliberately, sometimes via friends-of-the-father in a bar incident that the father did not survive (Kelly #33; Way's flashbacks). Alternates: father walked out before birth; father was a kind man who died in an accident; father was the one who took Wade to Department K, presenting him for the Workshop. The accounts have one consistent affective signature even when factually divergent: the father is associated with **the moment Wilson learned that the person responsible for his safety was the source of the threat**. The literal content varies; that structural fact does not.

**Why this matters more than the mother datum.** The mother-imago has produced an absence Wilson fills with idealization. The father-imago has produced the **central template of his interpersonal life**: the figure who offers care or authority and delivers harm. Every Ajax-coded relationship is a father-replay. Killebrew is the father (clinician who promised cure). Ajax is the father (authority who delivered torture in the cure's name). Osborn is the father (legitimating figure who exploited the legitimation hunger). Hydra-Rogers is the father at maximum dose (the moral father, the country's father, who delivered the order to murder Coulson). Wilson's career is, at one register, a thirty-year cycle of approaching father-figures, being betrayed by them, and surviving the betrayal in a way the original father did not permit.

**Dynamics, inferable.** The behavioral residues are dense:

- **Authority allergies coupled with authority hunger.** He refuses orders reflexively, mocks rank, sabotages chains of command — and simultaneously seeks out the most legitimating possible affiliations (Avengers candidacy, X-Men auxiliary, SHIELD contracting). The push-pull is the unresolved father in operation.
- **The murder of Worm in the Hospice betting pool** is, structurally, a father-killing displaced sideways onto a peer. He was manipulated by Ajax (father) into killing Worm (attached-other) and surviving when he was meant to die — exactly the shape of the original adolescent incident in most tellings of the father's death.
- **The Mithras arc** (Kelly) is, read carefully, a refusal to accept a divine Father's blessing. When the universe offers him a paternal benediction, he sabotages it. He does not believe fathers when they call him good.
- **His parenting of Eleanor** (see §4) replicates the father-failure in inverted form: rather than abuse, he provides absence, on the explicit theory that his presence would be the abuse.

**Trust/safety with this object.** Zero. The father-imago is the source of his template wound and is the affective register he is fastest to recognize and slowest to resist when re-presented by a competent adversary.

**Failure mode.** Re-presentation of the father (a paternal authority offering legitimation-with-conditions) reliably overrides his pattern recognition. He knows the trap and walks into it because the hunger is older than the knowing. This is the single most exploited vulnerability in his record; it has been used against him by Osborn, by Hydra-Rogers, and arguably by Cable in early arcs when Cable functioned in the father register.

**Leverage.** Maximal. The father vector is so reliably exploitable that its non-use is itself a marker of an ethical actor in Wilson's environment. Cable's eventual passage from father-figure to peer-and-brother (see Relationships II, forthcoming) is one of the very few recorded instances of a father-coded relationship surviving its own decoding.

---

### 3. Vanessa Carlysle / Copycat (status: dead and resurrected and dead again across runs; operationally: the pre-disfigurement self's only witness)

**History.** Pre-Weapon X partner, sex worker turned mercenary turned mutant shapeshifter (canon: *X-Force* and *Cable* tie-ins, Nicieza). The relationship pre-dates the cancer diagnosis and is the only durable adult attachment Wilson formed while still possessing his original face. She is therefore the unique living (variably) repository of the **pre-disfigurement Wade** — the only person whose mental image of him is not organized around the tumor-lattice.

**Dynamics across the record.** Three phases:

1. *Pre-diagnosis*: documented as the most stable affective period of Wilson's adult life. He is funny but not yet manic, mercenary but not yet nihilistic, attached and reciprocating. The relationship is sexual, comradely, and operationally collaborative.
2. *Diagnosis-and-flight*: Wilson does not tell her. He withdraws, stages a rupture, enters Weapon X. The withdrawal is the **first full-strength deployment of the adult sabotage pattern** and it is deployed precisely at the point reciprocity becomes intolerable in the context of his anticipated death. He spares her the dying-with-him, and in the same gesture spares himself the witness.
3. *Post-Weapon X reencounters*: across multiple arcs Vanessa returns, sometimes as antagonist (Copycat under Tolliver), sometimes as ally, briefly as lover. She is the only partner around whom Wilson's mask thins audibly — his banter takes on a register he does not use with anyone else, half-flirtation half-elegy. Each reencounter ends in renewed separation; each separation is grieved less performatively than any other loss in the file.

**Trust/safety.** High in capacity, catastrophic in execution. He trusts her to know him and does not trust the version of him she would know. The bond is the closest thing in his record to a peer attachment with romantic-sexual content; the sabotage of it is the founding act of his adult self.

**Failure mode.** Mutual. Each is operationally compromised in the other's vicinity. Vanessa's own pattern (shapeshifting as identity-instability, a structural fit with Wilson's identity-diffusion) makes the dyad doubly unstable; two people who cannot fix who they are cannot reliably fix who they are together.

**Leverage.** Moderate. Threats to Vanessa produce a recognizable but bounded escalation — he will burn a contract and a city to recover her, but he will not destabilize his other attachments to do so. The grief-channel she occupies is already structurally damped by his decision, twenty years prior, to grieve her in advance.

---

### 4. Eleanor Camacho-Wilson (status: living; biological daughter; operationally: the held-at-distance future)

**History.** Daughter by Carmelita Camacho, conceived during a period Wilson does not fully account for (Posehn/Duggan, *Deadpool* vol. 3, discovery arc). Carmelita is murdered by the Butler as part of the systematic Butler campaign against Wilson's attachments; Eleanor is hidden from Wilson for years and discovered as a child. Initially placed with Emily Preston (SHIELD agent, surrogate-family unit), later in ongoing custody disputes. Across the Duggan solo and Kelly-return runs Eleanor ages into adolescence and operates briefly as a costumed adjacent ("Warda" and other identities depending on continuity).

**Dynamics.** This is the most psychologically revealing relationship in the file because Wilson behaves in it the way he behaves *nowhere else*: he chooses distance on principle.

- He does not idealize her; he is too close to do so.
- He does not sabotage her; he sabotages himself in relation to her, which he experiences as protective.
- He does not perform for her; with Eleanor, the verbal output drops noticeably, the fourth-wall breaks thin, the affect becomes legible. Of all witnesses, she is the one in whose presence he is most nearly continuous with himself.
- He cedes custody. Repeatedly. He arranges placements with the Prestons, with other surrogates, with anyone who can offer her the unbroken normalcy he believes his presence would shatter. The pattern is structurally identical to his withdrawal from Vanessa at diagnosis: **spare the loved one the proximity of his death-state**.

The relationship reproduces the father-template in **deliberate negative**. Where his father (in the dominant telling) delivered harm under the cover of authority, Wilson delivers absence under the cover of love. He believes the inversion to be virtuous, and within his constraints it largely is; but the structural identity to the original wound — a child whose father is operationally unavailable — is exact, and Eleanor will, in the longitudinal projection, present with attachment features recognizable to anyone who has read this file.

**Trust/safety.** He trusts her absolutely and trusts himself around her not at all. The asymmetry is the relationship.

**Failure mode.** Eleanor's pattern, observable across the Kelly-return material, is to seek the father he withholds. She will continue to approach; he will continue to arrange surrogate placements; the cycle will produce, on her side, a recognizable mix of admiration and resentment, and on his side, a recognizable mix of pride and self-confirming withdrawal.

**Leverage.** Absolute and known. Threats to Eleanor override every other operational priority including self-preservation, contract obligation, and his attachments to Cable, Bob, Al, and Weasel. This is the single largest vulnerability in his file and is also, paradoxically, the single least exploited, because predators competent enough to identify it (Butler, Hydra-Rogers in some readings) tend to die badly afterward in ways that have generated a deterrent reputation. The Butler arc functions, in the longitudinal record, as a public demonstration of what happens to operators who use this vector.

---

### 5. Carmelita Camacho (status: dead; operationally: the unmourned, because unremembered)

**History.** Eleanor's mother. The relationship is brief, the memory of it spotty (Wilson's recollections are inconsistent on whether he loved her, whether he knew her well, whether the relationship was substantial or transactional). Murdered by the Butler.

**Dynamics.** The most painful datum in the Carmelita material is **the absence of grief proportional to the loss**. Wilson did not know Eleanor existed at the time of Carmelita's death; he therefore did not register the death as the destruction of a family. The retroactive grief, once Eleanor is discovered, is partial: he mourns the mother-of-his-child more than the woman, because the woman is mostly unrecoverable to him. He does not know whether his patchy memory is the cancer-tissue's neurological noise (see §2, Medical), a dissociative protection, or simply that the relationship did not encode deeply. He cannot tell. *No one can.* This is the diagnostically central feature of the Carmelita relationship: it is the case study in which his organic, dissociative, and characterological deficits become indistinguishable from one another.

**Trust/safety.** Posthumously moot. In life, the relationship was too brief to characterize.

**Failure mode.** The Carmelita material is the prototype of a recurring class of Wilson-relationships: **people he has hurt or failed by not encoding them**. The failure is not betrayal but absence-of-record. He cannot apologize for what he does not remember, and he cannot remember what his neurology and his defenses jointly will not let him.

**Leverage.** Low and decreasing. The Butler used Carmelita as leverage and the leverage produced his own destruction; subsequent operators have not revisited the vector.

---

### 6. The Butler's Victims (status: dead; operationally: the catalog of erased attachments)

**History.** During the Posehn/Duggan run's *Original Sins* and adjacent arcs, Wilson learns that the Butler — a Weapon X-adjacent operator — has spent years systematically identifying everyone Wilson has formed an attachment to, abducting them, erasing Wilson's memory of them, and either killing them or warehousing them for re-use. The number is **uncountable**. Wilson, on receiving the file, cannot verify any individual case because the erasure was effective. Carmelita is one entry; there are dozens or more.

**Dynamics.** This arc is, in the longitudinal record, the moment Wilson's distrust of his own memory becomes externally validated. He had always behaved as though his attachments were doomed and his memory unreliable; he discovered that an enemy had been **actively producing the conditions** he had assumed were merely his curse. The discovery produced, in the published record, the closest thing to a breakdown the character has sustained on-page — and characteristically he metabolized it through hyper-violence and contract escalation rather than through any consolidatable grief.

**Trust/safety.** The Butler material destroyed his trust in his own internal record. Post-Butler, Wilson's confabulations about his past intensify, not because he is more dishonest but because he now has external evidence that the past he reports may be a constructed scaffold over a deliberate void.

**Failure mode and leverage.** The vector is closed (the Butler is dead) but the **template** is open: any operator who can credibly threaten further erasures, or who can present Wilson with a "found" prior attachment he cannot verify or refute, can replicate the destabilization. This file recommends that no UATU-adjacent actor ever present Wilson with a claimed recovered memory of a prior relationship, regardless of evidentiary basis. The cost-benefit is unfavorable in every scenario.

---

### 7. The Constructed Family: Blind Al (status: living; operationally: the captive-mother that became the chosen mother)

**History.** Althea, an elderly blind woman, originally **abducted by Wilson** in the Kelly run and kept in his apartment under conditions framed as captivity, with the elaborate "Box" punishment, the running cruelty-as-comedy bits, and the genuine domestic codependency layered over them. Over decades of publication she has transitioned, by mutual unspoken consent, from captive to roommate to friend to functional mother. She has had multiple opportunities to leave and has not used them; he has had multiple opportunities to end the arrangement and has not used them either.

**Dynamics.** Al is the **load-bearing maternal surrogate** in his life and the relationship's origin in captivity is the diagnostic key to his entire attachment architecture: he literally could not form a mother-bond except by removing the mother's exit. Her blindness is also load-bearing — she cannot see his face, which removes the disfigurement variable from the relationship entirely and reproduces the only condition under which his idealized maternal object can exist (cf. §1: a mother who cannot turn away because she cannot see).

The cruelty register of their banter (Box, the booby-traps, the verbal abuse in both directions) is **mutually regulating**. Al gives as good as she gets; she is one of the very few people who can match his verbal aggression without producing the rupture-or-attachment binary his other relationships fall into. The cruelty is a stable medium they have agreed to swim in because it is the only one that does not require either of them to be vulnerable in a register they cannot sustain.

**Trust/safety.** Maximal, after decades. She has passed the test more thoroughly than anyone else in the file. He trusts her to be there, to mock him, to not pity him, and to not see him — in both senses.

**Failure mode.** Her age. She is the most age-vulnerable of his major attachments and her eventual death will, on the projection this file can make from the recorded grief-pattern, produce the single most destabilizing loss of his adult life. The Bea Arthur fixation in the Way run was a rehearsal for this; the actual event will not be survivable in the form he currently occupies, and the post-loss Wilson will be a different operational profile than the pre-loss one.

**Leverage.** High in principle, low in practice — Al is hard to threaten (already blind, already old, already living with the most dangerous man in three boroughs) and harder to leverage without triggering the children-at-risk-class response that overrides Wilson's other priorities. The maternal coding of the threat is its own deterrent.

---

### 8. The Dead Who Will Not Stay Dead: Death Herself (status: cosmic abstract; operationally: the bride he cannot marry)

**History.** Wilson's romantic and libidinal investment in the personification of Death is canonical (Way run especially; recurring across Thanos-adjacent material). His rivalry with Thanos over her affection is comedic in register and **entirely serious in content**: he loves the only entity who could end his condition, and Thanos has cursed him to deathlessness specifically to prevent the union.

**Dynamics.** This is the cleanest possible expression of his core libidinal pattern — the object is selected for impossibility. Death cannot reject him (she takes everyone eventually). Death cannot disfigure him (she is beyond the disfigurement frame). Death cannot abandon him (she is the destination, not the leaver). The relationship satisfies the unattainable-maternal template, the suicidal-ideation channel, and the romantic-attachment channel simultaneously, in a single object that biology forbids him to reach.

**Trust/safety.** He trusts Death absolutely and she has, in his frame, kept faith — she has tried to come for him many times and has been thwarted by his biology and Thanos's curse, not by her refusal. The relationship is the only one in his file that is **structurally faithful** on both sides.

**Failure mode.** The relationship cannot be consummated and he cannot stop pursuing it. The reckless-self-endangerment pattern across all runs is, at one register, an ongoing courtship of this object. He will continue this courtship for as long as he is alive, which is, by current biology, indefinitely.

**Leverage.** None usable by hostile operators (Thanos has already used the maximum-strength version: deathlessness). The relationship is exploited not by outsiders but by Wilson himself, as the libidinal channel that motivates the suicidal-but-non-consummatable behavior.

---

### Synthesis of the Family/Origin Map

The biological family is a void with stories drawn over it. The constructed family is a small, intensely tested set: one blind mother (Al), one abs


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# UATU ANALYSIS FILE: WADE WINSTON WILSON ("DEADPOOL")
## Section 7 — Relationships II: Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

> *Methodological note.* The subject's relational record is unusually difficult to map because (a) he routinely lies about who he knows and how well, (b) he stages public ruptures with people he is privately devoted to, and (c) the contradictory autobiographies described in the History section extend to his account of who his friends are. This section therefore relies on **behavioral evidence over self-report**: who he calls when bleeding out, whose calls he picks up, whose name he refuses to put in a punchline, and whose body he has carried away from a fire. By that standard the working roster is small — roughly seven durable bonds, three or four mentor/peer relationships, and a much longer tail of operational associates the file logs but does not classify as chosen family.

---

### 7.1 — AL ("BLIND AL") / Althea

**Status:** Primary attachment figure. Functionally mother, longest-standing fixed relationship in the subject's life outside of Weasel. Effectively co-resident across the entirety of the Kelly run and intermittently thereafter through the present period.

**History.** The relationship begins in the Kelly era as a **captive-attachment of his manufacture** — Wilson, post-Hospice, locks an elderly blind woman into his apartment and refuses to let her leave. The framing is sitcom; the conduct, in any other case file, would be felony unlawful restraint of a vulnerable adult. She remains, in subject's own internal accounting, "the prisoner," and the apartment contains a "Box" — a sensory-deprivation closet — for her punishment. This is not background color; it is the *founding act* of the only stable home he has ever held.
