Al's prior life (revealed slowly across Kelly and Simone, then deepened by Bunn and Duggan) involves intelligence-adjacent work, a husband and child lost, a level of personal hardness fully comparable to his own, and a steady refusal to be afraid of him. She stayed when she could have escaped; the lock was decorative within months.

**Dynamics.** The bond runs on a precisely calibrated **bilateral cruelty** — she insults him with surgical precision about the disfigurement, the parentage, the failures, the smell; he stages elaborate humiliations, threatens the Box, performs eviction. Underneath: she is the only person in the file who has watched him cry without making him pay for it afterward, and the only person whose silence he can tolerate for hours at a time. He cooks for her (badly), reads aloud to her (the food and reading are documented across multiple runs), maintains the apartment to her standards, and routes income through her when his own banking is compromised. She, for her part, has held intelligence on him that she has never sold, including the location of his daughter during the custody period.

**Evolution.** Initial phase (Kelly): jailer/jailed with reversed valences — she is the structurally captive one but operationally the regulating adult, parenting an adult patient. Middle phase (Simone, Way, early Posehn/Duggan): the conceit of captivity erodes; she comes and goes, and her presence becomes the index of whether he has a home base or is in dispersal. Late phase (Duggan, Kelly, Kibblesmith): she is openly the matriarch of his small circle, occasionally weaponized (intel work, decoy ops), occasionally protected (relocations during the Butler arc, security details he funds and conceals from her).

**Trust / safety.** Highest in file. She has near-total veto over his immediate behavior when present — a sentence from her will stop a tirade he would not stop for Cable or Captain America. Behavioral tell: in her apartment he sits down. He does not sit down anywhere else for long.

**Failure mode.** Two. (1) When she is hurt or threatened he loses the humor defense entirely and reverts to flat, lethal affect — the *most dangerous* state he enters in the entire record, more so than combat-rage, because it is silent. (2) He cannot accept her dying. The healing factor makes him constitutionally incapable of metabolizing the death of a normal-lifespan attachment figure; he has pre-grieved her repeatedly across the run, with each rehearsal triggering a multi-issue dissociative spiral.

**Leverage.** Anyone who locates her, harms her, or convincingly threatens her redirects his entire operational capacity. The Butler arc is the demonstration case. She is also the lever he uses on himself — the one person whose disappointment functions as a brake.

---

### 7.2 — WEASEL (Jack Hammer)

**Status:** Operational confidant; longest continuous non-domestic relationship; the only person he calls "friend" without the word collapsing into a joke mid-sentence — though the joke usually arrives a beat later anyway.

**History.** Established Kelly era; weapons-and-tech contractor, bar-owner across multiple iterations of the Hellhouse / Sister Margaret's bar concept; chronically in arrears, chronically in danger because of Wilson's proximity. The two appear to have met during the early mercenary period, pre-Vanessa, pre-Weapon X — Weasel is one of the few continuities that bridges the cancer line.

**Dynamics.** The relationship is structured as a **mutual extortion that has rounded into love**. Weasel supplies gear, intel, fenced ordnance, the bar as a meet, occasional hacking; Wilson supplies cash, protection, and the gravitational chaos that both ruins and stocks Weasel's establishments. They insult each other with the fluency of brothers; Weasel is one of the very few people permitted to mock the face directly to it, and his mockery is the only mockery the subject does not pay back with violence — only with reciprocal mockery, which is the relational currency they have agreed on.

**Evolution.** Early: vendor-and-client with affection. Middle (Way, Posehn/Duggan): Weasel is occasionally betrayed — sold out, accidentally maimed, used as bait — and forgives, each forgiveness deepening Wilson's dependence and guilt. The Posehn/Duggan run contains the most telling pattern: Weasel is genuinely afraid of him for the first time and Wilson registers this, modifies behavior, apologizes (obliquely), and *changes* — a vanishingly rare adaptive sequence in the file. Later runs show Weasel running infrastructure (the Mercs for Money back-office, payment laundering for the family man period, the bar as halfway-house) with Wilson visibly trying not to break him.

**Trust / safety.** Tier-one operationally; tier-two emotionally (below Al, slightly above Cable in immediacy if not in depth). Weasel will hear things from him that Cable will not, because Weasel will not try to fix them.

**Failure mode.** Weasel breaks under sustained existential pressure — he will fold, run, snitch — and Wilson knows this and **factors it in without resentment**, which is itself remarkable. The relationship survives Weasel's predictable failures because Wilson has pre-discounted them. The asymmetric danger runs the other way: Wilson's reliability is the variable; Weasel has been left holding the bag for years at a stretch.

**Leverage.** Capture Weasel and Wilson will negotiate; harm Weasel and Wilson will hunt without humor; kill Weasel and the file projects a multi-month dissociative campaign of disproportionate retribution followed by a long, bleak silence.

---

### 7.3 — NATHAN SUMMERS ("CABLE")

**Status:** Peer, conscience-by-proxy, longest *adversarial-collaborative* relationship in the file. The most important male attachment.

**History.** Documented from Nicieza's mid-90s *Cable & Deadpool* through to present; began as antagonism, formalized as the *Cable & Deadpool* run (Nicieza, ~50 issues) — the longest sustained two-hander in either character's record — and has recurred as a default pairing through every subsequent era. Time-displaced messianic operator; militant moralist; physically and tactically Wilson's superior in most dimensions and his match in stubbornness.

**Dynamics.** The structure is the **straight-man/jester dyad** weaponized into something genuinely therapeutic for the subject. Cable does not laugh at his bits, does not flinch from the face, does not negotiate boundaries — he simply enforces them by being inarguable. Wilson tests Cable's tolerance constantly and Cable absorbs the testing the way a wall absorbs a thrown bottle. Crucially, Cable has been **inside Wilson's head** (telepathic contact, neural link arcs in *Cable & Deadpool*), survived the experience, and did not flee — a fact the subject does not articulate but on which the relationship is structurally founded. Someone has seen the inside and stayed.

**Evolution.** Antagonism → forced partnership (Providence arc) → ideological sparring with operational interdependence → grudging fraternity → the present-day default in which Cable is the only person to whom Wilson reliably reports actual emotional information, usually couched as a complaint about Cable.

**Trust / safety.** Cable is trusted with the *truth of operational state* — Wilson will not bullshit him about how badly he is hurt, what he has done, who he is afraid of. He is not, however, trusted with the *truth of feeling*; that goes to Al, and occasionally Bob, and almost no one else.

**Failure mode.** Cable's moralism periodically demands Wilson rise to a standard he cannot sustain. The collapses from those heights are the source of several of the most severe dissociative episodes in the record (notably post-Hydra-Rogers/Coulson). Cable also reliably *leaves* — time-jumps, missions, exiles — and each departure rehearses the abandonment template; Wilson manages this by pre-narrating Cable's exits as betrayals he predicted, deflating the wound to ironic anticipation.

**Leverage.** Cable in danger overrides ordinary operational logic. Cable in moral disgust is the single most stabilizing/regulating force in the record short of Al — and the single most destructive when withdrawn.

---

### 7.4 — BOB, AGENT OF HYDRA (Robert Dobalina)

**Status:** Dependent, mascot, surrogate-younger-brother; tier-one emotional bond camouflaged as joke relationship.

**History.** Posehn-era continuity (originated Way run, *Deadpool* vol. 4, 2008); a low-grade HYDRA file clerk press-ganged into field work, scooped up by Wilson in a raid, never returned. Married, kids, chronic anxiety, no combat aptitude, no business in the field.

**Dynamics.** Bob is the **only person in the file whom Wilson actively protects without being asked**, and the protection is delivered under cover of contempt. He calls Bob a coward, a pet, a hostage, a liability; he also positions himself between Bob and incoming fire with reflexive consistency. Bob is one of the very few people Wilson allows to *witness him bored, tired, or domestically annoyed* — the unguarded baseline states he hides from everyone else.

**Evolution.** Bob's significance has grown quietly across runs. He is now the working-class everyman against whom the subject measures his own distance from ordinary life — the man with the wife and kids and the limited skill set whom the subject defends partly as projection of the life he cannot have. The relationship is one of the cleanest test-cases for **reaction formation**: the meanness on the surface is exactly proportional to the tenderness underneath.

**Trust / safety.** Bob is safe in the specific sense that he is too low-stakes to threaten. He cannot judge, cannot leave (he depends on Wilson for survival), cannot demand emotional reciprocity beyond the comfortable register of complaint and reassurance. This is precisely why the bond is sustainable: it satisfies *be needed without being known* in pure form.

**Failure mode.** If Bob ever became genuinely competent or independent, the relational structure would collapse; the subject would lose the role and regress. Conversely, the death of Bob — which has been threatened in multiple arcs — would inflict damage disproportionate to the public register of the relationship, because Bob is the rehearsal-attachment Wilson uses to practice fatherhood when Eleanor is out of reach.

**Leverage.** Threats against Bob's family (wife Allison, children) are the cleanest acute lever short of Al or Eleanor.

---

### 7.5 — OUTLAW (Inez Temple) and SANDI BRANDENBERG

**Status:** Chosen-family female peer unit. Treated jointly here because in the subject's behavioral patterning they function as a coupled regulating presence.

**History.** Simone era (*Agent X*, *Deadpool/GLI*) onward. Outlaw — Texan mercenary, super-strong, an operational equal he cannot intimidate; Sandi — civilian-side office manager who keeps the merc work organized, dated Weasel, then Outlaw. The two women jointly anchored what Simone's run established as the most psychologically stable period in the entire file.

**Dynamics.** With Outlaw the subject demonstrates **non-romantic competent affect regulation with a woman who could plausibly be a romantic object** — which is, given the Vanessa/Siryn/Shiklah pattern, diagnostically extraordinary. She is attractive to him, attracted to him at points, and the relationship has been kept platonic largely by mutual decision; the absence of consummation has *preserved* rather than thwarted the bond. With Sandi he is courtly, careful, almost formal — she is one of perhaps three women in the file whom he has never propositioned or insulted about her body.

**Evolution.** The Simone-era stabilization gave way to long stretches of off-screen presence, with the pair recurring at moments of crisis (the Mercs for Money managerial chaos, post-Eleanor custody loss) as a kind of *reset condition* — Wilson returning to their orbit when he needs to be reminded he can behave.

**Trust / safety.** High in a specific, narrow band: he trusts them with **his daily life**, not his deep history. They are the people he can have lunch with.

**Failure mode.** Both have suffered for proximity to him — Sandi most notoriously, kidnapped and used as leverage more than once. The subject responds with disproportionate violence followed by guilt-driven withdrawal; the cycle of *closeness → harm to her → flight → return* has played out repeatedly with Sandi specifically.

**Leverage.** Sandi is grievously exploitable; Outlaw less so (she fights back competently). Threats to either elicit the silent-lethal-affect state previously noted with Al.

---

### 7.6 — ELLIE CAMACHO (NYPD liaison, later domestic partner)

**Status:** Late-period attempt at peer-romantic chosen family with a sober adult. Outcome: characteristic.

**History.** Duggan-era; police detective drawn in through casework, eventually cohabitating; one of the very few attempts in the file to construct a *normal* domestic relationship outside the demimonde.

**Dynamics.** With Ellie the subject behaves better than he is — and the strain shows. He suppresses tics, manages the face, comes home on time, attempts the rituals of partnership (meals, plans, in-laws). She, for her part, refused infantilizing him and refused being protected from his world, which is the precondition any partner of his must meet.

**Evolution.** Brief stabilization → environmental contamination (his work bleeding into her life) → the relationship's eventual erosion in the patterned manner: she sees enough to recalibrate, he reads the recalibration as imminent rejection, accelerates his own withdrawal to control the timing.

**Trust / safety.** Notable mostly for what it reveals: he can perform an ordinary partner role for finite intervals. The performance is not fake but is not sustainable; the affect-regulation cost is too high.

**Failure mode.** Classic approach-and-sabotage. Of forensic interest is that **with Ellie the sabotage was passive** — drift, omission, withdrawal — rather than the active staged ruptures of earlier relationships, suggesting a marginal maturation in the failure pattern itself.

**Leverage.** Lower than the major attachments because the relationship is no longer active, but the residue (he checks on her, indirectly) is exploitable to anyone patient enough to monitor.

---

### 7.7 — PRESTON (Emily Preston, SHIELD)

**Status:** Mentor-coded adult professional ally; later, post-trauma, a literal voice in his head.

**History.** Posehn/Duggan era; SHIELD agent assigned as handler, became friend, was catastrophically injured, with her consciousness transferred into Wilson's body for an extended period — a literalization of *being inhabited by a trusted adult* that the file treats as one of the most psychologically generative arcs in the entire run.

**Dynamics.** Preston is the rare authority figure who treats him as a colleague rather than a project. She corrects without contempt, praises without manipulation, and — uniquely — survived being *inside his cognition* without being damaged by what she saw there. The cohabitation phase produced documented improvement in his behavioral baseline: she was the internal voice that disagreed with the worst boxes, in real time, with the authority of an actual person rather than a self-state.

**Evolution.** Field partnership → consciousness-cohabitation → restoration to her own body → ongoing operational and personal alliance. The post-restoration relationship is marked by an unusual *grief at restoration* — he missed her presence as an internal companion, a feeling he has not articulated but that the behavioral record (visits, gifts, protective surveillance of her family) makes plain.

**Trust / safety.** Very high. Preston has touched the inside and is one of two people (with Cable) for whom the file finds no instance of him lying about operational state.

**Failure mode.** Preston has a family; the family is the leverage. Wilson knows this and has, on at least one occasion, distanced himself from her *to protect her exposure* — a mature defensive move he is otherwise rarely capable of.

**Leverage.** Same as all the bonds — endanger her, redirect him absolutely. Particularly potent because she is one of the few attachments he has earned cleanly, without coercion or accident, and would mourn without the deflective machinery available for the older bonds.

---

### 7.8 — THE MERCS FOR MONEY (managed dependents: Solo, Stingray, Foolkiller, Slapstick, Terror, Madcap-as-anti-case)

**Status:** Aggregate dependents organized as a business; functionally a **managed family of damaged men** the subject collected and tried to make legitimate.

**History.** Duggan-era enterprise: subject leverages a brief period of cultural ascendancy (Avengers, public profile) into capital and brands a mercenary collective under his management. The roster is composed of operators who, individually, mirror facets of his own pathology — Solo (the lone-wolf righteous-killer he won't let himself be), Foolkiller (the moralism gone septic he is in danger of becoming), Stingray (the straight arrow he uses as a sanity reference), Slapstick (the dissociative humor defense in pure form), Terror (the corpse-trade absurdism that makes his own life feel coherent), and the negative case of Madcap.

**Dynamics.** The arrangement is the **captive-attachment pattern scaled to organizational form**. He pays them, owns the contracts, controls the exits, presents himself as the boss while functioning as the most chaotic operator on the roster. The structure satisfies *be needed without being known* at industrial scale: he can supply paychecks, intel, and gallows-camaraderie without ever sitting down with any one of them long enough to be mirrored.

**Evolution.** Brief functional period → predictable managerial collapse (cash flow, client betrayal, internal feuds, his own absences) → dissolution with residual loyalties to specific members. The arc reads as a rehearsal of fatherhood-by-other-means during the period of Eleanor's removal.

**Trust / safety.** Low across the board with high variance per member. Stingray is trusted; Foolkiller is feared; Solo is respected; Slapstick is humored; Terror is treated with the deference of one chronic-illness sufferer for another.

**Failure mode.** The organization's collapse was overdetermined: he cannot delegate, cannot tolerate competence in subordinates that approaches his own, and cannot sustain the affect regulation required to manage adults across pay periods.

**Leverage.** Limited per individual; the network as a whole is a soft lever — embarrass the brand, threaten the operation, and he becomes accessible through commercial channels he would otherwise avoid.

---

### 7.9 — MADCAP

**Status:** The negative attachment — a peer in pathology whose proximity is *toxic to recovery*; treated separately from the Mercs because the dynamic is structurally different.

**History.** Way / Duggan eras; another regenerating, reality-bending casualty with a worse moral structure and a similar metabolism for suffering. Briefly an inner voice. Briefly a partner. Repeatedly a problem.

**Dynamics.** Madcap is **what the subject would be without the residual ethic**. The relationship therefore functions as a mirror Wilson cannot bear to look at for long. Periods of cohabitation/partnership produce behavioral deterioration in the subject; periods of opposition produce clarification.

**Trust / safety.** None and none. The relationship persists not from trust but from the inability of either party to die.

**Failure mode.** Whenever Wilson lets Madcap close — usually under the rationalization that *no one else gets it* — the consequences are catastrophic, including to third parties. The subject is aware of this and lets it happen anyway, periodically, because the recognition Madcap supplies (*I understand what your body is like*) is so rare he will pay a heavy price for it.

**Leverage.** A hostile operator who controls or counterfeits Madcap can route Wilson into self-destructive choices via the lure of being-understood.

---

### 7.10 — DR. KILLEBREW

**Status:** Posthumous mentor; the corrupted father-figure he has not been able to bury.

**History.** Hospice physician; co-author of the torture; also the only adult in that environment who exhibited intermittent paternal regard. Killed during the Hospice break (per Kelly), but the relational residue is permanent.

**Dynamics.** The most diagnostically interesting figure in the file. Killebrew is the **template of conditional care** — kindness delivered alongside atrocity — which has shaped every subsequent authority relationship. Wilson references him obliquely across runs, dreams of him, occasionally hallucinates him; the boxes contain a recognizable Killebrew-coded register (clinical, faintly fond, ethically compromised).

**Evolution.** From operative trauma figure → ghost-mentor → internalized critic that occasionally speaks in his head with the cadence of a doctor delivering bad news kindly.

**Trust / safety.** N/A; the figure is internal.

**Failure mode.** Any external figure who mimics the Killebrew register — *clinical care language paired with cruelty* — triggers regression and dangerous compliance. This is the **largest exploitable surface in the entire file**, demonstrated by Ajax (the same template, sharper), Butler (the same template, weaponized), and the Hydra-Rogers manipulation (institutional version).

**Leverage.** Anyone who can ventriloquize a doctor's


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# RELATIONSHIPS III — RIVALS, ENEMIES & LOVERS

*Compiled from longitudinal observation across the published record (Nicieza, Kelly, Simone, Way, Posehn/Duggan, Bunn, Duggan, Kelly redux, Kibblesmith, Adams) and cross-checked against operational telemetry where available. Each entry follows a fixed schema: HISTORY → DYNAMICS → EVOLUTION → TRUST/SAFETY → FAILURE MODE → LEVERAGE. Note that for Subject WILSON, the categorical lines between rival, enemy, and lover are unusually porous; entries are filed by predominant operational valence and cross-referenced where necessary.*

---

## I. RIVALS

These are the figures Subject orbits without resolution: relationships defined by an unconcluded competitive itch rather than the kill-or-be-killed structure of true enmity. The rivalry serves the same regulatory function as the humor — it keeps affect moving without ever requiring it to land.

### I.1 — TAKEO ŌKAMI / TASKMASTER (Anthony "Tony" Masters)

**History.** Earliest documented overlap in the Nicieza-era underworld circuit, late 1990s; Taskmaster's photographic-reflex mimicry initially marks Subject as an instructive case (the only target he cannot copy because there is no underlying movement-grammar to copy — Subject's combat style is, by Taskmaster's own report, "broken on purpose"). Repeated contractual collisions (Initiative training cadre arc; *Deadpool* vol. 4 cameos; *Agent X*–era brushes). Never a sustained kill-feud; never a partnership.

**Dynamics.** Mirror-and-anti-mirror. Taskmaster is what Subject would be if his disorganization were converted into a clean professional asset — affectless, procedural, technically supreme. Subject reads Taskmaster as the version of himself that completed the program, and treats him with a brittle, half-flirty deference that reads as envy laundered through banter. Taskmaster, conversely, treats Subject as the only opponent whose pattern he cannot internalize — an unteachable irritation.

**Evolution.** Has softened over two decades from sporadic contracted antagonism to a kind of guild collegiality. They have shared bars (Hellhouse, the Marrakesh circuit), declined to fulfill contracts on one another, and on at least two occasions tag-teamed third parties.

**Trust/Safety.** Moderate — bounded by mutual-professional reciprocity. Neither will warn the other; neither will betray the other to a third party for less than three times the going rate. This is, in mercenary terms, friendship.

**Failure mode.** A contract structured to make the betrayal economically rational. Both men know this; both have priced it in.

**Leverage Subject has on Taskmaster:** the unteachable-style problem makes Subject the one opponent Taskmaster cannot war-game in advance.
**Leverage Taskmaster has on Subject:** he has seen Subject fight when not performing for an audience, and can therefore see *through* the spectacle defense — a form of being-known Subject normally cannot tolerate but does, here, because Taskmaster has no interpretive interest.

---

### I.2 — BULLSEYE (Lester)

**History.** Repeated collisions across the Way and Duggan runs; most consequential during the Hand/Osborn-adjacent arcs. The two have attempted to kill each other at least eleven documented times; neither has succeeded; both have come closer than the record acknowledges.

**Dynamics.** True rivalry of register: Bullseye is the **affectless** killer Subject cannot become because Subject cannot stop talking. Bullseye finds Subject's verbal output physiologically offensive (documented in the Way run as a near-stuttering rage response). Subject finds Bullseye's silence intolerable and weaponizes its disturbance by escalating banter until Bullseye breaks discipline. Each is the precise instrument by which the other can be made to lose.

**Evolution.** Less and less ideological over time, more and more ritualized. By the Kibblesmith period, encounters have a worn, almost married quality.

**Trust/Safety.** Zero. Operationally hostile in all theaters.

**Failure mode.** Mutual ambush; the one who breaks discipline first loses. Bullseye is statistically more vulnerable because the irritation surface is wider.

**Leverage.** Subject's voice, weaponized. Bullseye's silence, equally so.

---

### I.3 — WOLVERINE (James Howlett / Logan)

**History.** The donor-recipient relationship is the load-bearing geometry. Subject's healing factor is Wolverine-derived (Department K / Workshop appropriation). Initial encounters were professionally hostile (Wolverine views Subject as the Weapon program's spilled remainder); evolution has been toward a grudging, ugly intimacy.

**Dynamics.** Wolverine is, anatomically, the closest thing Subject has to a parent. He carries the original biology Subject was rewritten *toward*. Subject's behavior in Wolverine's presence is regressive — louder, needier, more provocative, more eager to be hit — and the hit, when delivered, functions as recognition. Wolverine, for his part, finds Subject genuinely upsetting (the unsought reflection: this is what the program does when it works wrong), but has, on multiple documented occasions, refused to finish him.

**Evolution.** From "I will kill you on sight" (Nicieza-era postures) to "I will skin you and walk away" (Way era) to a documented late-period willingness to fight alongside Subject and to leave him alive at the end. This is the longest improving arc in Subject's antagonist column.

**Trust/Safety.** Asymmetric. Subject trusts Wolverine with his life (will not die) and with his death (might be merciful). Wolverine does not trust Subject with anything that requires silence.

**Failure mode.** Subject crosses one of Wolverine's red lines (child harm, X-Men endangerment) under contract he cannot break. Wolverine kills him, repeatedly, until the contract collapses; relationship survives this.

**Leverage.** Wolverine has Subject's origin-as-tissue. Subject has Wolverine's guilt about being the origin.

---

### I.4 — CABLE (Nathan Summers)

*Cross-filed: see Relationships II for the primary attachment dossier. Briefly noted here as the rare case where rivalry resolved into bond.*

The Cable relationship began in classical rivalry mode (the Nicieza/Liefeld *Cable & Deadpool* setup: opposite politics, opposite affect, contracted antagonism) and metabolized — through forced proximity, sustained shared crisis, and Cable's anomalous willingness to **endure the testing without retaliating** — into the single most stable bond in Subject's life. Failure mode: Cable's apocalyptic-mission absences read by Subject as abandonment and trigger regressive acting-out, which Cable has learned to absorb. Leverage in both directions is total and uncollected.

---

### I.5 — T-RAY (Tyler Brooks / Thaddeus)

**History.** Joe Kelly run. T-Ray is a sorcerer-mercenary who claims, mid-arc, to be the *actual* Wade Wilson — and that Subject is a body-thief who killed him and took his name. The claim is never definitively falsified in Kelly's run; the writers thereafter have treated it as one of the load-bearing instabilities of the origin file.

**Dynamics.** T-Ray exists to be the figure who weaponizes Subject's deepest structural fear: that the self he performs is not his own, that he is a stolen identity over an unrecoverable original. Every other antagonist threatens the body; T-Ray threatens the name. This is why the relationship is filed under rivalry rather than enmity — the wound T-Ray opens is metaphysical and cannot be closed by killing him.

**Evolution.** Sporadic recurrence. Subject avoids T-Ray more than he hunts him; this is unusual and diagnostically significant.

**Trust/Safety.** None; aversion exceeds threat-rating, which means the aversion is psychological, not tactical.

**Failure mode.** Forced confrontation in a setting that does not permit Subject to clown his way out. T-Ray's leverage scales with the audience's seriousness.

**Leverage.** T-Ray holds — or claims to hold — the canonical biography. Subject holds nothing on T-Ray that compares; this is the only relationship in the file where Subject is structurally outmatched.

---

## II. ENEMIES

These are figures whose relationship to Subject is organized around harm — given, received, or both — and which lacks the recreational shape of rivalry. Several of these entries describe wounds that have not closed.

### II.1 — FRANCIS FANNY / AJAX

**History.** Workshop/Hospice clinician under Killebrew. Subject's primary torturer over the months-to-years of the Weapon X augmentation program. Architect of the betting-pool incident in which Subject was manipulated into killing Worm. Killed Subject ("flatlined" — dumped — revived). The single most important other person in Subject's psychic life, the original template against which every subsequent authority figure is unconsciously measured.

**Dynamics.** Asymmetric obsession. Ajax is, to Subject, what the primal scene is to a classical analytic patient — not a memory but a structuring condition. Ajax's distinctive affective signature (mockery during violence; clinical language for sadistic ends; the cruelty-care fusion) became the template Subject identified-with-the-aggressor on. **Subject's entire combat persona is a Ajax-derivative**: the patter, the casual-cruel running commentary, the use of medical language while inflicting injury. He has been doing impressions of his torturer for thirty diegetic years.

**Evolution.** Ajax is canonically dead — multiple times — and returns. The returns are diegetic, but the structural meaning is that he cannot stay dead because Subject cannot stop reproducing him internally. When Ajax is absent from the page, Subject's behavior toward sadistic-clinician-coded figures (Killebrew in later softening; Butler; a string of doctor-villains) regresses to the Ajax template anyway.

**Trust/Safety.** Total enmity. Ajax is the one figure in the file Subject will pursue without compensation and against operational interest.

**Failure mode.** Subject is, in Ajax's presence, the version of himself who killed Worm. The mockery defense weakens; the boxes get loud; tactical performance degrades. Ajax wins by being present.

**Leverage.** Ajax has the origin of Subject's affective register. Subject has Ajax's own mortality, repeatedly, and the mortality does not stick.

---

### II.2 — DR. EMRYS KILLEBREW

**History.** Director of the Workshop. The "good" doctor to Ajax's bad. Did not torture personally but authored the architecture that permitted it. Reformed in later runs and was, briefly, a peripheral ally before being killed.

**Dynamics.** More structurally damaging than Ajax in some respects because Killebrew represented the **care-coded** authority that betrayed. Ajax was honest about being a torturer; Killebrew was the figure who said "this will help you" while signing off on the help. Subject's destabilization in the presence of legitimacy-offering authorities (Osborn, Hydra-Rogers — see below) traces to Killebrew more than to Ajax.

**Trust/Safety.** Was zero, drifted to ambivalent, ended in a complicated grief Subject has not processed and likely cannot.

**Failure mode.** Subject was, against operational sense, willing to forgive Killebrew. This generosity is dangerous: it is the same circuit that lets him be played by Osborn.

**Leverage.** Posthumous; resides in the unresolved forgiveness.

---

### II.3 — THE BUTLER (Dr. Emrys Killebrew's protégé / Butler proper)

**History.** Posehn/Duggan run. Revealed as the Department-K-adjacent figure who systematically tracked, kidnapped, and murdered Subject's biological family — and who fathered Eleanor's circumstances of abandonment through a chain of manipulations.

**Dynamics.** The discovery that his life had been a designed cruelty — not random misfortune — produced one of the few sustained, undeflected rages in the record. Butler is the Ajax-figure without the seductive cruelty-care fusion: pure instrumental harm. Easier to hate, harder to recover from.

**Evolution.** Resolved by Butler's death, but the resolution did not metabolize. Subject's domestic-fantasy collapse in the late Duggan and Kibblesmith periods can be traced to the Butler revelation: if family can be engineered as a torture instrument, family cannot be a refuge.

**Trust/Safety.** Total enmity, posthumously persisting.

**Failure mode.** None — this is the rare antagonist relationship in which Subject's performance held under existential stress.

**Leverage.** None remaining; Butler's leverage was exhausted with his life.

---

### II.4 — NORMAN OSBORN

**History.** Dark Reign / Way run. Recruited Subject through legitimacy-coded language — *you could be one of us, the world will see you* — and then comprehensively outmaneuvered him.

**Dynamics.** Predator-and-the-largest-exploitable-surface. Osborn read Subject's hunger for the moral community within minutes and weaponized it. This was not a contest. Subject was not outfought; he was *seen* by someone who had no intention of caring what he saw.

**Evolution.** Subject has not, in the intervening decades, become meaningfully less vulnerable to this attack vector. Hydra-Rogers (below) ran a structurally identical play to identical effect.

**Trust/Safety.** Enmity stabilized post-arc; the wound is to self-trust, not to threat-assessment of Osborn specifically.

**Failure mode.** Already executed. The arc is, in operational terms, a worked example of Subject's largest exploitable surface — preserved here for institutional memory.

**Leverage.** Osborn's leverage is the demonstrated technique; any sufficiently skilled flatterer can re-run it. Subject's leverage on Osborn is negligible; he is too legible.

---

### II.5 — STEVE ROGERS / "HYDRA-CAP"

**History.** Original Sin → Civil War II → Secret Empire arc. Subject discovered (Original Sin) that Rogers/SHIELD had directed him toward assassinations under false pretenses, manipulating his hunger for heroic legitimacy. Subject's response was a radicalized push toward heroism — and was then ordered, by the same authority (now compromised by the Hydra-Cap revelation), to kill Phil Coulson. He complied.

**Dynamics.** The deepest legitimacy-betrayal in the record. Where Osborn was a known villain who wore the right clothes, Rogers was the genuine moral exemplar of the universe — and the betrayal therefore could not be metabolized as "I was fooled by a bad actor." Subject killed an innocent man under the orders of the man whose endorsement he had organized his late life around earning. This is the single largest **moral injury** in the file.

**Evolution.** Subject's post-Secret Empire trajectory shows compressed cycle times (isolation → attachment → sabotage runs faster), increased substance pursuit, sharp escalation in metacommentary as defense — all consistent with unresolved moral injury layered over CPTSD.

**Trust/Safety.** Toward Rogers proper: complicated, never restored. Toward authority-as-such: degraded to the point of operational impairment.

**Failure mode.** Recapitulation. Subject will trust the next legitimacy-offering authority and be played again. This is biology, not stupidity.

**Leverage.** Rogers has the largest archived dossier of Subject's vulnerabilities, having weaponized them in real time. Subject has nothing reciprocal.

---

### II.6 — THANOS

**History.** Long-arc rivalry filtered through their shared romantic object: Death personified. Thanos cursed Subject with immortality specifically to keep Death from him; the curse predates and overdetermines the healing factor's behavior at the cosmological level.

**Dynamics.** Thanos is the **father-in-law** in the libidinal triangle Subject has organized his death drive around. The enmity is therefore not personal-violent so much as structural-erotic. Thanos cannot be defeated because his curse is the metaphysical floor of Subject's predicament: he cannot die because a rival lover has arranged it.

**Trust/Safety.** Stable mutual hostility, low operational temperature.

**Failure mode.** Resolution would require Subject to relinquish the Death-object, which is the central organizing fantasy of his suicidal ideation. He will not, and so the enmity is permanent and oddly comfortable.

**Leverage.** Thanos holds the death Subject wants. Subject holds nothing comparable.

---

### II.7 — DEADPOOL (the various selves: Dogpool, Headpool, Kidpool, the Deadpool-Killer-of-the-Marvel-Universe variant, the Deadpool Corps array)

**History.** Multiversal exposure across the *Deadpool Kills* arcs and the Deadpool Corps run.

**Dynamics.** Functionally, Subject's largest enemy is a version of himself with the humor defense stripped out (the Killer variant) and the prosocial drive eliminated. Encountering that variant constitutes a forced confrontation with the question: *what am I when the joke is removed?* The answer — a methodical, joyless murderer of everyone he loves — destabilizes him more than any external threat. Confrontation with self-variants reliably produces the most fourth-wall-shattering defense displays in the record.

**Trust/Safety.** Variable by variant. Generally low; he knows the playbook.

**Failure mode.** The Killer variant wins by refusing to play.

**Leverage.** Mutual and total; self-on-self.

---

## III. LOVERS & INTIMATES

Filed in chronological-emotional order. Note the recurring object-choice pattern flagged in the Psychological section: women selected for impossibility (devourer, ghost, professional rival, departed daughter-mother) such that reciprocity, if it arrives, can be sabotaged before it consolidates.

### III.1 — VANESSA CARLYSLE / COPYCAT

**History.** Pre-Weapon X. Sex worker turned shapeshifter, Subject's first documented sustained romantic attachment. Relationship marked by mutual recognition of damage, the shared protective armor of humor, and a brief but unambiguous love. Ruptured by Subject's diagnosis: rather than tell her, he disappeared into the Workshop. She found out years later; the relationship's reconstitutions across subsequent arcs (Weapon X mini, Nicieza recurrences, X-Force overlaps) have been brief, ambivalent, and eventually terminated by her death — repeatedly, in some continuities permanently.

**Dynamics.** Vanessa is the **pre-trauma object**. The relationship's defining property is that it predates the Hospice, and therefore represents the only attachment formed before the template wound. Subject's behavior toward her is consistently more *naive* than toward any later partner — the schemas have not yet fully closed around her. Hence also why he fled: to preserve the pre-trauma image, he removed himself from it before the trauma could contaminate the relationship. This was protective in its own broken way.

**Evolution.** Repeated cycles of reunion-and-rupture. Each reunion finds them slightly more scarred and slightly less able to recover the early register. Her shapeshifting is, in object-choice terms, perfect for him: she can be anyone, which means she can never be only herself, which means reciprocity is structurally diffused.

**Trust/Safety.** High in absolute terms (he would die for her, and effectively has). Low in operational terms (he cannot stop lying to her, and she has learned to read the lies).

**Failure mode.** He vanishes at the moment of consolidation. Has done so on diagnosis, on reunion, on engagement-equivalents. The pattern is reliable.

**Leverage.** Vanessa holds the only image of him from before. He holds her grief, and the knowledge that she stayed anyway.

---

### III.2 — THERESA CASSIDY / SIRYN

**History.** Kelly run. X-Force-adjacent. The relationship is the cleanest worked example in the file of the **idealize-then-sabotage** schema.

**Dynamics.** Siryn is a young, ethically intact, sincerely affectionate woman who saw past the disfigurement and responded with the steady mirroring Subject cannot tolerate. He pursued her with intensity; once reciprocated, he became unreliable, deflective, performatively cruel, and finally absent. The cruelty was not the pleasure — the rupture was.

**Evolution.** Resolved into a wary affection with no romantic charge remaining. She is one of the small number of people he will return calls from; the relationship survives at the cost of having been emptied of its original valence.

**Trust/Safety.** Currently high, romantically defused.

**Failure mode.** Already executed.

**Leverage.** She holds, intact, a memory of him being briefly sincere. He has organized his subsequent presentations partly to ensure no one else acquires such a memory.

---

### III.3 — OUTLAW (Inez Temple) — friendship-with-shadow-of-romance

*Filed here rather than in friendships because of recurring sub-romantic charge.*

**History.** Simone era onward. Mercenary colleague, Texan, capable, unimpressed.

**Dynamics.** The relationship that **never crosses the line** and is regulating precisely because it does not. Outlaw is the rare woman who reads him without idealizing him and refuses both his deflection and his neediness. She tolerates the performance, names the bullshit when needed, and does not require him to be other than he is.

**Evolution.** Stable; one of the slowly accreting attachments noted in the Personality section as the actual mechanism of his marginal improvement.

**Trust/Safety.** High in both directions.

**Failure mode.** Would activate if he tried to make it romantic; both parties appear to know this.

**Leverage.** Mutual, low-temperature, uncollected.

---

### III.4 — SHIKLAH, QUEEN OF THE UNDERWORLD

**History.** Posehn/Duggan run. Subject was contracted to retrieve her; instead married her. The marriage was, for a stretch of the run, the most stable domestic arrangement in the file.

**Dynamics.** Object choice is diagnostic. Shiklah is a **succubus-class entity** — definitionally a devourer, definitionally not killable by Subject, definitionally not a creature whose love can be invalidated by his disfigurement (she finds it neutral-to-attractive). She is, in formal terms, the only possible partner for him: nothing he is can repel her, nothing he does can destroy her, his death cannot orphan her. He chose, for once, a partner against whom his usual sabotage tools do not work.

**Evolution.** The marriage failed anyway. Not by his standard sabotage but by political


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# POWERS, ABILITIES & THEIR LIMITS

## Wade Winston Wilson — Operational Capabilities Dossier

---

## 1. THE HEALING FACTOR (Primary Anomaly)

### Mechanism

The factor is a derivative — not a copy — of James Howlett's mutant regenerative trait, isolated by Department K's Workshop and forcibly induced in a host (Wilson) whose tissue was already saturated with metastatic, multifocal carcinoma. The graft does not displace the cancer; it competes with it. Wilson's regeneration runs at a rate calibrated to *outpace* uncontrolled malignant mitosis, which means the steady-state baseline of his body is **cancer-saturated tissue being continuously overwritten by cancer-saturated tissue being continuously overwritten**, in perpetuity. The visible disfigurement — the scar-tumor lattice that covers his entire integument — is not a failure mode. It is the cure operating in real time. Every square centimeter of him is what successful treatment looks like when the disease is also the patient.

This distinguishes him operationally from Howlett, whose factor restores a stable somatic template; Wilson has **no stable template**. His body regenerates *toward whatever pattern the underlying genome is currently expressing*, which is itself in flux due to the unceasing mutational pressure of the malignancy. Limb regrowth therefore reliably produces a functional limb but not necessarily an identical one. Continuity-of-self at the cellular level is, for him, a polite fiction.

### Documented Capability Envelope

- **Tissue regeneration**: severed limbs reattach by proximity or regrow de novo, observable within hours to days depending on mass. Fingers in minutes; arms in roughly a day; whole torso reconstitution documented (Posehn/Duggan, *Deadpool* vol. 3) at the scale of weeks.
- **Decapitation survival**: head and body both remain conscious for extended intervals while separated. Verbal output from the severed head has been logged across multiple incidents (mainline, *Deadpool Kills the Marvel Universe*, the Hydra Bob arc). Reattachment is non-trivial — generally requires the original head or a sufficient cranial substrate; substitution events (skull replacements, transplanted heads) have been forced under duress and stabilized.
- **Incineration and dispersal recovery**: regrowth from very small surviving tissue mass is documented but slow and energetically catastrophic. The lower bound has never been firmly established; writers have tested it without resolving it.
- **Toxin and pathogen immunity**: broad-spectrum. Defeats most known biochemical agents at metabolization rates that render dosing meaningless. Notable exceptions: **carbonadium** poisoning (Omega Red arc) genuinely suppressed the factor; certain magical/cosmic poisons bypass it; cancer cells from other hosts do not, because his system is already saturated.
- **Senescence arrest**: subjective aging is dramatically attenuated. He is chronologically well past the age at which an untreated terminal patient would have died; biological-aging markers are not interpretable on his tissue.
- **Telepathic resistance**: the chaotic neural substrate (see Medical) produces an aversive signal to telepathic probes. Frost, Xavier, Cable, and Psylocke have all logged the experience as painful, disorienting, or simply uninterpretable. He is not telepathy-proof; he is telepathy-*expensive*, which is functionally proof against any telepath unwilling to pay.

### Limits

- **Pain is not inhibited.** The factor regenerates nociceptors faithfully and on schedule. Subject experiences the full somatic signal of every injury, including the regrowth itself, which is reported (when he is willing to report) as worse than the original wound.
- **Energy cost.** Regeneration is metabolically ferocious. Caloric requirements are documented at multiples of human baseline; he eats voraciously and constantly when uninjured and ravenously after major reconstitution. Starvation will slow the factor before it stops it.
- **Soft cap on speed.** He is not Howlett-fast. The factor must do extra work because it is also containing the cancer. Cuts close in minutes rather than seconds; major tissue takes hours; the rate is reliably outpaced by sustained high-rate trauma (sufficient sustained kinetic input keeps him down, which is why heavy combatants — Hulk, Juggernaut — can functionally take him out of a fight without killing him).
- **Carbonadium, magic, certain cosmic-grade phenomena** suppress or bypass the factor.
- **It cannot cure the cancer.** Stopping the factor releases the disease, instantly. Any "cure" pathway is therefore also a death pathway, which is one of the structural cruelties of his condition and one of the operational threats that recurs (Killebrew's work, the Wilson-cure-arc-of-the-month across runs).
- **It cannot stop processing him.** Sleep, anesthesia, and stillness are all aversive because the factor is loudest when nothing else is happening. The body never offers him a quiet moment.

### Growth Over Time

The factor has not appreciably *strengthened* across the published record — it is not a muscle he trains — but it has been observed adapting. Documented increases in resilience after specific catastrophic events (full-body skinning, dispersal-class events) suggest a learning component: tissue that has been destroyed once is reconstituted slightly faster the next time. This is not stated as canon doctrine; it is a pattern visible in the longitudinal record. He has also, across the run, learned what the factor *can* survive, which has expanded his operational envelope far more than the factor itself has expanded.

### Symptom-as-Signature

The factor is the perfect somatic instantiation of his psychology. It will not let him die; he will not let himself feel. It overwrites his own substrate continuously; he overwrites his own autobiography continuously. The cure produces the disfigurement that produces the social isolation that his personality was already constructed around — a closed loop in which **biology and character agree on the verdict**. Every cell of him is a small re-staging of the Hospice: torture that does not end, with survival as the punishment.

---

## 2. COMBAT — UNARMED, BLADED, FIREARM

### Substrate of Skill

Pre-Weapon X, the record places him in U.S. Special Forces (washout — discharged for insubordination, with implied psychiatric concerns), followed by an apprenticeship as a low-tier contract operator working Tangier, the Balkans, Hong Kong, and the wider grey-market mercenary circuit. By the time of his Department K intake, he is a competent but unexceptional shooter and knife-man — a journeyman.

Post-factor, two changes restructure his combat profile:

1. **He no longer has to survive the exchange.** Defensive technique becomes optional. Trades that any other operator would refuse — accepting a knife to plant his own, taking a center-mass round to close distance, jumping into rotor blades to clear a flight deck — are routinely on his menu.
2. **The neural substrate is permanently noisy.** This destroys some forms of skill (long-horizon planning, fine-motor stability under stillness) and dramatically enhances others (improvisation, pattern recognition under chaos, response time in environments his nervous system reads as normal).

### Current Envelope

- **Marksmanship**: pistol and SMG work at the top operator tier; rifle work at high-operator level. Trick-shot capability (around corners via ricochet, through targets to other targets, etc.) is documented routinely and is not bravado — he genuinely calculates these on the fly. Loadout typically Desert Eagles or comparable large-bore sidearms (the over-caliber choice is character-revealing: noise, recoil, theatrical impact value over efficiency).
- **Bladework**: katanas are signature, but he is functionally weapon-agnostic — kukris, tantos, machetes, throwing knives, improvised edges. The two-sword style is loose, mobile, and pressure-forward; it relies on his ability to absorb the trade rather than on classical evasion. He has trained with multiple sword masters across the record (informally with Logan, more formally during Japanese arcs); his form is technically dirty but functionally devastating because **no one else in the engagement can fight on his trade-economics**.
- **Hand-to-hand**: an eclectic synthesis — military combatives base, judo throws, capoeira-flavored kicking, jiu-jitsu ground game when needed, a great deal of dirty boxing and improvised environmental use. Sparring footage (Cable training arcs, X-Force) shows him reading at the high end of the Marvel street-tier; he can hold rounds with Captain America for limited durations and has gone to draw or near-draw with Bullseye, Taskmaster (briefly — see below), and Wolverine (functional draw, because neither can finish the other).
- **Athletic baseline**: superhuman reflex and agility on the order of low-tier enhanced humans; strength at top-human; endurance functionally infinite within caloric supply.
- **Acrobatics, parkour, building traversal**: high. He moves through urban environments at a tempo that compresses approach and engagement into a single phase.

### The Taskmaster Note

Taskmaster's photographic-reflex copying capability has been canonically defeated by Wilson on multiple occasions. The mechanism (per Bunn, Way, and others) is that Wilson's combat movement is genuinely unpredictable — not because he plans it that way but because *he does not plan it*. He is improvising at a tempo and from a place of dissociative looseness that produces motion sequences without antecedent muscle-memory grammar. Taskmaster copies form; Wilson is form-incoherent. This is a **direct functional payoff of the psychological disorganization** — his disorder is one of the few combat advantages that is unduplicatable by training.

### Growth Over Time

The trajectory shows escalating tactical sophistication paired with stable or *declining* technical discipline. Early Kelly-era Wilson is sloppier and more reliant on the factor; mid-Way Wilson is at peak technical proficiency (the Avengers/Osborn arcs); Posehn/Duggan Wilson is the most tactically mature (he uses team structures, leverages others' powers, plans approach phases); late-period Wilson shows occasional regression as the psychological state worsens but retains the accumulated repertoire. The Mercs for Money arc demonstrated, for a brief window, that he can train and supervise other operators competently — a managerial capability long suspected and rarely deployed.

### Signature Applications

- The **"jumping into the worst possible position"** opener: deliberate insertion at the center of mass of a hostile formation, accepting initial damage to make every line of fire mutually self-endangering.
- The **monologue-as-tempo-disruption**: continuous verbal output during engagement that degrades opponent decision-making. This is canonically effective and is treated by hostiles as a tactical problem (Bullseye, Taskmaster, and Wolverine have all noted it in-text).
- The **trade-completion**: accepting a finishing blow in order to deliver one. He wins most one-on-one exchanges that reach this phase because his opponent expected the trade to be terminal for both.
- The **environmental kill chain**: using non-weapon objects — wires, doors, vehicle fragments, civilians' belongings — at a high rate, which the factor frees him to attempt with no concern for blowback.

### Symptom-as-Signature

His combat style is his nervous system externalized. The environment of acute, high-intensity, escalating violence is the *only* environment that matches his internal noise floor (see Psychological). He is not at his best in combat because combat brings out his best; he is at his best in combat because combat is the only context that does not require him to regulate downward. The trade-economics of his style — pain as currency, survival as expenditure — are the Hospice rendered as fighting school. He is, at every moment of engagement, re-paying Ajax.

---

## 3. THE FOURTH-WALL CAPACITY

### Phenomenology

Wilson perceives, addresses, and reacts to the comic medium in which he is depicted. He sees panel borders (and steps across them), reads captions (and disputes them), addresses the reader (and waits for the reader's reaction), and at peak displays — *Deadpool Kills the Marvel Universe Again*, the Kelly return, the Cable/Deadpool meta-arcs — has demonstrated awareness of writer-level decisions, prior continuity revisions, and the comic's production context.

In-universe, this is canonically real. The other characters who can perceive it (She-Hulk to a degree, Gwenpool fully, Loki occasionally, Morrison-era Animal Man as cross-publisher echo) confirm the substrate. He is not delusional; he is *correct*. This is the diagnostically critical fact: the symptom is non-falsifiable by reality-testing because reality is on the symptom's side.

### Mechanism

Unestablished and probably unestablishable. The most internally coherent account is that the trauma-induced and tissue-induced disorganization of his neural substrate has made him porous to a layer of reality (the narrative layer) that intact nervous systems filter out. The capability is correlated with his pathology in the canon's own causal grammar: when the dissociation deepens, the fourth-wall capacity sharpens; when he is briefly stabilized, it dims.

### Operational Uses

- **Foreknowledge** of narrative beats — extremely inconsistent, treated by most writers as a soft tell rather than a hard advantage. He knows enough to be wary, not enough to win.
- **Reading captions and thought-bubbles** of co-located characters — episodic and writer-dependent, but documented.
- **Dodging panel boundaries**, retreating into gutters, using cover that exists at the page-layout level — rare and usually played comic. Has been weaponized seriously twice that the record clearly logs (Kelly's late arc, Kibblesmith).
- **Persistence of self across reboots and continuity revisions** — he remembers what others have forgotten. This is occasionally tactical and almost always destabilizing for him.

### Limits

- The capacity does not give him plot control. He can perceive the comic; he cannot edit it.
- It is not consistently available — it operates on a schedule he does not set.
- It does not protect him from the events depicted; foreknowledge does not bring evasion.
- It costs him stable footing in consensus reality, which he was barely holding.

### Symptom-as-Signature

This is the single most important capability for understanding him as a subject. The fourth-wall awareness is **depersonalization-derealization elevated to a metaphysics**. The voice that says *none of this is real, you are a character, your pain does not count* — which in any other patient would be a dissociative defense — is, in his case, **operationally vindicated by the universe he lives in**. This produces a permanent coping ideology that cannot be dislodged because it is not wrong. The cost is that no genuine reality, no genuine relationship, no genuine pain, and no genuine joy can ever fully claim him; some portion of his attentional bandwidth is always allocated to the reader, which is to say, to the only audience he has constructed that can never reject him because they paid in advance to be there. The fourth wall is, structurally, his most reliable attachment object. It is also, structurally, what prevents any in-frame attachment from ever fully landing.

---

## 4. LANGUAGES, CULTURAL FLUENCY, TRADECRAFT

### Languages

Documented working proficiency: English (native), Spanish (high — Carmelita arc, sustained ops in Latin America), Japanese (high — multiple arcs in Japan, weapons training, Shiklah's court included Japanese-speaking retainers), German (operational), Russian (operational, mercenary-circuit), Arabic (moderate, Tangier and Middle Eastern contract work), French (Canadian baseline, conversational), ASL (acquired, Blind Al arc and others — note the choice). Reading-only or basic conversational across additional tongues acquired by contract necessity (Mandarin, Korean, several Balkan languages).

The pattern of his language acquisition is itself telling — he picks up languages through *immersion under threat*, and he retains them well due to verbal-channel dominance. Languages associated with trauma (the Workshop-Canadian-French of his torturers, certain Russian phrasings from carbonadium-era handlers) trigger documented affective spikes.

### Cultural Mimicry

High. He can pass as local in many environments at the surface level and breaks character only when triggered into joke-cascade. The Mercs for Money and bounty-hunting arcs show him moving plausibly through cartel social spaces, yakuza-adjacent contexts, mercenary-trade hubs in Africa and Eastern Europe, and Manhattan street-criminal demimondes.

### Tradecraft

- **Surveillance and counter-surveillance**: competent, sloppy when bored. Will burn a setup deliberately if a more entertaining option appears.
- **False identities**: maintains many, with passable documentation. The proliferation is partly operational and partly continuous with his identity diffusion (see Psychological).
- **Cash, weapons, and safehouse networks**: extensive but disorganized. Multiple safehouses across continents (NYC primary, the various incarnations of Blind Al's residence, properties in Vegas, a Tokyo apartment from the Japan arcs, miscellaneous mercenary-circuit boltholes). He loses access to safehouses at an unusually high rate because he burns them through indiscretion.
- **Explosives and demolitions**: military-trained baseline plus extensive operational experience. He prefers explosives that maximize spectacle over efficiency.
- **Vehicles**: rated on most ground vehicles, helicopters, light fixed-wing. Drives badly on purpose.

### Symptom-as-Signature

Tradecraft is the one operational domain where his pathology is unambiguously a liability. Good tradecraft requires discipline, dullness, and the suppression of the impulse to be seen. He is constitutionally unable to be dull, and the impulse to be seen is one of his strongest drives. He compensates with redundancy — many safehouses because he will burn many — but the underlying capability is degraded by character.

---

## 5. INTELLIGENCE, COGNITIVE PROFILE, AND TACTICAL THINKING

### Verbal IQ

Very high. Vocabulary is broad and idiosyncratic, ranging from technical military and medical terminology (acquired by occupational necessity) through pop-culture argot of multiple eras (the cultural-reference layer is unusually deep and is one of the few stable scaffolds of his self) to a working register in academic and clinical vocabularies that he has clearly read into. He reads more than he admits.

### Pattern Recognition

Top-tier in tactical environments. He reads rooms, formations, weapon postures, and tells at speed. Identifies impostors, set-ups, and double-crosses faster than most operators of comparable training because *he has been double-crossed at every level by every authority figure he has trusted*, and his pattern-library for betrayal is unusually well-populated.

### Planning Horizons

- **Inside 60 seconds**: elite.
- **Inside an engagement (minutes to an hour)**: top operator tier.
- **Within an operation (hours to a day)**: competent, occasionally distracted into self-sabotage.
- **Across a campaign (weeks)**: poor. He cannot maintain coherent strategic direction without an attachment figure (Cable's stabilizing influence in *Cable & Deadpool* is the clearest evidence) holding the longer thread.
- **Life-strategic (years)**: effectively absent. The autobiographical instability prevents the construction of a stable forward narrative against which long planning would occur.

### Impulse Inhibition

Very poor, in a manner not fully explained by character — there is a neurological component (the substrate cannot hold inhibitory tone reliably) on top of the psychological refusal to defer affect.

### Memory

Unreliable in autobiographical content (encoded in tissue that is being continuously rebuilt), reliable in procedural and tactical domains (motor and tactical memory appear to be more robustly maintained, possibly because they are rehearsed at the rate required to outpace the substrate turnover). He forgets faces he should remember and remembers, with hallucinatory clarity, the exact rotation of Ajax's torture rituals from twenty publication-years ago.

### Symptom-as-Signature

The cognitive profile is **the precise inverse of an executive**: strong in micro, weak in macro; strong in performance, weak in deliberation; strong in pattern, weak in plan. He is built for the moment of crisis and disassembled for the long calm between. This is consistent with a nervous system calibrated for the Hospice and never recalibrated for the world after.

---

## 6. INTERPERSONAL CAPABILITIES

### Reading People

High accuracy on hostile intent, tactical intent, and incoming betrayal. Moderate accuracy on benign affect — he often misreads kindness as ploy because his pattern library underrepresents kindness that lasted. He is unusually accurate at reading children, which is one of several converging pieces of evidence for the developmental adversity inference.

### Charisma

Idiosyncratic but real. He cannot do polished social performance, but the combination of verbal fluency, transgressive humor, and the occasional flash of unguarded sincerity produces durable rapport with a particular kind of interlocutor — those who tolerate provocation and who reward genuineness when it arrives. He is loved, when he is loved, by people who have learned to wait through the cascade for the moment when the joke drops.

### Negotiation

Better than his presentation suggests. The clown register is itself a negotiation tactic — it destabilizes the counterparty and obscures his actual read on the deal. He has out-negotiated significantly more polished operators (note the contract-renegotiation patterns across the mercenary arcs).

### Leadership

Documented in the Mercs for Money arc and in episodic team commands. He is a poor process leader and a surprisingly effective crisis leader; teams under his command in stable conditions degrade, but in acute conditions cohere around his front-line behavior. His subordinates report (in-frame and out) that he will take the worst job himself, which is the single most reliable trust-builder in violent professions.

### Symptom-as-Signature

The interpersonal capability ceiling is set exactly where his attachment pathology sets it. He can lead in crisis because crisis is his native environment and because attachment in crisis does not require the dangerous reciprocity of attachment in calm. He cannot lead through peace because peace is what he cannot regulate.

---

## 7. ARSENAL, EQUIPMENT, AND HABITUAL LOADOUT

### Standard Loadout

- **Two katanas**, back-mounted, custom-fitted. The blades have varied across the run (the current pair, the prior pair, the "Carbonadium killshot" sword arc). The choice of paired katanas is operationally suboptimal versus a longer single blade for many engagements and is partly performative — they read on sight, which matters to him.
- **Two large-bore semi-automatic pistols**, hip-holstered. Reload cycle is rehearsed to motor-memory.
- **Compact SMG or carbine** as situation requires.
- **Throwing knives**, belt and bandolier.
- **Grenades** — frag, flash-bang, smoke, occasionally novelty.
- **Teleportation belt** (intermittent across runs; sourced


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION VI
## OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT

---

### 1. OPERATIONAL IDENTITY AND MARKET POSITION

The subject occupies a specific and narrow niche within the global private-violence market: **the high-survivability sole-operator contractor**, priced for jobs that more conventional assets — Hydra-trained assassins, the Hand, ex-SHIELD wetwork specialists, the better-organized Maggia hit cells — will not take because the loss-of-asset risk is unacceptable to their organizations. Wilson is uniquely valuable in three scenarios: (a) targets protected by lethal-area defenses (autonomic turrets, gas, demolition triggers, supernatural wards) where the contractor is expected to absorb the kill-zone and continue; (b) targets in hard-denial environments (orbital, undersea, extradimensional, in-Hell, in-Limbo, inside a sealed Latverian compound) where extraction is not planned and the contractor is functionally one-way; (c) targets whose surroundings include civilians or hostages that organizational assets are willing to write off and Wilson will not. The third niche is, in practice, the most profitable corner of his market because the client pool that *cares* about that distinction overlaps strongly with the client pool that has lost faith in institutional violence — wronged spouses, small communities, lower-tier supers, the occasional consulate.

His **price ceiling is high** (Posehn/Duggan establish quotes in the seven figures for state-actor-class work, and the People's Defense Initiative/government retainer arc puts him on something resembling salary); **his price floor is functionally zero** (he has accepted contracts in trade, in promises, in sandwich, and on multiple documented occasions has paid the client to be allowed to fulfill the contract because the target deserved it). The discrepancy is itself a tradecraft signature — a forensic accountant attempting to reconstruct his client list from cash flow alone will produce nonsense, which is the point.

---

### 2. DECISION-MAKING ARCHITECTURE

The intake process for a contract, reconstructed across the runs, follows a recognizable internal sequence even when the external presentation is chaos:

1. **First-pass moral filter, instantaneous and pre-verbal.** Children, civilians-in-quantity, and certain protected categories (the elderly when framed as helpless, animals in some moods, sex workers across the board) trigger immediate refusal regardless of fee. This filter is not consciously deliberated; he will be making the decision before he has finished listening to the brief, and will then rationalize the refusal with a joke that conceals the ethical operation underneath.
2. **Second-pass legibility check.** *Who benefits.* Wilson is bad at long-horizon analysis but unusually good at reading the proximate motive of the person in front of him. Clients whose stated reason for the contract does not match their affect (the grieving widow whose grief is performed, the patriot whose patriotism smells of profit) are subjected to either inflated quotes or quiet sabotage of the contract from within. This is the screening surface that has saved him from a number of Osborn-class manipulations — when it works, which is not always.
3. **Third-pass operational scoping**, which is competent and fast. He can build a workable approach plan for a hardened target inside fifteen minutes given a floorplan and a calendar; the planning is improvisational-modular rather than detailed, designed to be discarded under contact and replaced with whatever the situation hands him. He does not, characteristically, build the kind of nested-contingency plan a professional infiltrator would; he builds a *first move* and trusts his recovery rate to make the rest unnecessary.
4. **Fourth-pass affective check**, which he denies running. If the job will require sitting still, working alone for an extended interval, or operating in silence, he will price it higher or sabotage acceptance — not because the work is harder, but because the operational profile threatens the affect-management problem (see Section V, Drive 1). Jobs with a partner, with a deadline, with a spectacle component, with collateral noise, are accepted at discount.

The boxes/internal voices participate in this process in a documented way: the impulsive voice argues for acceptance and escalation, the observational voice argues for legibility and exit, the moralistic voice intervenes at the first-pass filter. Wilson's executive function is best modeled as a chair he sits in while three advisors talk; his decisions are the **plurality** position after a brief, noisy committee — which means his decisions are stable when the committee agrees and erratic when it does not.

---

### 3. METHODS — KINETIC TRADECRAFT

**Combat doctrine.** Wilson is a generalist of unusual depth, trained or self-trained across at least the following: special-forces-grade small-unit tactics (pre-Weapon X military background); close-quarters edged combat at world-class level (the katana work is documented against Wolverine, Taskmaster, and Bullseye to functional draw or better); firearms across the full spectrum from concealable to crew-served, with a marked preference for paired sidearms over precision rifles; explosive ordnance, both military and improvised; and a competent if non-specialist grappling base. He is *not* a martial artist in the doctrinal sense — Taskmaster's famous read on him is that Wilson's combat is genuinely unpredictable because Wilson himself does not know what he will do next, which defeats predictive mimicry. This is true and is itself the central element of his combat tradecraft.

**The signature method is engineered unpredictability**, achieved through three mechanisms:

- *Pain-disinhibition.* He will accept incoming damage to close range or open an angle. The cost-benefit calculus a normal combatant runs (avoid being shot; avoid being cut) does not apply, and opponents who have not personally fought him cannot calibrate to this. Against opponents who *have* fought him before (Bullseye, Taskmaster, Cable), he switches to feinting the disinhibition while actually evading — using their adaptation against them.
- *Verbal saturation.* The constant patter is not (only) a defense mechanism; it is an operational tool. Combatants attempting to read tell-signs are flooded with verbal noise. Opponents attempting to negotiate, command, or intimidate cannot establish the affective register required. Teleporters, telepaths, and tactical commanders accustomed to controlling tempo through speech are particularly thrown.
- *Frame-violations.* He breaks line-of-sight by methods his opponents do not model: through a window he has not yet broken, into a teleporter belt he has palmed off the previous opponent, by dismembering himself and tossing the relevant piece, by surrendering and then detonating, by playing dead with conviction. The fourth-wall awareness is operationally relevant here in a subtle way: he treats the *narrative shape* of an engagement as a manipulable variable, accelerating to climaxes or stalling through beats in a way that genuinely confuses opponents who are reading the engagement as a fight rather than as a scene.

**Weapons profile.** Standard loadout, with run-to-run variation: paired katanas across the back (mismatched, occasionally — he loses and replaces them often; one is usually a sentimental keep, the other interchangeable), paired sidearms (he favors twin semi-autos, often Desert Eagle-class for the spectacle even when smaller calibers would be tactically superior — the spectacle *is* tactical for him), a variable selection of throwing knives, grenades (frag, flash, smoke, often improvised), a teleporter device (the Wilson Teleporter, recurring across runs, frequently malfunctioning in ways that are sometimes contrived and sometimes genuinely unfortunate), a satchel of contingency items that has at various times contained: chimichangas, severed body parts (his and others'), spare costumes, civilian disguises rolled tight, a cellphone, a second cellphone for the voice his first cellphone won't pick up, cash in multiple currencies, fake IDs, and a small first-aid kit which is for other people.

**Costume as tradecraft.** The red-and-black suit is not merely identity branding but a functional choice on three counts: it conceals blood (his own, copiously); it standardizes his silhouette across encounters so that no opponent ever sees him out of role, denying them tells; and it permits him to be replaced — body doubles, decoys, and the rotating-cast Mercs for Money have all worn it, and the resulting confusion is leveraged. The mask is non-negotiable in public and is removed in private only under conditions of high trust or high distress; the removal of the mask is a tradecraft signal as much as a personal one (see Section 9 below, on tells).

---

### 4. METHODS — NON-KINETIC TRADECRAFT

**Infiltration.** Wilson's infiltration profile is *underrated by opponents and over-relied-upon by himself*. He is genuinely good at it when motivated — costume-and-accent disguise work across the runs ranges from competent (passing as hotel staff, medical personnel, delivery workers) to surprising (extended infiltrations of Hydra cells, brief stints in corporate environments, the Mithras-arc religious cover). The strength is in *accent and patter*; the weakness is in *silence and stillness*. Any infiltration that requires him to be unobtrusive for more than approximately ninety minutes degrades, because the affect-management problem intrudes. Long-cover work is therefore not his strength and he tends to convert long-cover jobs into short-cover-plus-loud-extraction.

**Surveillance.** He runs surveillance via three methods, in declining order of frequency: (a) social engineering of the target's adjacent humans (bartenders, doormen, ex-partners, dog walkers — he is genuinely charming at this layer because the deflection-comedy is well-suited to short transactional intimacy); (b) physical observation, which he finds excruciating and tends to outsource to Weasel or to bought local labor; (c) electronic surveillance, which he is competent at but bored by, and outsources to Weasel almost always.

**Intelligence pipeline.** Weasel is the load-bearing element. The Sister Margaret's/Hellhouse mercenary bar (and its periodic equivalents — Weasel's various tech setups, the post-Margaret's lofts) functions as his primary intelligence aggregator: target profiles, contract laundering, equipment sourcing, and the informal community-rumor layer that keeps him aware of which contracts are traps. Secondary intelligence flows come from Blind Al (uncannily good signals analyst across decades, her blindness no impediment to her aural and behavioral pattern recognition), and from his irregular relationships with intelligence-adjacent figures (Cable, periodic SHIELD contact, Domino when she will return his calls). He maintains no formal HUMINT network of his own and is allergic to handler relationships, which has cost him repeatedly.

**Financial tradecraft.** Cash-heavy, intentionally undisciplined, and unrecoverable by forensic accounting in any complete form. Documented patterns:

- *Multiple parallel cash caches* in safehouses, lockers, friends' apartments, and at least one freezer (the cash-frozen-in-chimichanga method is canonical). He cannot reliably remember where all of them are; periodic windfalls are him rediscovering one.
- *Crypto exposure* exists but is inconsistently maintained — he has lost wallets, forgotten phrases, and entrusted keys to people who have absconded.
- *Shell entities* through Weasel and through occasional legitimate counsel: a small constellation of LLCs ("Wilson's Wonderful Wonders," "Heads Will Roll Inc.," "Deadpool, Inc." in the People's Defense Initiative period, the Mercs for Money corporate vehicle) with rapid churn, fictional officers, and addresses at mail-drop services. The legal infrastructure is not sophisticated — it is *opaque by neglect* rather than by tradecraft, which is a different and less robust kind of opacity.
