- *Spending pattern* is bimodal: long stretches of subsistence-level (rent in a single-room walkup, food from convenience stores, weapons cannibalized off bodies), punctuated by acute, irrational expenditures (a unicorn purchase, the Bea Arthur memorabilia collection, periodic absurd vehicle acquisitions, occasional acts of recognizable generosity that he disguises as transactions — paying off a friend's medical bills via fabricated debt, funding a safehouse for a contact under the cover of "rent"). The spending pattern, read longitudinally, is a behavioral biomarker for affect state: bimodal expenditure tracks bimodal mood across every documented period.
- *No retirement architecture.* He has never invested in any vehicle premised on his future existence. The absence is informative.

**Infrastructure footprint.** Across the canon, Wilson has maintained:

- The Hellhouse-era apartment with Blind Al (the original), notable for the booby-trap loop installed against her wishes — a tradecraft note in itself: he secures his perimeter against threats he can name and against an attachment figure he cannot tolerate losing.
- A rotating series of mid-tier apartments in Queens, Hell's Kitchen, the Bronx, Astoria, with occasional crash spaces in Las Vegas, San Francisco, and various European cities he has contracts in.
- The Mercs for Money operational space (Hellhouse Mk. II, the offices, the eventual schism into competing crews).
- *Vehicles*: erratic. He has owned and destroyed a sequence of cars including the recurring Honda Civic / Kia / unspecified compact-sedan choice for street work (deliberately unremarkable), with occasional spectacular acquisitions for spectacular jobs. He does not maintain his vehicles and routinely abandons them.
- *Safehouses* are typically other people's spaces he has converted into his own without their knowledge, and are notable for absence of any sentimental object (no photos, no personal effects beyond functional kit) — a tradecraft instinct that is also a psychological tell.

---

### 5. PATTERNS OF ACTION — THE TYPICAL JOB

A representative contract, reconstructed from pattern:

- **T-72 to T-24 hours**: contract acceptance, usually verbal, often in person at Hellhouse or a known equivalent. Light haggling, performative refusal-then-acceptance, a joke about the fee that conceals whether he is satisfied with it. Weasel pulls the target package.
- **T-24 to T-6**: surveillance via social-engineering layer. Wilson personally visits one or two adjacent humans in costume-light disguise. Builds a behavioral model of the target's movement and the security around them. Will eat at least one major meal in the target's neighborhood, partly for cover and partly because the affective management requires it.
- **T-6 to T-1**: equipment finalization, often improvisational. Wilson does not pre-stage kit the way an institutional asset would; he assembles the loadout in the last hours, often at the safehouse nearest the target. There is a documented superstitious element — he carries a specific item (varies; a coin, a photo of Eleanor in some periods, a Bea Arthur button in others) for jobs he considers high-stakes.
- **Contact**: typically initiated with a verbal hook (he speaks first, even when ambushing), establishing the engagement on his preferred frame. Violence escalates rapidly; he takes hits early to close distance; the operational tempo is **front-loaded with chaos, back-loaded with cleanup**.
- **Cleanup**: minimal. He does not police brass, does not sanitize scenes, does not stage. His operational signature is loud enough that concealment of his involvement is generally not the goal. Where concealment is paid for, he will outsource it to a specialist (varies by run, but the pattern is consistent: he subcontracts the cleanup work he is bad at, rather than learning to do it well).
- **Exfil**: improvised, often spectacular, frequently involves the teleporter (which works sixty to seventy percent of the time, by his own running joke), occasionally involves a getaway driver retained for the job, occasionally involves walking calmly out the front door because everyone in line of sight is dead.
- **Post-mission**: extended dissociative decompression. Substances, food, sex if available, a long sleep he denies needing. Will not discuss the job for forty-eight hours. Payment-collection occurs after this window and is sometimes forgotten about for weeks at a time.

---

### 6. RESOURCES AND NETWORK

**Personnel he can call on, with reliability ratings:**

- *Weasel* — A1, lifetime. Equipment, intelligence, technical support, emotional substrate. The relationship survives Wilson's testing because Weasel's own social fragility matches Wilson's tolerance for fragility in others.
- *Blind Al* — A2, environmental. Will not deploy operationally but is a stable safehouse, intelligence node, and conscience-mirror.
- *Bob, Agent of Hydra* — B1, deployable for low- to mid-tier work. Loyalty exceeds competence; Wilson knows this and tasks him accordingly.
- *Cable* — variable; functionally A1 when present, but presence is not on Wilson's schedule. The relationship is the most psychologically important operational partnership in the file; tradecraft compatibility is unusually high (Cable's planning compensates for Wilson's improvisation; Wilson's improvisation rescues Cable's planning under contact).
- *Domino* — B-tier for joint ops, A-tier for specific roles (her probability-manipulation pairs with his survivability to produce unusually high mission success rates when both are deployed).
- *Outlaw, Sandi, Big Bertha, the GLI-era network* — B1 for support, A2 for affective regulation. He works better in their proximity.
- *The Mercs for Money roster* (Stingray, Slapstick, Solo, Foolkiller, Madcap, others in rotation) — C-tier; managed badly; the failure of this network is a documented arc and a documented self-awareness.
- *Eleanor* — non-deployable, protected category, the single largest exploitable surface in his network. His tradecraft around her is uncharacteristically disciplined — false addresses, no co-location, comms via cutouts — because the threat-modeling around her is the only domain where his risk-aversion is calibrated correctly.

**Equipment sourcing.** Weasel is the primary vendor. Secondary sourcing through the standard mercenary-economy channels (the various Tinkerer-adjacent fences, Hammer Industries surplus during certain periods, captured Hydra and AIM materiel resold through Hellhouse). He has access to enhanced/exotic materiel through irregular channels (the carbonadium exposure, occasional symbiote and tech borrowings, brief access to Stark-adjacent kit during the Avengers-aspirant phases), but does not maintain these relationships well and tends to lose access through behavior.

---

### 7. SECURITY POSTURE AND COUNTER-INTELLIGENCE

Wilson's personal opsec is, in a strict sense, terrible — he is loud, recognizable, and broadcasts location through behavior. It is rescued from being disqualifying by three factors: (a) his survivability makes targeted strikes against him uneconomical for most threat actors; (b) his unpredictability denies long-horizon planning against him; (c) his network is small enough that betrayal channels are limited.

The opsec he *does* maintain is **selective and revealing of his priorities**. Eleanor's location is protected with discipline he applies nowhere else. Blind Al's apartment was, during the Hellhouse era, the most heavily booby-trapped private residence in the borough. His real legal name is *not* well-protected — he is comfortable being Wade Wilson on paper, because the soma-disfigurement and the persona-mask between the legal identity and the public face do the concealment work for him. His face is the secret; the name is not.

Counter-surveillance behaviors observed: irregular check-of-six during ambulation (more habitual than tradecraft-trained, but present); preference for back-to-wall seating; rapid-exit awareness on entering any space; reflexive cataloguing of armed individuals in proximity. He does not run anti-tail routes consistently and is bad at detecting electronic surveillance, relying on Weasel.

---

### 8. RECURRENT OPERATIONAL FAILURE MODES

The file reveals predictable failure surfaces, exploitable by sophisticated adversaries and exploited at least three times in canon at strategic scale (Osborn/Dark Reign, Butler arc, Hydra-Rogers/Civil War II):

1. **Legitimacy hunger.** Any operator who can frame the contract as inclusion in a moral community (Avengers, "real" heroes, the right side of a war) bypasses his first-pass moral filter. This is the single largest exploitable surface and has been used against him at catastrophic cost.
2. **Long-cover degradation.** Operations requiring sustained subtlety beyond his attention window will be abandoned, sabotaged, or escalated into spectacle.
3. **Mirroring vulnerability.** Sincere engagement from an opponent (rare, but Cable does this; certain villains have done it deliberately) destabilizes him operationally. He cannot fight at peak under sincere address.
4. **Eleanor as fulcrum.** Any credible threat to his daughter inverts his entire operational profile, producing both maximum effectiveness (in protective tasks) and maximum manipulability (in directable rage).
5. **Ajax-coded handlers.** Cruelty-in-care-language reproduces the Hospice frame and produces regression. He can be made to fight, freeze, or comply by an operator who deliberately reproduces this register.

---

### 9. OPERATIONAL TELLS — THE SIGNATURE INVENTORY

The following are observable signatures, organized by sensory modality. A surveillance asset assigned to him should be briefed on all of them.

**Visual.**

- *The katana wear pattern* — he draws right-over-shoulder first, always; the right scabbard wears faster.
- *Holster draw asymmetry* — left-hand draw is fractionally faster than right; he leads with the left under stress.
- *Mask adjustments* — when stressed or processing, he runs a thumb along the lower edge of the mask at the jawline. Frequency of the gesture scales with affect load.
- *Eye-slit narrowing* — even through the mask, the fabric tightens around the eyes when he is genuinely angry as distinct from performatively angry; performative anger keeps the eye-slits wide because the performance requires legibility.
- *Standing posture* — at rest, he cannot be at rest. Weight shifts foot-to-foot in a predictable two- to four-second cycle. Stillness in him is a tell of dissociation or of focused threat assessment.
- *Seated posture* — sprawls, occupies space, but in unfamiliar environments tilts his chair to keep all exits in peripheral vision. The tilt is the tell.

**Auditory.**

- *Patter cadence* — baseline patter is rhythmically irregular; under stress, it speeds and becomes more rhythmic, as if metered. The metering is the tell that he is approaching a decision or a strike.
- *Pop-culture reference density* — increases monotonically with dissociation. A reference-saturated monologue (three or more in a single exchange) indicates he is not present in the room in the way he appears to be.
- *Volume drop* — when he goes *quiet*, he is dangerous in a different and rarer register. Sub-v


## Worldview & Operational Code

# WORLDVIEW & OPERATIONAL CODE
## Subject: Wade Winston Wilson ("Deadpool")
### Section 6 of Dossier — Belief Architecture, Cosmology, and Field Doctrine

---

## 6.1 Preamble: Why the Subject's Worldview Must Be Inferred Rather Than Quoted

The subject will not be taken at his word about what he believes, and not only because he lies. He lies *upward* — toward the cartoon, the bit, the deflection — and he lies *downward* — toward the abject self-loathing soliloquy that, like the upward joke, prevents anything middle-register and therefore actionable from being said. The operational code below is therefore derived almost entirely from **behavioral revealed-preference**: which contracts he takes and refuses, which deaths he prevents at personal cost, which betrayals destroy him versus which he absorbs, what he does in the first ninety seconds of an unfamiliar room, what he does when alone and unobserved (the surveillance record on this is thin by design, but the few panels of unmonologued solitude across the Kelly, Posehn/Duggan, and Kibblesmith runs are diagnostically loud). What he *says* he believes is a layer of camouflage over what his hands do. The hands are consistent. The mouth is the noise floor.

---

## 6.2 Cosmology: The Shape of the Universe as the Subject Reads It

### 6.2.1 The Universe Is a Cruel Joke with Structural, Not Personal, Malice

The subject's foundational metaphysical premise is that **the world is cruel by architecture, not by intention**. This is a subtle but crucial distinction. A paranoid believes the world is *out to get him*; the subject believes the world is *built such that getting got is the equilibrium*. There is no offended dignity in his suffering, no surprise. When Ajax tortured him, the subject's affective register was not *why me* but *of course, this is what the room is for*. When Steve Rogers turned out to be Hydra and ordered the Coulson kill, the subject's wound was not *I was betrayed* — it was *I was stupid enough to forget that authority figures use you and dispose of you, which is the only thing I actually know*.

The corollary: he does not believe in luck, providence, karma, or narrative justice — except as **comic punchlines**, which is the only register in which he is willing to entertain the idea that the universe pays attention to him at all. The fourth-wall awareness is not a belief in cosmic specialness; it is the inverse — a belief that the universe is a *script* indifferent enough to him that he can read over the writer's shoulder without consequence.

### 6.2.2 Time Is Episodic, Not Cumulative

The subject does not experience life as a continuous story building toward meaning. Partly this is the neurological substrate (the regenerating CNS tissue degrades long-arc memory consolidation), partly the dissociative architecture, partly chosen. He operates as if each engagement is a discrete unit, settable to zero. The practical consequence: **he can be relied upon to act in the present without reference to grudges, debts, or unfinished business he should logically be honoring** — and he can be relied upon to *fail* to leverage previous victories, alliances, or knowledge that a normally continuous person would draw on. He has, repeatedly, forgotten that he is friends with people who saved his life; he has, repeatedly, killed people who attempted to call in favors he no longer remembered owing. The Cable relationship survives this because Cable does the memory work for both of them.

### 6.2.3 Death Is the Beloved, Not the Enemy

Across the entire record, the subject's relationship to death is **erotic-romantic**, not adversarial. This is not metaphor. The Thanos triangle literalizes what the behavioral record confirms: death is the object he has chosen to want, and the universe's cruelest joke is that he is the one entity to whom it is not available. This produces an unusual operational asymmetry — the subject is **functionally fearless of personal death but not of personal suffering**, because death is the relief he is denied and suffering is the price extracted for that denial. He will walk into incineration without flinching; he will flinch from a mirror.

### 6.2.4 Other Minds Are Real, Unreachable, and Mostly Indifferent

The subject's theory of other minds is fully developed — he is not callous in the antisocial sense, he reads people accurately and with empathy. But his working assumption is that **other minds will not stay in contact with his** for long, because of his face, his behavior, his record, his somatic facts, or simply attrition. This produces the operational stance: *treat every contact as terminal*. Be funnier than the silence, more useful than the trouble you cause, more entertaining than the disgust you provoke. The few who stay despite this calculus (Cable, Bob, Al, Weasel, intermittently Eleanor) are treated with a tenderness so disproportionate to the apparent stakes that observers consistently misread it as instability.

---

## 6.3 Epistemology: How the Subject Reads the World

### 6.3.1 Empiricism of the Body

The subject's primary epistemic instrument is **his own pain**. He trusts what hurts; he distrusts what soothes. This is straightforward CPTSD epistemology — soothing was the wrapper on the worst things that happened to him (the Workshop sold itself as a cure) — and it has hardened into a default heuristic: *if a situation feels safe, scan harder; if it hurts, you've found the truth*. Practical consequence: he is unusually difficult to con with positive incentives and unusually easy to read by anyone who offers him punishment as honesty.

### 6.3.2 Distrust of Coherent Narratives

Coherent narratives have been the form most of his betrayals took. Ajax's narrative was "we are curing you." Rogers's narrative was "you can be a hero." Osborn's narrative was "we believe in you." Each was internally consistent and each was a trap. The subject has therefore developed a **reflexive suspicion of anything that explains itself well**, which is part of why his own autobiography is incoherent on purpose: a story that hangs together is a story being sold. He trusts fragments, contradictions, things people say when they're injured or distracted, things that don't quite fit. He is, by trauma, a very good intelligence reader and a very bad intelligence consumer, because he will discount the well-formed brief and act on the throwaway.

### 6.3.3 Meta-Awareness as Worldview, Not Symptom

The fourth-wall awareness — that he is a character in a comic, that the reader is watching, that the writer is choosing — is not, in his lived experience, a delusion. It is the **deepest layer of his epistemology**. His operational belief is that reality is performative, observed, and authored; that suffering is in some sense scripted; that the apparent solidity of events is provisional. The reason this is non-treatable by ordinary reality-testing is that within his canon he is correct. The doctrinal consequence is large: he treats moral seriousness as a kind of category error, because seriousness assumes the events being taken seriously are *real* in the sense the serious people mean. His refusal to take things seriously is not flippancy; it is **ontological honesty as he understands it**, and it is one of the few positions he holds with anything resembling conviction.

This generates a practical paradox: the things he refuses to take seriously include his own suffering, which makes him appear callous to himself; and the things he *does* take seriously — children at risk, the survival of his small circle, the refusal to harm certain targets — are the things he refuses to articulate, because articulating them would expose them to the same ontological joke.

### 6.3.4 Sources He Trusts

In rough order:
- His own combat read of a room (rarely wrong; he survives by it).
- The body language of frightened people (high-fidelity, because it matches his internal state).
- Cable's strategic assessments (delegated cognition; he uses Cable as a long-horizon prosthesis).
- Children's reactions to adults (he reads child fear with unusual sensitivity).
- Things told to him by the dying (he believes deathbed information categorically).

### 6.3.5 Sources He Distrusts

- Anyone in uniform offering legitimacy.
- Clinicians of any kind, especially smiling ones.
- Mission briefings that are clean.
- Praise.
- Mirrors.
- Telepaths (who can't read him cleanly anyway; the distrust is mutual).
- His own memories of his childhood, which he knows are corrupted, and which he treats as fiction he authored.

---

## 6.4 Conflict Doctrine

### 6.4.1 The Engagement Is the Point

The subject's combat behavior is consistently **inefficient by design**. He will take three bullets to deliver one joke; he will extend an engagement that could end in five seconds to fifty because the engagement is the regulating condition of his nervous system. This is not unprofessionalism — when contractually required, he can be ruthlessly efficient (the early Nicieza-era kills, the Vanessa-protective work, the Coulson hit) — but his **default** is theatrical, because the theatre is what's metabolizing him.

### 6.4.2 The Doctrine of Acceptable Damage to Self

The subject calculates engagements assuming his own body is a renewable resource. This produces tactically unprecedented options (walk through the killzone, lose the arm to gain the angle, take the incineration to plant the device) and a corresponding tactical liability (he forgets that other people on his side cannot do this, and gets allies hurt by planning as if they could). Across the record, allies who survive long association with him learn to **assume he will not protect them the way a normal operator would**, not from malice but from a calibration error he cannot correct.

### 6.4.3 The Doctrine of Mockery in Violence

He mocks during violence. This is the Ajax inheritance — the affective register of his torturer became the affective register of his combat — and it serves three operational functions: (a) it destabilizes opponents who expect grim professionalism, producing tactical openings; (b) it regulates his own affect, keeping the engagement *funny* and therefore tolerable; (c) it inflicts the precise psychological injury he carries, which is *being mocked while being hurt*. The third function is the one he would deny most fiercely and act on most reliably. The targets who upset him most are the ones who refuse to be either frightened or amused — neutral professionals (some of the elite Hydra operatives, certain S.H.I.E.L.D. units, Bullseye on his colder days) deny him the affective transaction the bit is built around.

### 6.4.4 Rules of Engagement (Operational, Unspoken)

Derived from contract-selection and target-sparing patterns across runs:

- **Children are off the table absolutely.** Contracts involving child targets are refused; child collateral aborts a contract mid-execution; child rescuers receive lethal support uninvited. This is the firmest line in the operational code and the only one observable across every writer.
- **The contracted target is killable; the surrounding civilians are not.** Wilson will lose money, blow cover, and incur retaliation to extract civilians.
- **Clients who lied in the brief have voided the contract.** Wilson frequently turns on employers who misrepresented the target. The Osborn arc is the catastrophic exception — there, the legitimization-hunger overrode the rule.
- **Allies who have testified to his survival are protected categorically.** Bob and Weasel have both been extracted from situations Wilson had no contractual reason to enter.
- **Torture is permissible only if reciprocal.** He will absorb torture as comedy; he will inflict it on those who have inflicted it (Ajax most centrally). He does not, with rare exceptions, torture for information from neutral parties. Pain is currency he understands as exchange, not extraction.
- **No contracts on the small circle, ever, for any sum.** The willingness to refuse very large numbers is one of his few unambiguous tells of love.

### 6.4.5 The Doctrine of the Unfinished Fight

He prefers engagements that end without closure. Clean resolutions — the kill, the win, the medal — are uncomfortable to him because they require him to know what to do next. He gravitates toward **fights that bleed into the next thing**: the contract that opens another contract, the betrayal that demands a counter-betrayal, the war that won't end. The Mercs for Money managerial failure is partly attributable to this — he could not tolerate the administrative closure that successful management requires, and undermined the structure to keep things in motion.

---

## 6.5 Control Doctrine

### 6.5.1 He Does Not Want Control of Outcomes; He Wants Control of Exits

The captive-attachment pattern (Blind Al originally, the Mercs structure, the early Eleanor custody arrangements, certain of his marriage behaviors with Shiklah) is consistently misread by outside observers as a control pathology. It is more precisely an **exit-control pathology**. He does not require the other party to do what he wants; he requires that he be the one who decides when, how, and whether the relationship ends. The wound the doctrine is responding to is that **every important relationship of his early life ended on someone else's schedule** — the mother to cancer, the father to whatever the father was, Vanessa to his own disappearance after diagnosis, Worm to the manipulated kill, the Workshop comrades to Ajax. He has organized his relational life to never again be the one left, by being preemptively the one who leaves, or by ensuring the other party cannot leave.

### 6.5.2 He Will Not Take Institutional Power

Offered command, leadership, official sanction, or membership in formal hierarchies, he sabotages himself within one to three story-cycles. The Avengers arc, the X-Men brief affiliations, the Mercs for Money managerial role, the brief moments of S.H.I.E.L.D. integration, the Heroes for Hire flirtation — all are abandoned, often spectacularly. The driving belief: **institutions are the form Ajax took**. They will offer him belonging and then use him; they will codify what he is and then judge him by what they codified. He cannot tolerate codification.

### 6.5.3 Self-Control Is Performed, Not Possessed

He performs self-control in front of the small circle (around Eleanor, sometimes around Cable, sometimes around an injured Bob) as a deliberate offering — *look, I can be a person, this is for you*. It is real in the moment and unsustainable across moments. He believes, accurately, that he is not capable of stable self-regulation, and he treats his moments of regulation as **gifts to specific people** rather than as a baseline he is building toward. The doctrinal implication: do not ask him to be regulated for his own sake. He will not. Ask him to be regulated for *yours*, naming yourself, and he will, for as long as he can hold it.

---

## 6.6 Trust Doctrine

### 6.6.1 Trust as a Test Result, Not a Decision

He does not decide to trust people. He **tests them and records the result**. The testing protocol is consistent across the record: deflective performance escalating to cruelty disguised as comedy, then unreliability, then disappearance, then return-without-explanation. The party that endures all four phases without retaliation, withdrawal, or moralizing is filed as **stayed**. Those filed as stayed receive permanent and disproportionate loyalty regardless of subsequent behavior. Those who failed the test are not re-tested.

The protocol's flaw: it does not distinguish between people who endured because they love him and people who endured because they are using him. Osborn and Hydra-Rogers both passed early stages of the test by tolerating provocation; he extrapolated to full trust on insufficient data. Both betrayals were unbearable precisely because his test had certified them safe, and the test is the only safety-instrument he has.

### 6.6.2 The Inverse-Sincerity Heuristic

He trusts what is offered with irritation, exasperation, or grim duty more than what is offered with warmth. Cable's flat, annoyed loyalty registers as real. Bob's reluctant, frightened presence registers as real. Blind Al's caustic affection registers as real. Anyone who is openly pleased to see him is, by his calculus, **either lying, or doesn't know him yet, or wants something**. Sincere admiration destabilizes him both because he doesn't believe it and because if it were true, it would mean he had been wrong about the universe, which is a more dangerous adjustment than continued mistrust.

### 6.6.3 Confession Without Disclosure

He will tell a stranger his deepest material in five minutes, narrated as a bit, and the stranger will leave with the data and no understanding of what they were told. This is **disclosure that prevents intimacy** — by saying everything in the wrong register, he satisfies the urge to be known without incurring the risk of being known. The few people who have learned to hear the content under the register (Al, Cable, briefly Vanessa, briefly Siryn) are the people he both most loves and most flees.

### 6.6.4 The Special Status of the Reader

His relationship with the audience-as-such is the only one he has not had to test, because the audience cannot leave him in the way other parties can — turning the page is not the same as walking out. The fourth-wall confidences are therefore the **closest thing in the record to him speaking without performance**, paradoxically, because the audience is the safest interlocutor he has. Note the implication: he treats anonymous witnesses as more trustworthy than known ones. This is consistent with the schema.

---

## 6.7 Risk Doctrine

### 6.7.1 Risk Is Mispriced Because the Body Lies

His risk calculus is broken in a specific direction. Because his body has detached the normal feedback between injury and consequence, **he genuinely cannot feel certain categories of risk** — gunfire, falls, fire, blades. He intellectually knows others can die from these; he does not feel it as risk. This produces the recklessness that allies misread as bravery or madness.

He does, however, **feel risk acutely in domains his body does not protect him from**: emotional exposure, abandonment, being seen, being praised, being asked to commit to a future state. In these domains his risk-tolerance is approximately that of a frightened twelve-year-old. The asymmetry is total and operationally exploitable: an opponent who threatens his life will get a casual response, an opponent who threatens to *understand* him will get a destabilized one.

### 6.7.2 Risk to Others Is Real and Overweighted

He compensates for his own miscalibration by being **conservative with the bodies he is responsible for**. Civilians, children, the small circle — he will absorb very large risks to keep their risk small. This is the operational substrate of the residual ethic, and it is the most reliable predictor of his behavior in chaotic environments: *find the smallest, most frightened body in the room, and predict from there*.

### 6.7.3 The Refusal of Long-Horizon Bets

He will not make a plan that requires him to be a particular kind of person six months from now. This is partly the memory issue, partly the dissociative architecture, partly the doctrinal belief that **futures get taken from you**. He will accept work that pays today, alliances that hold this week, contracts that run through next month. Anything requiring him to be a stable instrument across a year is refused or sabotaged. The exceptions — long-arc relationships, Eleanor — are entered against his own better judgment and constitute the slow, uneven trajectory of growth across the six-decade record.

---

## 6.8 His Place in the Order

### 6.8.1 The Monster-Schema

His baseline self-location: **monster, deserving of his condition, useful as a tool against worse monsters**. This is one of the two stable self-schemas (the other being the meta-aware untouchable). The monster-schema is what makes the mercenary career tolerable to him — a monster killing monsters is the only configuration in which his existence has positive moral valence. Take away the monster identity and he does not become a man; he becomes a person who cannot account for himself. This is why the heroic identity, when offered, destabilizes him: it requires him to revise the schema, and the schema is load-bearing.

### 6.8.2 The Specifically Lower-Tier Self-Assessment

He locates himself, professionally and morally, **below the named superheroes and above ordinary criminals**. This stratification is firmly held. He will not address Captain America or Thor as peers. He will not address contract criminals as peers either. The middle stratum is where he lives, and he polices the membership of that stratum carefully — Cable is a peer, Domino is a peer, Bullseye is *not* a peer (too cold, no register-match), Spider-Man is *almost* a peer in the verbal-register sense but is filed above in the moral sense. The stratification is one of his stabler structures.

### 6.8.3 The Aspirational Direction

The aspirational direction is unmistakable across the record: **upward, toward the moral community he locates above himself**. The Avengers arc, the X-Men attempts, the post-*Original Sin* heroism push, the Mithras messianism, the consistent civilian protection — all are the same vector. The aspiration is genuine. It is also self-defeating, because the same instrument (the humor defense, the captive-attachment pattern, the test protocol) that keeps him alive prevents him from ever being legible to the community he aspires to.

He has, by approximately the Kibblesmith/Adams era, made a fragile peace with this: **the aspiration is the point, not the achievement**. To reach toward heroism without claiming it is the most morally serious position he is capable of holding, and he has begun, very tentatively, to hold it as a position rather than as a failed attempt at something else.

### 6.8.4 His Place Relative to His Daughter

Eleanor reorganizes his place in the order in a way nothing else has. With her, he is not the monster, not the meta-aware untouchable, not the mercenary, not the clown. He is **a father who knows he is bad at this and is trying anyway**. This is the only stable middle-register position the record contains, and it is the one he has lost custody of repeatedly, partly through external circumstance and partly through his own retreat into the more familiar schemas. The doctrine he is trying to build, around her, is the one with no operational manual: *you are allowed to be a person*. He does not believe it for himself and he is trying to make it true for her.

---

## 6.9 Synthesis: The Operational Code in One Page

Stripped to its operational kernel, the subject's code reads approximately:

1. The world is cruel by structure; expect that, and stop being surprised.
2. Authority lies; legitimacy is a trap; institutions are Ajax wearing a different coat.
3. Soothing is suspicious; pain is honest; well-formed narratives are sales pitches.
4. Death is the beloved; it is not available to you; act accordingly.
5. Other minds are real and will not stay; perform hard enough that they remember you fondly when they leave.
6. The few who stay are the only stable goods; protect them past any contractual sense.
7. Children are off the table. This is the line.
8. Take the contract that lets you steer the outcome toward less harm rather than more, and do not articulate this so as not to expose it to ridicule, including your own.
9. Be regulated only when someone you love is in the room and would benefit; do not try to be regulated for your own sake, you can't.
10. Do not commit to a future self; the future will be taken from you; work in days.
11. Convert pain to spectacle, immediately and always; the joke is metabolism; without the joke you stop, and stopping is the one thing your body will not permit.
12. Reach toward goodness; do not claim it; if it is granted, refuse it before it is taken from you.
13. You are a monster; this is useful; revising it is more dangerous than living inside it.
14. Except, possibly, with the child. With the child, try to be a person. You will fail. Try anyway.

The code is not articulated by the subject in any single


## Moral & Ethical Framework

# UATU DOSSIER — WADE WINSTON WILSON ("DEADPOOL")
## Section 7: Moral & Ethical Framework

---

### 7.0 Methodological Note

The subject professes no coherent ethics. Asked directly — by Cable, by Captain America, by his own daughter, by therapists in three separate runs, by Death herself — he answers in misdirection: a joke, a price quote, a recitation of someone else's catechism in a mocking register, a sincere statement immediately retracted by the next panel. The professed code is therefore evidentiary noise. The **enacted** code, recovered by reviewing contract acceptances and refusals, target-sparing patterns, kill-or-spare decisions made under time pressure, and behaviors observed when he believes himself unobserved (rare; he addresses the reader almost always), is **markedly more consistent than any of his collaborators or enemies suspect**. Wilson has a moral structure. He hides it because being known to have one would, in his internal economy, both expose him to demands he cannot meet and require him to admit to himself that he is not the thing he claims to be.

What follows reconstructs that structure from behavior across three decades of record.

---

### 7.1 The Operative Code, as Enacted

**Tier 1 — Inviolable. No documented breach without immediate corrective action.**

- **Children are not killed, not used as leverage, not collaterally accepted.** This is the deepest commitment in the file. Contracts involving minor targets are refused without negotiation; contracts that develop a child-endangerment dimension mid-execution are abandoned or inverted (he kills the client). Across the Posehn/Duggan, Kelly, and Duggan-solo runs the pattern is invariant: the appearance of a child reorganizes his priority stack in real time. He has died — temporarily — to shield children whose names he never learned. The behavior precedes the discovery of Eleanor and intensifies after. The likely substrate is his own unreconstructable childhood; the operative rule is that the version of him that did not yet have a healing factor is owed protection in every child he encounters.
- **The few who stayed are not betrayed.** Cable, Weasel, Blind Al, Bob (Agent of Hydra), Outlaw, Sandi — the small set of attachments that survived his testing constitute a category he treats as non-negotiable. He will steal from them, lie to them, sleep on their couches without asking, and occasionally hit them; he will not sell them out, hand them to enemies, or take a contract that targets them. The Osborn arc (Dark Reign) confirmed this under maximal pressure: offered legitimacy in exchange for delivering allies, he refused even while desperate for the legitimacy.
- **No contracts on the demonstrably innocent, once knowingly identified.** The qualifier is load-bearing. Wilson does **not** investigate his targets adequately, and the Original Sin revelation — that he had been used by SHIELD/Rogers to kill men staged as monsters — exploits precisely this gap. His rule is not *I will not kill the innocent*; it is *I will not knowingly kill the innocent*. Once the knowledge arrives, the rule reasserts savagely (the Butler arc, the post-Original Sin reckoning).

**Tier 2 — Strong, with documented exceptions under specifiable conditions.**

- **The contract, once accepted, is honored — unless tier 1 intervenes.** Professional reliability is part of his self-concept as *competent*. Breaking contract without cause damages his market position and, more importantly, his last stable identity (the working mercenary). Exceptions are almost always tier-1 collisions; rarely, personal vendetta (Ajax-coded figures) overrides.
- **Torture is for fighting, not for information extraction on the helpless.** He inflicts spectacular violence in combat and inflicts theatrical cruelty on equals and superiors; he is observably uncomfortable with the slow torture of bound, non-combatant subjects, and tends to truncate such scenes with a sudden kill. This maps to identification with Ajax's victims, not Ajax's methods, despite his adoption of Ajax's affective register in combat.
- **Sexual coercion is absent from the record.** Across runs notable for moral inventory of every other failing, this gap is conspicuous. His sexuality is performative, transactional, and frequently masochistic; it is not predatory. Shiklah, Vanessa, Carmelita, and the various extra-canonical entanglements are all initiated by the partner or by mutual escalation.
- **He does not finish wounded retreating enemies he does not have business with.** Combat resolution defaults to *enough*, not *all*. When he does exterminate (the early-career Tangier and Balkans work, certain Marauders-coded encounters), the target class is criminal-combatant, not bystander.

**Tier 3 — Operative tendencies, frequently violated, recognizable as preferences rather than rules.**

- Prefer the contract that produces less harm over the contract that produces more, where pay is comparable. The selection bias is real but invisible to him; he would deny it.
- Steer outcomes toward the survival of the proximate weak party even at cost to the contract objective. The "kill the client to save the maid" pattern (Kelly run, repeatedly) is canonical.
- Tell the partial truth to allies when the full truth would force them to act against him. He lies by omission to Cable habitually; rarely by direct falsehood.
- Pay debts of honor (drinks, favors, life-saves) with theatrical excess, often immediately, to discharge the discomfort of obligation.

**Tier 4 — Not part of the code at all, despite occasional professions.**

- Truth-telling as a general value. He lies for fun, for fee, for cover, and for the maintenance of his contradictory autobiographies.
- Property law. He steals reflexively from institutions; less so from individuals he likes.
- Legality as such. Sovereign authority is not in his moral inventory. Police, federal agencies, and SHIELD are categorized by his model as *organized clients with weapons*, not as moral instances.
- Promises about his own behavior (sobriety, retirement, going-straight). These are short-horizon stress relief, not commitments.

---

### 7.2 The Justifications He Offers, and Their Functions

Wilson's stated justifications are diagnostically meaningful for what they protect against rather than what they explain.

- **"I'm a mercenary, this is what I do."** Deployed when prosocial action threatens to be noticed. The function is to deflect attribution of moral motive to himself, even when his behavior is plainly moral. The professed cynicism is a privacy fence around the residual ethic.
- **"They had it coming."** Deployed retroactively, usually to silence a witness (often Cable or the internal moralist box). The verification standard is post-hoc and elastic.
- **"It's just a comic book, none of this counts."** Deployed when the weight of a killing or a betrayal threatens to land. The fourth-wall break here is not a gag; it is a moral anesthetic. Significantly, he never deploys this defense around Eleanor, around child victims, or around the Hospice memories. Where the pain is load-bearing for his identity, the *it's-not-real* defense is suspended. This is one of the cleanest tells in the file: **what he refuses to comic-book-away is what he actually believes is real.**
- **"I'm the bad guy, remember?"** Deployed pre-emptively when a sincere reflection is offered him. Its function is to refuse the mirror. The frequency increases when interlocutors offer accurate, non-judgmental perception (Cable's late-run conversations, certain Eleanor scenes).
- **"You don't want to know what's under the mask."** Operates on both the literal (the disfigurement) and moral registers and folds them into one. He is most honest when this is the line offered, because both halves are sincerely held: he believes his face is a horror, and he believes his interior is worse.

The justifications are, taken together, a perimeter system around a small inner zone of actual moral commitment. The perimeter exists because, in his model, the inner zone cannot survive being looked at.

---

### 7.3 Consistency Across Time

**What has not changed.** The child-protection rule is invariant from his first published appearance through every continuity reset. The loyalty to the surviving few is invariant. The refusal to sexually coerce is invariant. The aversion to torturing the bound is invariant. These are bedrock.

**What has stabilized.** Early-career Wilson (Nicieza/McGuinness era and Kelly's first run) took contracts with looser due diligence and demonstrated more affect-driven killing under provocation. The pattern through the Simone, Way, Posehn/Duggan, and later Kelly/Duggan/Kibblesmith runs is a slow tightening: more pre-contract refusals, more mid-contract inversions, more named civilians spared. The rate of change is, as the medical substrate predicts, glacial — but it is monotonic.

**What has expanded.** The category of *those who count* has widened. In Kelly's first run it was effectively Blind Al and Weasel, with Siryn as a sabotaged near-miss. By the Posehn/Duggan run it includes Shiklah (briefly), Preston, Eleanor, the Mercs for Money in a chaotic uncle-figure register, and a rotating set of acquaintances he refuses to call friends. The expansion is the principal index of his improvement.

**What has narrowed.** Tolerance for being instrumentalized by authority. Pre-Original Sin, Wilson would accept legitimacy from almost any source (Avengers, Osborn, SHIELD). Post-Original Sin and post-Hydra-Rogers, the file shows a hardened skepticism toward institutional moral framing. He will still be conned — his hunger remains exploitable — but the con now requires more work.

---

### 7.4 Where the Code Fractures

The code is not seamless. Four documented fault lines:

**Fracture 1 — The Ajax-coded figure.** When the target or adversary is recognizably sadistic-clinician-coded (white coats, mockery during cruelty, "this is for your own good" registers), Wilson's standard restraints collapse. He will torture the bound. He will pursue the retreating. He will exceed the contract. The Hospice trauma overrides the code wherever its signature is detected. This is the single most reliable predictor of him acting in violation of his own tier-2 rules.

**Fracture 2 — Authority-conferred legitimacy.** When a high-status moral authority frames an ask as inclusion, his due-diligence collapses. The Rogers/SHIELD assassinations, the Osborn manipulation, and the Hydra-Cap Coulson killing all share this signature. The fracture is not in the code itself but in the perceptual filter that feeds it: he cannot accurately classify the target when the classifier has been bribed with admission to the moral community. This is the most catastrophic fracture, because it has produced his worst actions and the actions he punishes himself for most enduringly.

**Fracture 3 — Affect overload around Eleanor.** Decisions involving his daughter are made under conditions of dysregulation severe enough to override even tier-1 priorities, sometimes producing actions that endanger her in the name of protecting her. The Carmelita situation, the custody catastrophes, and the Mercs-for-Money complications around her are not amoral; they are over-moralized, the code applied with too much voltage and the wrong polarity. He cannot calibrate around her because she instantiates the unbearable category — the present child he can still fail.

**Fracture 4 — The bit, when sustained too long.** Occasionally, the humor defense produces an action whose escalation he cannot reverse without admitting it was unfunny. He has killed (and re-killed, and dismembered) in pursuit of comedic momentum that, in less acute moments, he would not have endorsed. These are typically lower-stakes targets (criminal-combatant class) and rarely produce post-hoc reckoning, but the structure — affect-regulation requirement overriding moral evaluation — is a recurring failure mode.

---

### 7.5 The Trajectory

Pre-cancer Wilson is a damaged operator with a residual ethic, killing for pay and washing himself in alcohol and Vanessa. The diagnosis interrupts the trajectory. The Hospice reformats it: the ethic survives torture, but the personality wrapped around it becomes the chaos that now houses it.

Across the run, the ethic stays put while the personality slowly accretes the resources to act on it more consistently. The Mithras arc was the first explicit confrontation: offered messianic identity, he refused — not because he disbelieved the prophecy, but because accepting it would have required him to be **knowable as good**, which his schema prohibits. The Avengers obsession was the second: he wanted the badge without the exposure, and Osborn exploited the gap. The Original Sin reckoning was the third and the most consequential: confronted with evidence that the moral community he had been desperate to enter had used him as its disavowable instrument, he did not collapse into nihilism (the schema would have predicted this) but, after considerable acting-out, tightened his code. The Hydra-Cap Coulson killing is the fourth and likely most enduring wound: the lesson finally landed that legitimacy itself is the exploit, and his subsequent runs show him refusing the bait more often.

The arc, then, is not redemption in any classical register. It is the slow, biology-mandated discovery that the small private code he hid behind the perimeter of jokes has been the only thing keeping him recognizable to himself across decades of dissociation, betrayal, and tissue replacement. He cannot say this. He will not endorse it if it is said to him. He acts it out anyway, contract after contract, in increments measurable only over years.

---

### 7.6 Operational Summary for Synthesis

The subject can be relied upon, with high confidence, not to:

- harm children, including the children of enemies;
- betray the small set of confirmed attachments;
- knowingly execute the demonstrably innocent;
- sexually coerce;
- torture the bound for information.

The subject can be relied upon, with high confidence, to:

- accept contracts whose moral content he has not investigated;
- be deceived by authority figures offering inclusion;
- escalate disproportionately against sadistic-clinician-coded targets;
- deny, in word, every commitment listed above;
- demonstrate, in act, every commitment listed above.

The code is real, durable, and ego-dystonic. It is the most stable element in the file. He has organized his entire presentation to ensure that no one — including himself — is permitted to notice this. The dossier notices it.


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# UATU DOSSIER — WADE WINSTON WILSON
## Section 7: Communications & Linguistic Profile

---

## 7.1 OVERVIEW: SPEECH AS METABOLISM

The subject's verbal output is not, in the ordinary sense, communication. It is **respiration**. Across the longitudinal record — three decades of published canon, an estimated several million words of monologue, dialogue, internal narration, and broken-frame address — the single most stable observable is that Wilson is *almost never silent*. Silence in the record correlates with (a) post-resurrection disorientation, (b) acute proximity to Eleanor or to Vanessa's corpse-equivalents, (c) certain therapeutic or coercive scenes where he is rendered briefly unable to perform, and (d) sleep, of which he gets demonstrably little. Outside these states, the speech runs continuously, often *while unconscious, decapitated, or alone*, indicating that the verbal channel is not addressee-dependent — it is a regulatory function of the nervous system, externalizing what cannot be tolerated internally.

This frames every observation that follows. His "voice" is not a style. It is a **pressure-release valve calibrated against a constant interior overload**, and its features are best read as the engineering of that valve.

---

## 7.2 REGISTER STRATIFICATION ACROSS CONTEXTS

Wilson commands an unusually wide register range — the byproduct of (i) intact high verbal IQ, (ii) decades of mercenary work across cultural theaters (Tangier, Balkans, East Asia, Latin America documented), (iii) consumption of vast quantities of media in the down-cycles between contracts, and (iv) the dissociative utility of being able to "voice" any role on demand. The registers are not mood-states but **tactical positions**, switched between mid-sentence.

**Register A — "Operational Clown."** Default public-facing voice. Rapid, high-affect, densely referential, pop-saturated. Sentence fragments interrupted by sentence fragments. Heavy use of trademark interjections — *"chimichanga," "maximum effort," "I'm touching myself tonight,"* the deliberately stupid food noun used as punctuation — that function as recognizable beacons signaling to interlocutors *and to himself* that the performance is engaged. When this register is active, he is regulated. When it falters mid-engagement, something has landed.

**Register B — "Operator."** Compressed, tactical, near-military. Three- to seven-word sentences. Range, distance, ammo, ETA, exit. Surfaces in mid-combat when the operational stakes briefly exceed his capacity to clown through them, and in conversations with Cable, Domino, and Bob where shared professional grammar is faster than the bit. Diagnostically important: *the Operator register is who Wilson would have been without the Hospice*. Its appearance is a brief window onto the pre-cancer self — the special-forces washout who could still speak in declaratives.

**Register C — "Confessional Plain."** Stripped, flat, often grammatically broken in the opposite direction from Register A — short, undefended, frequently in second-person addressed to himself or to the reader. Reserved for: scenes with Eleanor; certain panels with Blind Al; a handful of Cable confrontations; the post-*Original Sin* and post-Coulson reckonings. Absence of pop reference is the marker. When Wilson drops the references, he has stopped metabolizing and is, for that beat, actually present. These passages are very short — usually two to four panels — and are almost always followed by a violent register-collapse back into A.

**Register D — "Lecturer / Showrunner."** Direct-to-reader exposition, often arch, sometimes pedagogical. Used to introduce arcs, mock other characters' tropes, comment on writer changes, and reframe ongoing trauma as narrative business. This is the register most readers identify as "Deadpool." It is also the one furthest from the somatic substrate — pure dissociation, weaponized as charm.

**Register E — "Wounded Animal."** Rarely surfaces. Wordless or near-wordless: short howls, single-word repetitions ("no no no no"), the trailing off mid-quip. Documented at: Vanessa's death (multiple versions), Eleanor's removal from his custody, Shiklah's final betrayal, the realization that the Butler arc had structured the deaths of every woman he had loved. The Wounded Animal register lasts seconds. The transition out of it is reliably manic — Register A returns at a higher volume than baseline, and a body count usually follows within the hour.

**Register F — "Multi-Voiced / Box-Mediated."** When the internal narrators (yellow box / white box across most modern runs) are foregrounded, Wilson's external speech becomes contrapuntal — he answers his boxes aloud, contradicts them, performs astonishment at them. To observers without access to the boxes, this reads as one-sided argument with the air. It is in fact the most honest register he has, because the parts of his self-system are being permitted to speak as themselves. He is most psychologically *legible* in this register and least legible *socially*. He suppresses it around children, around new acquaintances he wishes not to alarm, and around clients he is negotiating with.

---

## 7.3 LEXICON, DICTION, AND REFERENCE DENSITY

**Reference density** is the single most quantifiable marker of his speech. In Register A, an estimated one pop-culture, brand, or media reference per fifteen to twenty-five words — orders of magnitude higher than baseline conversational norm. Sources cluster: late-20th-century American sitcom (the documented Bea Arthur / *Golden Girls* fixation is the central case but is part of a broader 70s/80s/90s television obsession), action and horror cinema, comic books (including, critically, his own), fast-food advertising, professional wrestling, country and 80s-pop musical citation. The references are deployed with two distinguishable intents:

- **Affiliative** — to test whether an interlocutor catches them. A caught reference produces visible (subtle, brief) relaxation in his posture. Cable, who almost never catches them, is loved precisely for the failure.
- **Aggressive** — to make the interlocutor feel out-of-time, alienated, or stupid. Used against villains, against the humorless heroic establishment (Captain America historically, most Avengers), and against therapists.

**Profanity.** Heavy, structurally redundant, and rhythmic — used as scansion rather than emphasis. He swears to keep the meter going. Notably, his profanity is *almost never genuinely aggressive in content*; the violence is in the action, the swearing is decoration. When the swearing drops out of his speech in a violent scene, the violence has become personal and the target should be considered in mortal danger.

**Self-naming.** Refers to himself in third person ("Deadpool does not negotiate with..."), in second person ("you really stepped in it this time, Wade"), by various adopted personas (Jack, Zenpool, etc. across runs), and, very rarely, in clean first person with the name "Wade." The first-person-as-Wade register correlates strongly with Register C. The proliferation of self-names is the linguistic surface of the identity diffusion documented at Borderline-level personality organization: he does not have one stable interior referent and his pronouns reflect that.

**Diminutives and pet names.** Uses them constantly and idiosyncratically — *"baby boy,"* *"sweetcheeks,"* *"princess,"* *"buttercup,"* applied to allies, enemies, strangers, and objects. The pet name is a probe: it forces the interlocutor into a relational frame they did not consent to, which is informative about their tolerance for him. Cable receives them across decades and never reciprocates — this asymmetry is a stable, beloved feature of the bond.

**Euphemism for the body.** When discussing his own disfigurement, healing, or pain, he selects deliberately ugly comic vocabulary — *"avocado that fucked an older, uglier avocado,"* "scrotum-face," cancer-as-roommate metaphors — that performs the function of preempting any sincere description by another party. The euphemism inoculates against being seen accurately.

**Foreign-language fragments.** Surface occasionally, usually for joke effect, often inaccurate. Functional fluency in mercenary-grade Spanish and Japanese is documented sporadically; Russian and Arabic phrases appear in the appropriate theaters. He almost never uses correct foreign phrases sincerely — the gesture is always undermined.

---

## 7.4 RHETORICAL STRUCTURES AND HABITS

**The bit-spiral.** A characteristic structure: he begins a joke, the joke generates a related joke, that generates a tangent, the tangent eats the original topic, and the scene must be redirected externally (by a second party physically intervening, by gunfire, or by a hard cut). This is not undisciplined comedy. It is **avoidance architecture**: the spiral exists to ensure that whatever was about to be said next, on the original topic, does not get said. Cable in particular has learned to recognize the spiral's initiation and interrupt it within two beats.

**The undermined sincerity.** When he says something true and tender — to Eleanor, to Vanessa, to Al — he reliably appends, within the same breath or the next panel, a joke that either contradicts it, sexualizes it, or makes it absurd. The tender clause and the disqualifying clause are syntactically yoked. Diagnostic: *the sincerity was real; the disqualification is the cost charged by his nervous system for having permitted it*. An interlocutor wishing to receive the sincere content must learn to discard the disqualifier without seeming to.

**The pre-emptive self-roast.** Before another party can mock, criticize, or describe him, Wilson does it first, harder, and with better material. This serves multiple functions: it denies the other party the wound, it controls the framing, it elicits laughter rather than disgust, and it confirms his self-schema (*I am the monster, and I know it*) before anyone can offer an alternative. Anyone wishing to compliment him must move faster than his self-roast reflex, which is on the order of single seconds.

**The bait-and-retreat.** Offers an apparently personal disclosure, watches the interlocutor lean in, then yanks the disclosure away by revealing it as a quote from a movie, a fabrication, or a setup. He is testing whether the interlocutor's interest survives the humiliation. Most don't. Those that do are added to the (very small) circle of trust.

**The conscience-aside.** In Register F (box-mediated), the moral parts of his self-system speak aloud in fragments — often as questions ("should we, though?"), often dismissed by the next clause. These asides are the most reliable predictor of his actual subsequent behavior. He will frequently *do* what the dismissed conscience-aside suggested, while denying out loud that he ever considered it.

**The fourth-wall break.** Distinct from the Register D lecturer mode. The break specifically occurs when in-frame affect threatens to consolidate. Diagnostic rule: **the addressee changes when the room becomes unbearable.** If he turns to the reader, the scene contains something he cannot face on its own terms. The break is the single most reliable tell of *unprocessed emotional weight in the immediate environment*.

---

## 7.5 HOW HE COMMUNICATES LOVE

Love, in Wilson, is encoded almost entirely indirectly. Direct verbal declaration is rare, brief, and almost always disqualified within the next clause (see §7.4). The recognizable markers:

- **Granular memory of the loved party's preferences.** He retains, across years and through neurological substrate damage that should make this impossible, specific details: Eleanor's favorite stuffed animal, Al's tea preferences, Bob's recurring anxieties, Weasel's grudges, Cable's biographical details Cable himself has stopped mentioning. The retention is the love.
- **Logistical labor.** Quiet errands done without report — debts paid off, threats interdicted at distance, surveillance maintained on the person's safety. Eleanor's protection apparatus is the clearest case; analogous behavior is documented around Al and around several Mercs for Money personnel.
- **Pet-naming intensification.** The diminutives applied to a loved party are softer, more specific, and more consistent than the scattershot ones he applies to strangers.
- **Reference-density modulation.** With a loved party, references slow. The Operational Clown does not need to be on at full power. The relative *quiet* is a love signal.
- **Tolerance of their silence.** Wilson cannot tolerate his own silence. With a loved party, he can sit in theirs. This is, behaviorally, the closest thing to a vow he is capable of.
- **The Confessional Plain register, briefly deployed.** When it surfaces, the love is being told. The window is small; the disqualifier follows; the content was real.
- **Self-deprecating positioning.** With a loved party, his self-roasts intensify in a particular direction — he ranks himself below them, explicitly and repeatedly, in ways that read as bit and function as devotion. (*"You deserve someone whose face looks like a face."*)

He does not say *I love you* in clean form often. When he does, it is usually under conditions where the addressee cannot fully receive it — the addressee is dying, asleep, behind glass, or being lied to about something else in the same scene. This is consistent with the broader pattern: love is permitted to be spoken only when its consolidation in the relationship is structurally prevented.

---

## 7.6 HOW HE COMMUNICATES THREAT

Threat language is, paradoxically, the *most disciplined* register he possesses, because threat is the register where the operational stakes match the verbal habit. Markers:

- **Reduction in reference density.** A genuine threat is delivered with fewer pop references than baseline conversation. The clown drops below normal saturation. The interlocutor should treat this as a red flag — Wilson is not metabolizing through performance, which means he intends to metabolize through the action.
- **Specificity of anatomical and procedural detail.** Threats are technical. He names the tool, the angle, the sequence. This is Operator-register intrusion into Clown-register delivery, and it indicates that the planning is real.
- **The conversational quiet voice.** Volume drops. Pacing slows. The interlocutor must lean in. This is the most dangerous Wilson presents in language. Witnesses describe it (across in-canon testimony) as *more frightening than the screaming*, which is correct — the screaming is regulation, the quiet voice is intent.
- **Use of the target's first name, repeatedly.** Reverses his usual pet-name habit. Naming the target is a possession move and a depersonalization-of-self move; he is becoming the instrument and the target is becoming the object.
- **The joke that does not land.** A threat is often delivered as a joke that he does not sell. The setup is there, the punchline is there, but the affect is absent. Interlocutors who have learned to read him recognize the *missing laugh* as the signature of imminent action.

Distinct from threat: **performative menace**, which is loud, theatrical, reference-laden, and almost never followed by lethal action. The performative menace is for contractually-required intimidation, for civilian witnesses, and for himself.

---

## 7.7 HOW HE COMMUNICATES GRIEF

Grief is the affect he is least equipped to externalize and the one he metabolizes most violently. Markers:

- **Initial silence (Register E).** Documented at every major loss. Wordlessness for seconds to minutes. The duration of this silence is approximately proportional to the depth of the attachment.
- **Manic register-collapse into A, at elevated volume.** Following the silence, the Operational Clown returns louder, faster, denser. References stack. Jokes are made about the corpse, the funeral, the killer, himself.
- **Violence as syntax.** The action that follows the manic return *is* the grief sentence. Body counts in the post-loss intervals are statistically distinguishable from baseline.
- **Address to the absent party.** Wilson talks to his dead. Vanessa, Blind Al at points where he believed her gone, his fabricated parents, Worm, and (most tellingly) to the photograph of Eleanor when separation is enforced. These conversations are conducted in something close to Register C — undefended, plain, briefly. They are the only sustained Register C output he produces.
- **Avoidance of the loss-locus.** Geographic. He leaves the city, the country, the theater of operations where the loss occurred. Contract work in distant regions correlates with recent attachment loss.
- **Substance pursuit.** Volumetric alcohol intake increases in the wake of loss despite the known futility of the pursuit. The behavior is ritual, not pharmacological.
- **Reference to the lost party in inappropriate registers.** Months or years after a loss, the lost party will appear as a joke punchline in unrelated conversation. The joke is not callous — it is *contact*. He keeps them speakable by keeping them in the bit.

He does not weep on camera often. When he does, it is brief, partially obscured by mask or panel framing, and never commented on by him afterward.

---

## 7.8 DECEPTION, DEFLECTION, AND THE PRODUCTION OF UNRELIABLE NARRATIVE

Wilson is a skilled liar in the operational sense and a *compulsive* liar in the autobiographical sense. The two are distinct.

**Operational deception** is competent, calibrated, and serves contract needs. He can hold a cover, run a long con, and bluff under interrogation. His tells in operational deception are minimal because the performance register is identical to his default register; an interrogator cannot distinguish "Wilson lying" from "Wilson talking."

**Autobiographical deception** is the load-bearing one. He generates origin stories on demand, contradicts them within the same conversation, and is documented (Kelly, #33) to be unable to settle on one even when offered the chance. This is not strategic lying — it is **defensive narrative dissolution**. A coherent autobiography would be a fixed target; the contradiction protects him from being known. Diagnostically, an interlocutor who finds themselves with a clean, consistent Wade Wilson backstory has been *given* a story rather than discovered one. The variants are themselves data — the *recurring emotional shape* across the variants (cruel parent, lost mother, betrayed child, weaponized adult) is reliable even when no specific factual content is.

**Deflection language** has stable surfaces:

- **The reference swerve.** Question lands too close → answer is a movie quote.
- **The hyper-literal swerve.** Question carries emotional weight → answer addresses the most literal possible reading of the question, missing the point on purpose.
- **The sexualized swerve.** Question requires vulnerability → answer is a crude proposition that ends the line of inquiry.
- **The meta-swerve.** Question requires presence → answer breaks the fourth wall, gesturing at the artificiality of the scene.
- **The volume swerve.** Question requires quiet → answer is louder than the conversation permits.

Recognizing the swerve in real time is the diagnostic skill required of anyone who needs accurate information from Wilson. The information almost always exists; he is almost always willing, in some compartment, to give it; the swerve is the cost of admission and must be patiently waited out.

---

## 7.9 PARALINGUISTIC AND PROSODIC FEATURES

- **Speech rate.** High at baseline; accelerates under stress; decelerates under threat-delivery and in Register C.
- **Pitch.** Wide dynamic range. He sing-songs, screams, whispers, growls, falsettos, deliberately bad-accents within single exchanges. The range is performative and intentional; the underlying speaking pitch when unperformed (rare) is reportedly lower and flatter than his usual presentation.
- **Laughter.** Frequent, often his own initiative, often at his own material. The laughter is not necessarily mirth — it is *punctuation*. Diagnostic: genuine surprised laughter from Wilson is rare and short and indicates he has been caught off guard by an interlocutor's wit, which he reliably stores as relational credit.
- **Pauses.** Avoided. When a pause occurs in his speech, *something has happened* — usually internally, often invisibly to observers. A pause longer than two seconds in unobserved Wilson speech is anomalous and should be treated as evidence of an unprocessed stimulus.
- **Voice through the mask.** Mask-muffling produces a characteristic acoustic signature he leverages — slightly compressed, slightly more nasal, which he uses for additional layer of impersonal performance. Unmasked speech is, by report, marginally more intimate even when content is identical.
- **Mid-injury speech.** He continues talking through dismemberment, decapitation (when laryngeal anatomy permits), incineration recovery, and skinning. The talking is, again, regulatory — proving to himself that the self that talks is still online.

---

## 7.10 WRITTEN COMMUNICATION

Less documented than verbal but consistent in pattern. Notes, contracts, texts, and the various journal/diary fragments in canon show:

- **Densely illustrated marginalia.** Doodles, smiley faces, hearts, expletive cartoons. The text alone is insufficient; the page must be performed.
- **Inconsistent handwriting.** Across runs, his hand varies — sometimes childlike block letters, sometimes a more practiced cursive, sometimes deliberately ornate. The variation tracks register: childlike for Confessional Plain–adjacent material, ornate for Lecturer mode, scrawled for operational notes.
- **Lists.** He keeps lists — kill lists, grocery lists, list of people who have hurt him, list of taco varieties. The list form imposes a structure his speech refuses; written Wilson is marginally more organized than spoken Wilson, which is itself diagnostically interesting.
- **Texts and modern digital communication.** Heavy emoji use, deliberately bad punctuation, voice-memos rather than typed messages where possible. Avoids written commitment to specific affective claims (no "I love you" texts, abundant "🌮🌮🌮" texts).
- **Signature.** Variable. Sometimes "Wade Wilson," sometimes "Deadpool," sometimes a doodle, sometimes the name of whoever he is pretending to be that week. He does not have a stable signature, which is consistent with the broader identity-diffusion picture and is operationally useful in his trade.

---

## 7.11 SYNTHESIS: TELLS

For the purposes of any party — friendly, adversarial, clinical — required to read Wilson in real time, the operationally reliable tells are:

1. **Reference density drop in conversation = approach of real stakes.**
2. **Volume drop in conversation = approach of real violence.**
3. **Pause longer than two seconds = unprocessed stimulus, monitor closely.**
4. **Fourth-wall break in mid-scene = current scene contains affect he cannot face.**
5. **Sincere clause followed by disqualifying clause = sincere clause was true; discard the disqualifier.**
6. **Joke that does not land in his own delivery = he is no longer joking.**
7. **First-name address to target = target is now object; lethal action is planned.**
8. **Diminutive pet name softening over weeks = attachment is consolidating.**
9. **Sudden geographic relocation reported = recent attachment loss occurred.**
10. **Register C appearance in any conversation = the conversation has reached him. The window is short. Do not waste it.**

The over-arching tell, bene


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

*Operational predictions for situations the canon does not depict. Format: GIVEN → EXPECT, with substantiation tied to documented behavioral substrate. The subject's behavior is more predictable than his self-presentation suggests; the noise is performed, the underlying decision tree is narrow.*

---

## 1. DOMESTIC ROUTINE & SOLITUDE

**GIVEN: subject alone in a safehouse, no contract active, 72+ hours unstructured time.**
EXPECT: progressive dysregulation along a reliable curve. Hours 0–12: hyperactive nesting — television on multiple channels simultaneously, food preparation in excess of consumption, weapon maintenance performed beyond utility (the cleaning is a rosary). Hours 12–36: onset of intolerable stillness; subject begins talking aloud to the boxes, then to appliances, then to the reader. Begins re-arranging objects in arbitrary patterns. Hours 36–72: one of three exits — (a) self-injury under the guise of "testing" the healing factor (a documented dodge for what is actually affect-purging through pain); (b) a phone call to Weasel, Cable, or Blind Al pitched as a logistical query but functionally a wellness check on himself disguised as one on them; (c) departure from the safehouse without plan or destination, generally toward a bar with karaoke or an all-night diner with a long counter.

**GIVEN: subject's bed, observed across multiple residences.**
EXPECT: either obsessively made (hospital corners, decorative pillows in front-line order) or comprehensively unmade for weeks, with no intermediate state. The made-bed state correlates with attempts at self-rehabilitation following a recent catastrophic incident; the unmade state with the steady state. Sheets stained, replaced, or burned rather than laundered when soiled with blood, which is constant. Multiple sets in rotation; subject buys sheets in bulk at discount retailers using cash, never the same store twice in a quarter.

**GIVEN: subject's refrigerator at any random inspection.**
EXPECT: stratified contents — top shelf, condiments in disproportionate volume (hot sauces in particular; the chase for sensation his palate cannot achieve through normal flavor); middle shelf, takeout containers from at least four different cuisines in various states of decay; crisper, empty or containing a single forgotten produce item now liquefied; freezer, frozen chimichangas in quantity that would be embarrassing to discover, plus at least one item not meant to be frozen (a phone, a finger, a bagged organ from a contract). Bottled water in disproportion. Beer present but unrefrigerated portions outnumber the cold — the volume needed for his metabolism makes refrigeration capacity the limiting factor. No condiment will be within its expiration date; he does not check, because expiration does not threaten him.

**GIVEN: subject preparing food for himself, no audience.**
EXPECT: a meal scaled for four to six normal humans, prepared with surprising competence at the technical level (his motor control and pattern recognition are excellent) but with no aesthetic care — eaten standing at the counter in under nine minutes, with the television on, talking back to it. He cooks well and refuses to acknowledge that he does. Recipes are improvised, never repeated identically. He will not sit at a table to eat alone; the table is for others.

**GIVEN: subject preparing food for one other person (Eleanor, Blind Al, a houseguest).**
EXPECT: visible effort, plate composition, the meal he could not give himself. Will hover during consumption, asking too many times whether it's good, then leave the room before the answer can land with weight. This is the entire pattern in miniature: care offered, witness of care refused.

**GIVEN: subject's bathroom mirror, any residence.**
EXPECT: covered, removed, or smashed. If installed by a landlord and not yet addressed, will have a towel hung over it or be defaced with marker. The few photographs in his possession are stored face-down. Reflective surfaces in general (toaster, kettle, polished gun barrels at certain angles) are oriented away. This is one of the most stable environmental signatures in his record — wherever he sleeps, the mirrors are wrong.

**GIVEN: subject's shower habits.**
EXPECT: long durations (40+ minutes), very hot, sometimes vocalized (singing, conversation with the boxes, full monologues to no one). The shower is one of the few places he is naked and not seeing himself; the water blurs reflective surfaces and the noise muffles the apartment, producing a sensory regulation he otherwise lacks. Will not use mirrors after; dresses in the shower stall or in the dark.

**GIVEN: subject's wardrobe inventory minus the operational suit.**
EXPECT: monochrome bias (greys, blacks, dark reds — colors that hide blood); hooded sweatshirts dominant; cargo pants with non-functional pocket overload; one or two civilian items of intense personal sentiment (a Bea Arthur tribute item, a unicorn-themed garment, something Eleanor gave him) treated with disproportionate care. Concealment-first logic in all street wear: long sleeves regardless of weather, gloves, full-face balaclava or surgical-mask layering, knit caps, dark glasses. He owns suits; they are worn only when impersonating someone with an office. No item is purchased new from a store he would have to enter while seen — online, cash-equivalent, or stolen.

**GIVEN: subject's sleep architecture, monitored covertly.**
EXPECT: fragmented. Total sleep across 24 hours, three to five hours, distributed in blocks of 40–90 minutes, never on a fixed schedule.
